Raising Hands and Takbir for Qunut in Witr
Ruling on raising hands and takbir for qunut in witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for qunut in witr, including the timing of raising hands and takbir, and identify the proofs cited.

Core Idea
Raise hands and say takbir for qunut after recitation, before bowing, throughout the year.

In the Hanafi school, qunut in witr is a wajib act performed in every rak'ah of witr? Actually, it is in the third rak'ah. This passage details the specific procedure: after completing surah recitation, one raises the hands to the ears and says takbir, then recites the qunut supplication before bowing. The text provides evidence from the practice of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and a general principle that takbir marks a change of state in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is raising hands and saying takbir for qunut in the third rak'ah of witr. The overall qunut is wajib in Hanafi fiqh; the raising of hands and takbir are sunnah.
Qunut itself is wajib; the specific actions described are sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Outline the procedure
After finishing the surah recitation in the third rak'ah, one raises the hands to the ears, says 'Allahu Akbar', then recites the qunut dua before bowing. This is done throughout the year, not only in Ramadan.
The takbir marks the transition from recitation to supplication.
3
Analyze the first proof: takbir for state change
The author argues that takbir is said when moving from one state to another in prayer. Since qunut is a new state after recitation, takbir is appropriate.
This is a general principle (qiyas jali).
4
Analyze the second proof: athar of Ibn Mas'ud
The athar from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah shows that he would say takbir after recitation, then qunut, then takbir again before bowing. This establishes the practice.
This is a direct transmission from a prominent sahabi.
5
Note the madhhab emphasis on year-round qunut
The text explicitly states that qunut is recited throughout the year, contradicting those who limit it to Ramadan. This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
Shafi'is restrict qunut in witr to the second half of Ramadan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه (۲۰۳) اور جب تیسری رکعت میں سورت ملانے سے فارغ ہو جائے تو دونوں ہاتھ کانوں تک اٹھائے اور اللہ اکبر کہے

تشریح : تیسری رکعت میں دعاء قنوت پڑھے، اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ سورت ملانے کے بعد اللہ اکبر کہ کر ہاتھ کا نوں تک اٹھائے اور رکوع سے پہلے دعاء قنوت پڑھے، اور پورے سال دعاء قنوت پڑھے ، صرف رمضان شریف میں پڑھنا کافی نہیں ہے۔ وجه : : (۱) دعاء قنوت کا ارادہ کرے تو تکبیر کہے اور ہاتھ اٹھائے ، اسکی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قرآت کرنے کے بعد اب دعاء قنوت پڑھنے کی طرف بدل رہی ہے ، اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ ایک حالت سے دوسری حالت کی طرف بدلے تو تکبیر کہے، اسلئے یہاں حالت بدلنے پر تکبیر کہے۔(۲) اثر میں ہے۔ ان عبد الله بن مسعود كان اذا فرغ من القرأة كبّر ثم قنت فاذا فرغ من القنوت كبر ثم ركع . (مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ، باب ۵۹۰ فی التکبیر للقوت، ج ثانی ص ۱۰۱ نمبر ۶۹۴۷ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ قنوت پڑھتے وقت تکبیر کہے۔ (۳) ہاتھ اٹھانے کا ثبوت اس اثر میں ہے عن عبد الله بن مسعود) انه كان يرفع يديه في قنوت
Translation: (203) And when he finishes reciting the surah in it (the third rak'ah), he should raise both his hands up to his ears and say Allahu Akbar.

Explanation: In the third rak'ah, he should recite the qunut supplication. Its form is that after finishing the surah, he says Allahu Akbar, raises his hands up to his ears, and recites the qunut supplication before bowing. And he should recite the qunut supplication throughout the whole year, it is not sufficient to recite it only in Ramadan. Evidence: (1) When he intends the qunut supplication, he says takbir and raises his hands, the reason being that after recitation, he is now turning to reciting the qunut supplication, and it has passed before that when turning from one state to another, he says takbir, so here due to changing state, he says takbir. (2) There is an athar: That Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, when he finished recitation, he said takbir, then recited qunut, and when he finished from qunut, he said takbir, then bowed. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab 590 fi al-takbir li al-qunut, vol. 2, p. 101, no. 6947) This athar states that he says takbir at the time of qunut. (3) Proof of raising hands is in this athar: From Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that he used to raise his hands in qunut.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage covers the procedure for qunut in the third rak'ah of witr. After completing the surah recitation, one raises the hands to the ears and says Allahu Akbar, then recites the qunut dua before bowing (ruku). The takbir is recited to mark the transition from recitation to supplication, consistent with the principle that a takbir is said when moving between states. The author emphasizes that qunut is recited throughout the year, not only in Ramadan. Evidence is provided from the practice of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, who would say takbir after reciting, then perform qunut, then say takbir again before bowing. Raising hands is also confirmed from his practice.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunut): A specific supplication recited in the witr prayer after rising from bowing or before bowing, depending on school.
تکبیر (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar', used here to transition from recitation to qunut.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When should the takbir for qunut be said according to this passage?
A) Before reciting the surah
B) After reciting the surah and before qunut
C) After qunut and before bowing
D) After bowing

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, qunut in witr is performed every night by raising the hands and saying takbir after surah recitation, before bowing, and this practice is established by the principle of takbir at state change and the practice of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud.

Recitation and Sitting in Witr Prayer
Ruling on recitation and sitting in Witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recitation requirements for each rak'ah of Witr and explain why only tashahhud is recited in the middle sitting.

Core Idea
Each rak'ah of Witr needs Fatiha + surah; sit after two for just tashahhud.

Witr is a unique prayer: wajib in the Hanafi school but its performance resembles nafl. This passage clarifies the specific recitation pattern and the middle sitting, based on the Prophet's practice. Understanding these details ensures your Witr is performed correctly according to the Hanafi method.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
Witr is a three-rak'ah prayer that is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school, as opposed to sunnah mu'akkadah in others. Its performance follows patterns similar to nafl and sunnah prayers.
The hukm level (wajib) distinguishes it from fard; omission is sinful but may be compensated later.
2
Locate the recitation rule
The passage states: 'you recite in every rak'ah of it al-Fatiha and a surah.' This is based on hadith reports that the Prophet (ﷺ) recited multiple surahs in each rak'ah of Witr.
The surah recited after Fatiha can be any surah; the hadith shows examples of reciting from the mufassal.
3
Determine the middle sitting
After the first two rak'ahs, you sit and confine yourself to the tashahhud only. You do not recite salawat (durud) or make dua because the prayer is not yet complete—you still have the third rak'ah to perform.
This is unlike the final sitting in fard prayers where salawat and dua are recited.
4
Apply the rule for the third rak'ah
When standing for the third rak'ah, you do not recite the opening supplication (thana). The reason is that the third rak'ah is considered part of the same pair as the first two; it is not a separate shaf' (pair) that would require its own thana.
This is derived from the analogy with nafl prayers where each pair is independent, but here the third is attached to make the total odd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الوتر
۴۱۲
(۲۰۲) ويقرأ في كل ركعة منه الفاتحة وسورة. ويجلس على رأس الاوليين منه ويقتصر على التشهد ولا يستفتح عند قيامه للثالثة (٦٠٣) واذا فرغ من قراءة السورة فيها رفع يديه حذاء اذنيه نہیں چھوڑنی چاہئے ترجمه : (۲۰۲) اور ہر رکعت میں فاتحہ اور سورت پڑھے، اور دورکعت پر بیٹھ کر صرف تشہد پر اقتصار (اکتفا) کرے، اور تیسری رکعت میں کھڑے ہو کرشنا نہ پڑھے۔
تشریح : وتر واجب ہے لیکن اس کی دوسری حیثیت نفل اور سنت کی ہے، اور نفل اور سنت کی تمام رکعتوں میں سورہ فاتحہ پڑھتے ہیں اور سورہ ملاتے ہیں کیونکہ اس کی ہر دور کعتیں الگ الگ شفع ہیں، اس لئے وتر کی تینوں رکعتوں میں فاتحہ پڑھے اور سورت ملائے اور دورکعتوں پر بیٹھے اور صرف تشہد پڑھے، درود شریف اور دعا نہ پڑھے کیونکہ ابھی تیسری رکعت پڑھنی ہے۔ اور تیسری رکعت میں ثنا اس لئے نہ پڑھے کہ یہ پہلی دو رکعتوں کا ہی حصہ ہے، الگ سے شفع نہیں ہے۔
صلى الله
وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے۔ عـن عـلـى قال كان رسول الله علة يوتر بثلاث يقرأ فيهن بتسع سور من المفصل يقرأ في كل ركعة بثلاث سور آخر هن قل هو الله احد - ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الوتر بثلاث ص ۱۰۶، نمبر ۴۵۹) (۲) عن ابی بن كعب قال كان رسول الله الله كان يقرأ في الوتر بسبح اسم ربک الاعلی وفی الركعة الثانية بـقـل يـا ايها الكافرون وفى الثالثة بقل هو الله احد ولا يسلم الا في آخرهن (نسائی شریف، باب ذکر اختلاف الفاظ الناقلین بخبر ابی بن کعب فی الوتر ص ۱۹۱، نمبر ۱۷۰۲ مستدرک للحاکم ، کتاب الوتر ، ج اول ص ۴۴۶، نمبر ۱۱۳۹ار ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء ما يقر آفی الوتر، ص ۱۰۶، نمبر ۴۶۳ / ابو داؤد شریف، باب ما يقر آفی الوترص ۲۰۸ نمبر ۱۴۲۳) ان دونوں حدیثوں میں تینوں رکعتوں میں سورت ملائی ہے۔
Chapter of Witr. (202) And he recites in every rak'ah of it al-Fatiha and a surah. And he sits at the end of the first two rak'ahs and confines himself to the tashahhud, and does not recite the opening supplication when standing for the third. (603) And when he finishes reciting the surah in it, he raises his hands to the level of his ears. It should not be left. Translation: (202) And in every rak'ah he recites Fatiha and a surah, and sitting after two rak'ahs he confines himself to tashahhud, and when standing for the third rak'ah he does not recite thana. Explanation: Witr is wajib, but its second aspect is that of nafl and sunnah, and in all rak'ahs of nafl and sunnah they recite Surah Fatiha and join a surah, because each pair of rak'ahs are separate shaf'. Therefore, in the three rak'ahs of Witr he recites Fatiha and joins a surah, and sits after two rak'ahs and recites only tashahhud, not reciting the noble durud or supplication because he still has to pray the third rak'ah. And he does not recite thana in the third rak'ah because it is only part of the first two rak'ahs, not a separate shaf'. Proof: (1) The hadith is: From 'Ali, he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, performed witr with three rak'ahs, reciting in them nine surahs from the mufassal, reciting in each rak'ah three surahs, the last of them being Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad. (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-witr bi thalath, p. 106, no. 459) (2) From Ubayy ibn Ka'b, he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, used to recite in Witr Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la, and in the second rak'ah Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun, and in the third Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad, and he did not make taslim except at the end of them. (Nasa'i, Bab dhikr ikhtilaf alfaz al-naqilin bi khabar Ubayy ibn Ka'b fi al-witr, p. 191, no. 1702; Mustadrak al-Hakim, Kitab al-witr, vol. 1, p. 446, no. 1139; Tirmidhi, Bab ma jaa ma yuqra' fi al-witr, p. 106, no. 463; Abu Dawood, Bab ma yuqra' fi al-witr, p. 208, no. 1423) In both of these hadiths, a surah is joined in all three rak'ahs.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding the method of performing the Witr prayer. The author states the Hanafi position that in each rak'ah of Witr, one must recite Surah al-Fatiha and another surah. After the first two rak'ahs, one sits for tashahhud only, without sending salawat upon the Prophet or making supplication, because the prayer is not yet complete. When standing for the third rak'ah, one does not recite the thana (opening supplication) because the third rak'ah is considered part of the same pair as the first two? Actually, the explanation clarifies that each pair of rak'ahs in nafl are separate, but here Witr is three rak'ahs; the first two form one shaf' (pair) and the third is separate? The commentary says the third is not a separate shaf' but part of the first two? Let's follow the text: The Urdu commentary says that Witr is wajib but its secondary status is like nafl and sunnah. In nafl and sunnah, each pair of rak'ahs are separate (shaf'), so in Witr, one recites Fatiha and a surah in all three rak'ahs, sits after two rak'ahs for only tashahhud, and does not recite thana in the third because it is part of the first two rak'ahs, not a separate shaf'. This seems contradictory: if each pair is separate, then the third rak'ah would be a separate shaf'? Actually, the Hanafi position is that Witr is prayed as three rak'ahs with one taslim at the end, and the first two rak'ahs are like a shaf' (pair) and the third is a witr (odd). However, when it comes to recitation, each rak'ah gets its own Fatiha and surah, and the sitting after two rak'ahs is not a final sitting but a middle sitting, so only tashahhud is recited. The proof is from the hadith of 'Ali and Ubayy ibn Ka'b where the Prophet recited surahs in each rak'ah.

Key Terms
وتر (witr): A prayer of odd number of rak'ahs (three in this context) that is wajib in the Hanafi school.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs considered as a unit in nafl and sunnah prayers.
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony recited while sitting in prayer: 'At-tahiyyatu lillah...'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi method of Witr prayer, what does one recite when sitting after the first two rak'ahs?
A) Only the tashahhud
B) Tashahhud followed by salawat and a supplication
C) The opening supplication (thana)
D) Nothing; one stands up immediately

Key Takeaway
In Witr, each rak'ah requires Fatiha and a surah, and the middle sitting is for tashahhud only.

Raising Hands and Qunut in Witr: Hanafi Ruling and Proof
Ruling on raising hands and reciting qunut in Witr prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when and how to raise hands and recite qunut in Witr, and identify the proof from the practice of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud.

Core Idea
Qunut in Witr is wajib all year; hands raised with takbir before bowing, proven by Ibn Mas'ud.

The Witr prayer includes a special supplication called qunut. This lesson examines the Hanafi position on when and how to perform qunut, supported by the practice of the Companion Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. Understanding this ruling ensures correct performance and avoids common mistakes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, determine exactly what act is being ruled upon: the raising of hands and recitation of qunut in the third rak'ah of Witr. The text states that it is wajib to do so throughout the year.
Ruling level: wajib in Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the athar (practice) of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, as recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba. This shows his consistent practice of saying takbir and raising hands before qunut.
Dalil type: Sunnah_ahad (practice of a Companion).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the dalil proves the ruling: The explicit action of Ibn Mas'ud—raising hands, saying takbir, and reciting qunut before bowing—demonstrates the prescribed method. The Hanafi school considers the practice of a Companion binding.
Thubut: zanni; Dalala: qati (clear indication).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that qunut in Witr is sunnah and only recited in the second half of Ramadan. This is a valid scholarly difference based on different interpretations of evidence.
Cross-madhhab: mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi) due to the strong transmission of Ibn Mas'ud's practice and its consistency with the general principle of marking state changes with takbir.
Tarjih authority: established in zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text

ترجمه (۲۰۳) اور جب تیسری رکعت میں سورت ملانے سے فارغ ہو جائے تو دونوں ہاتھ کانوں تک اٹھائے اور اللہ اکبر کہے تشریح : تیسری رکعت میں دعاء قنوت پڑھے، اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ سورت ملانے کے بعد اللہ اکبر کہ کر ہاتھ کا نوں تک
اٹھائے اور رکوع سے پہلے دعاء قنوت پڑھے، اور پورے سال دعاء قنوت پڑھے ، صرف رمضان شریف میں پڑھنا کافی نہیں ہے۔ وجه : : (۱) دعاء قنوت کا ارادہ کرے تو تکبیر کہے اور ہاتھ اٹھائے ، اسکی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قرآت کرنے کے بعد اب دعاء قنوت پڑھنے کی طرف بدل رہی ہے ، اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ ایک حالت سے دوسری حالت کی طرف بدلے تو تکبیر کہے، اسلئے یہاں حالت بدلنے پر تکبیر کہے۔(۲) اثر میں ہے۔ ان عبد الله بن مسعود كان اذا فرغ من القرأة كبّر ثم قنت فاذا فرغ من القنوت كبر ثم ركع . (مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ، باب ۵۹۰ فی التکبیر للقوت، ج ثانی ص ۱۰۱ نمبر ۶۹۴۷ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ قنوت پڑھتے وقت تکبیر کہے۔ (۳) ہاتھ اٹھانے کا ثبوت اس اثر میں ہے عن عبد الله بن مسعود) انه كان يرفع يديه في قنوت

كبر (۲۰۴) و قنت قائما قبل الركوع فى جميع ال
السنة
الوتر . (مصنف ابن ابی هیته ، ۵۹۱ فی رفع الیدین فی القصوت ج ثانی ص ۱۰۱ نمبر ۶۹۵۳)(۴) عبد الرحمن بن الاسود عن ابيه قال كان ابن مسعود يرفع يديه في القنوت الى ثدييه ( من البيهقی ، باب رفع اليدين في القنوت، ج ثالث ص ۵۹ نمبر ۷ ۴۸۶ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ قنوت پڑھنے سے پہلے ہاتھ اٹھائے گا۔
Translation (203): And when he finishes reciting the surah in it, he raises both hands to the ears and says Allahu Akbar. Explanation: In the third rak'ah, he recites the qunut supplication. Its form is that after joining the surah, he says Allahu Akbar, raises his hands to the ears, and recites the qunut supplication before bowing. And he recites the qunut supplication throughout the entire year; it is not sufficient to recite it only in Ramadan. Proof: (1) When he intends the qunut supplication, he says takbir and raises his hands. The reason is that after recitation, he is now turning to reciting the qunut supplication, and it has passed before that when turning from one state to another, he says takbir; therefore, here upon changing state, he says takbir. (2) There is an athar: 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, when he finished recitation, said takbir, then performed qunut, and when he finished qunut, he said takbir then bowed. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bab 590 fi al-takbir li al-qunut, vol. 2, p. 101, no. 6947) This athar shows that at the time of qunut, he says takbir. (3) The proof of raising hands is in this athar: From 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that he used to raise his hands in qunut. (Page 415 line: takbir (204) And he performs qunut standing before bowing in all the year of Witr. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bab 591 fi raf' al-yadayn fi al-qunut, vol. 2, p. 101, no. 6953) (4) 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Aswad from his father said: Ibn Mas'ud used to raise his hands in qunut to his chest. (from al-Bayhaqi, Bab raf' al-yadayn fi al-qunut, vol. 3, p. 59, no. 7486) From this athar, it is understood that he will raise his hands before reciting qunut.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling and proof for the manner of performing qunut in the Witr prayer. According to the Hanafi school, after completing the recitation of the surah in the third rak'ah, one raises the hands to the ears, says 'Allahu Akbar', and then recites the qunut supplication while standing before bowing. This qunut is recited throughout the year, not only in Ramadan. The proof is drawn from the practice of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, as recorded in the musannaf works, showing that he would say takbir when beginning qunut, raise his hands, and then recite qunut. The reasoning is that moving from the state of Quran recitation to supplication constitutes a change of state, which is marked by takbir, analogous to other transitions in prayer.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunut): A special supplication recited in the Witr prayer after raising hands and before bowing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the evidence used by the Hanafi school for raising hands in qunut?
A) Athar of Ibn Mas'ud
B) Quranic verse
C) Ijma
D) Qiyas

Key Takeaway
Qunut in Witr is wajib throughout the year; its performance involves raising hands and takbir before bowing, proven by the practice of Ibn Mas'ud.

The Hanafi Qunut in Witr: Before Ruku' Throughout the Year
Ruling on qunut in Witr with proof and distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qunut in Witr and explain the distinction between the regular qunut and qunut nazilah.

Core Idea
Qunut in Witr is wajib before ruku' all year; qunut nazilah is separate for Fajr during calamities.

Many students confuse the qunut recited in Witr with the qunut nazilah recited during calamities. In this lesson, we clarify the Hanafi position on the regular qunut of Witr—its timing, its status as wajib, and its practice throughout the year—supported by clear proofs from the Sunnah and the practice of the Sahaba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
State what qunut in Witr is and its hukm in the Hanafi school: wajib, performed in the third rak'ah before ruku' throughout the year.
Wajib means omission requires sajdah al-sahw.
2
Distinguish the two qunuts
Differentiate between regular qunut in Witr (before ruku', all year) and qunut nazilah (after ruku' in Fajr, during calamities). This is crucial to avoid mixing the two practices.
Qunut nazilah is not the focus of this ruling.
3
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b: the Prophet performed qunut in Witr before ruku'. This establishes the timing and location.
Hadith is ahad, zanni al-thubut, but qat'i al-dalalah in Hanafi view.
4
Examine supportive proofs
Review the athar of Ibn Mas'ud (no qunut except Witr before ruku') and the hadith advising Witr before sleep (showing Witr is year-round, so qunut is year-round).
These reinforce the ruling and answer objections.
5
Address cross-madhhab dispute
Compare Hanafi (before ruku', all year) with Shafi'i (after ruku', last half of Ramadan). Note the thamarah al-khilaf in practice.
Both positions are valid ikhtilaf; Hanafi mufta bihi is as stated.

صلى الله
Translation (204): And he performs qunut while standing before bowing in all the year. Explanation: There are two types of qunut supplication: [1] One is qunut nazilah, which is recited at the time of calamity, 'Allahumma ahdina fi man hadayt...' etc. The Prophet recited qunut nazilah at the time of the attack on the tribes of Banu Sulaym, Ra'l, and Dhakwan, and after some days he discontinued it. Among the Hanafis, qunut nazilah is also practiced at the time of calamity; it is recited in Fajr prayer after rising from bowing in the second rak'ah. [2] The second qunut supplication is the one that the Hanafis recite in Witr before bowing, and they recite it throughout the year; this is the supplication mentioned here. Proof: (1) There is a hadith: From Ubayy ibn Ka'b that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, performed qunut in Witr before bowing. (Abu Dawood, Bab al-qunut fi al-witr, p. 209, no. 1427; Nasa'i, Bab dhikr ikhtilaf alfaz al-naqilin bi khabar Ubayy ibn Ka'b fi al-witr, p. 191, no. 1700; Ibn Majah, Bab ma ja'a fi al-qunut qabl al-ruku' wa ba'dahu, p. 16, no. 1182) This hadith shows that the qunut supplication in Witr is recited in the third rak'ah before bowing. (2) There is this athar: Ibn Mas'ud would not perform qunut in any prayer except Witr before bowing. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 581 fi al-qunut qabl al-ruku' aw ba'dahu, vol. 2, p. 97, no. 1903) This athar shows that he did not perform qunut in any other prayer except Witr, and the second point is that he performed qunut before bowing. (3) And the hadith that indicates qunut after bowing or in Fajr prayer is that of qunut nazilah, which is recited at the time of calamity. Its proof is the hadith: From Ibn 'Abbas, he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, performed qunut for a consecutive month in Zuhr, 'Asr, Maghrib, 'Isha', and the morning prayer at the end of each prayer, when he said 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' from the last rak'ah, supplicating against the living from Banu Sulaym, Ra'l, Dhakwan, and 'Usayya, and those behind him said 'Ameen'. (Abu Dawood, Bab al-qunut fi al-salah, p. 211, no. 1443; Bukhari, Bab al-qunut qabl al-ruku' wa ba'dahu, p. 136, no. 1002) This hadith shows that qunut after bowing was qunut nazilah at the time of calamity. The evidence for performing qunut throughout the year is the hadith: Abu Hurayra said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, advised me to perform Witr before sleeping. (Bukhari, Bab sa'at al-witr, p. 135, no. 995; Abu Dawood, Bab fi al-witr qabl al-nawm, p. 210, no. 1432) From these hadiths, it is understood that Witr is to be performed throughout the year. Therefore, reciting the qunut supplication in it throughout the year will also be wajib. Because of Ubayy ibn Ka'b, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage clarifies that the qunut in Witr is recited before bowing (ruku') and is practiced throughout the year. It distinguishes between two types of qunut: qunut nazilah (recited during calamities, after ruku' in Fajr) and the regular qunut of Witr (recited before ruku' in the third rak'ah of Witr). The Hanafi school holds that the regular qunut in Witr is wajib and is performed all year. The proof is from the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b that the Prophet performed qunut in Witr before bowing. The athar of Ibn Mas'ud confirms that he only performed qunut in Witr and before bowing. The hadith about qunut after bowing refers to qunut nazilah, which is a different practice. Also, the hadith advising Witr before sleep indicates that Witr is a regular practice throughout the year, thus its qunut is also year-round.

Key Terms
قنوت نازلہ (qunut nazilah): A special supplication recited during times of calamity, performed after ruku' in Fajr prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only in Fajr prayer

Key Takeaway
The regular qunut in Witr is a distinct practice, wajib and performed before ruku' throughout the year, separate from qunut nazilah for calamities.

Ruling of Qunut in Witr Before Ruku' Throughout the Year
Ruling statement and proof for qunut in witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qunut in witr and identify the evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
Qunut in witr is wajib before ruku' all year, established by hadith and companion practice.

The Hanafi school holds a distinct position on qunut in witr. This lesson examines the ruling and its proofs, distinguishing it from qunut nazilah and from the positions of other schools.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the exact ruling: the worshiper recites qunut while standing, before ruku', in the third rak'ah of witr, throughout the entire year.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Examine the primary dalil
Read the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b: the Prophet recited qunut in witr before ruku'. Note its chain and the Hanafi inference of obligation.
The imperative 'qanat' indicates action; Hanafi usul treats the Prophet's actions as evidence for obligation unless proven otherwise.
3
Examine the companion practice
Consider the athar of Ibn Mas'ud that he only recited qunut in witr before ruku'. This confirms the practice of the early community.
Qawl Sahabi is a source of law in Hanafi usul.
4
Distinguish qunut nazilah
Understand that qunut recited after ruku' in Fajr is qunut nazilah, recited only during calamities, not the regular witr qunut.
The hadith of Ibn Abbas about qunut after ruku' refers to this temporary practice.
5
Evaluate the evidence for year-round practice
Link the hadith of Abu Hurayrah about the Prophet's advice to pray witr before sleep and the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b to establish that witr qunut is performed all year.
Since witr is prayed throughout the year, its qunut is also year-round.

Chapter of Witr: (204) And he recites qunut standing before ruku' in all of the year in witr. Commentary: There are two types of qunut: qunut nazilah recited at times of calamity, and the regular qunut in witr. Evidence: (1) Hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b that the Prophet recited qunut in witr before ruku'. (2) Athar of Ibn Mas'ud that he only recited qunut in witr before ruku'. (3) Hadith of Ibn Abbas about qunut nazilah after ruku' in Fajr. Evidence for reciting qunut all year: Hadith of Abu Hurayrah that the Prophet advised witr before sleep, and the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b that he recited qunut all year.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof regarding the Hanafi position on qunut in witr. The author first states the ruling: the worshiper recites qunut while standing, before ruku', throughout the entire year. The commentary then distinguishes two types of qunut: (1) Qunut Nazilah, recited during calamity in Fajr prayer after rising from ruku', based on the Prophet's practice during the attack on the tribes of Ri'l and Dhakwan. (2) The regular qunut in witr, which the Hanafis recite before ruku' in the third rak'ah all year. The proof includes the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b that the Prophet recited qunut in witr before ruku', and the athar of Ibn Mas'ud that he only recited qunut in witr before ruku'. The hadith of Ibn Abbas about qunut after ruku' is explained as qunut nazilah, not the regular witr qunut. The requirement to recite qunut all year is derived from the encouragement to pray witr all year and the practice of the Prophet and companions.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunut): Supplication in prayer; specifically here, the supplication recited in witr before ruku'.

Qunut: Restricted to Witr – Ruling and Proof
Ruling with proof: qunut is only in witr, with the prescribed supplication, definition, and refutation of the Shafi'i view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that qunut is only recited in witr, explain the proof from the hadith of Khalid ibn Abi 'Imran, and differentiate the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i practice in Fajr.

Core Idea
Qunut is only in witr; it is not a regular part of Fajr or any other prayer in the Hanafi school.

This passage establishes a key Hanafi ruling: qunut is confined to witr prayer. It also provides the exact supplication taught by Jibril to the Prophet, emphasizing that qunut means supplication—not cursing. The author contrasts the Hanafi position with the Shafi'i view, grounding the ruling in the practice of the Companions and a clear hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states 'لا يقنت فى غير الوتر' (do not recite qunut in other than witr). This is the core ruling: qunut is exclusive to witr.
The ruling is stated at the beginning of the matn.
2
Analyze the evidence
The hadith of Khalid ibn Abi 'Imran shows Jibril teaching the Prophet this specific qunut, which is purely supplication without curses. This is the primary proof.
The hadith is cited in the commentary as dalil.
3
Understand the definition
The author defines 'qunut' as supplication (دعاء), meaning it should not contain curses. The taught supplication consists only of praise and petition.
This definition is used to refute any qunut that includes cursing.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i permits qunut in Fajr based on a hadith of the Prophet reciting qunut for a month. The Hanafi response is that this was qunut nazilah during a calamity, not regular practice.
The dispute is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both schools have strong evidence.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, Hanafis recite this qunut in witr every night (after recitation and before ruku' according to one narration). They do not recite it in Fajr or any other prayer.
The athar from Ibn Mas'ud confirms reciting qunut in witr every night throughout the year.

صلى الله
مضر اذ جاه جبرئيل فأومأ اليه ان اسكت فسكت فقال يا محمد ان الله لم يبعثك سبابا و لا لعانا و انما بعثك رحمة و لم يبعثك عذابا لیس لک من الامر شيء او يتوب عليهم او يعذبهم فانهم ظالمون ، ثم علمه هذا القنوت ((اللهم انا نستعینک و نستغفرک و نؤمن بک و نخضع لک و نخلع و نترک من یکفرک اللهم ایاک نعبد و لک نصلی و نسجد و الیک نسعی و نحفد و نرجو رحمتک و نخشی
(205) And do not recite qunut in other than witr. Qunut means supplication, and it is to say: 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuka wa nastahdeeka wa nastaghfiruka wa natubu ilayka wa nu'minu bika wa natawakkalu 'alayka wa nuthni 'alayka al-khayra kullahu nashkuruka wa la nakfuruka wa nakhla'u wa natruku man yafjuruka, Allahumma iyyaka na'budu wa laka nusalli wa nasjudu wa ilayka nas'a wa nahfidu narju rahmataka wa nakhsha 'adhabaka inna 'adhabaka al-jidda bil-kuffari mulhiq.' Commentary: The Shafi'i school deducts qunut in Fajr, but the author restricts it to witr. The supplication is taken from the hadith of Khalid ibn Abi 'Imran that Jibril taught the Prophet this qunut.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof that qunut is only recited in witr, not in any other prayer, and it presents the text of the qunut supplication. The author states the ruling and specifies the supplication. The commentary explains that Imam Shafi'i holds qunut in Fajr, but the matn (author) restricts it to witr. The author also indicates that qunut means supplication, so it should not contain curses, as the Prophet was forbidden from that. The proof is the hadith of Khalid ibn Abi 'Imran that Jibril taught the Prophet this specific qunut. The athar of Ibrahim and Abdullah ibn Mas'ud are also cited to emphasize that witr without qunut is not valid and that Ibn Mas'ud recited qunut in witr all year, not in Fajr.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunut): Supplication; specifically the prescribed supplication in witr.
قنوت نازلہ (qunut nazilah): Qunut recited during calamity in any prayer after ruku'.

Qunut is Exclusive to Witr Prayer
States ruling and text of qunut for witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that qunut is recited only in witr prayer and recite the standard qunut text.

Core Idea
Qunut is wajib only in witr; its text is a comprehensive supplication.

This lesson establishes a key Hanafi position: qunut is recited exclusively in witr prayer, not in fajr or any other prayer. The passage also provides the full text of the qunut, which is a supplication that includes praise, seeking help, and expressions of faith. Memorizing this text and the ruling is essential for proper witr practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage states 'ولا يقنت فى غير الوتر' meaning qunut is not performed in any prayer other than witr. Recognize that this is the Hanafi ruling: qunut is wajib in witr.
This is a clear prohibition excluding other prayers.
2
Understand the meaning of qunut
The author defines qunut as 'الدعاء' (supplication). This helps distinguish it from other actions in prayer; it is a specific verbal invocation.
Qunut here means a particular du'a, not the general concept of humility.
3
Memorize the qunut text
Read and memorize the Arabic text from 'اللهم انا نستعينك' to 'ملحق'. This is the standard Hanafi qunut recited before ruku' in witr.
Focus on the key phrases: praise, seeking help, repentance, and disavowal of disbelievers.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school limits qunut to witr, while the Shafi'i school also recites it in fajr. This lesson implicitly refutes the Shafi'i position.
Understanding this ikhtilaf will help you appreciate the Hanafi evidence (though not cited here).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقنت فى غير الوتر والقنوت معناه الدعاء وهو ان يقول اللهم انا نستعينك و نستهديك و نستغفرك ونتوب اليك و نؤمن بك و نتوكل عليك و نثني عليك الخير كله نشكرك و لا نكفرك و نخلع و نترك من يفجرك اللهم اياك نعبد و لك نصلي و نسجد واليك نسعى و نحفد نرجو رحمتك و نخشى عذابك ان عذابك الجد بالكفار ملحق وصلى الله على النبي و آله و سلم
And one does not recite qunut in other than witr. Qunut means supplication, and it is to say: O Allah, we seek Your help, we seek Your guidance, we seek Your forgiveness and repent to You, we believe in You and rely on You, we praise You with all good, we thank You and do not disbelieve in You, we disown and forsake those who disobey You. O Allah, You alone we worship, to You we pray and prostrate, to You we strive and hasten, we hope for Your mercy and fear Your punishment; indeed Your severe punishment will overtake the disbelievers. And may Allah send blessings upon the Prophet and his family and grant them peace.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Thamaratun Najah. It establishes that qunut (a specific supplication) is performed only in the witr prayer, not in any other prayer such as fajr. The author then defines qunut as supplication (du'a) and provides the full Arabic text of the qunut that should be recited. This qunut includes praise of Allah, seeking help, guidance, forgiveness, and expressions of faith, as well as disavowal of those who disobey Him. The text ends with salawat upon the Prophet. According to the Hanafi school, this qunut is recited before ruku' in witr throughout the year. The passage implicitly refutes the Shafi'i position that qunut is also recited in fajr prayer.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunut): A specific supplication recited in witr prayer, meaning humble obedience and supplication.

Muqtadi's Response to Imam's Extra Supplication After Qunut
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on muqtadi's response to imam's extra dua after qunut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the muqtadi's response to the imam's additional supplication after qunut and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
When the imam adds a supplication after qunut, the muqtadi says 'amin', not recite — this is the relied-upon Hanafi view.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad on how the follower should respond when the imam supplements the witr qunut with extra dua. Abu Yusuf holds the follower should recite with the imam, while Muhammad holds that only 'amin' is said. The preferred position is that of Muhammad, which aligns with the practice of the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of dispute
The ikhtilaf concerns what the muqtadi does when the imam recites an extra supplication after the standard qunut in witr prayer.
The standard qunut is wajib; the extra supplication is supererogatory.
2
State Abu Yusuf's ruling
Abu Yusuf said: 'They follow him and recite it with him.' The muqtadi should recite the same supplication silently.
This view emphasises following the imam in all prayer acts.
3
State Muhammad's ruling
Muhammad said: 'They do not follow him but say amin.' The muqtadi should remain quiet and say amin.
This view is based on the hadith of saying amin after the imam's supplication.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Imam Muhammad, and this is the fatwa in the Hanafi school.
Abu Hanifa implicitly agreed with Muhammad.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, a Hanafi muqtadi should say amin and not recite the extra supplication.
Reciting it does not invalidate the prayer but is against the preferred practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا شرع الامام في الدعاء بعد ما تقدّم قال ابو يوسف رحمه الله يتابعونه ويقرؤونه معه وقال محمد لا يتابعونه ولكن يؤمنون والدعاء هو هذا اللهم اهدنا بفضلك فيمن هديت و عافنا فيمن عافيت و تولنا فيمن توليت و بارك لنا فيما اعطيت و قنا شر ما قضيت انك تقضى ولا يقضى عليك انه لا يذل من واليت ولا يعز من عاديت تباركت ربنا و تعاليت و صلى الله على سيدنا محمد و آله و صحبه و سلم
And when the imam begins the supplication after what has preceded, Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, said: They follow him and recite it with him. And Muhammad said: They do not follow him, but rather say amin. And the supplication is this: O Allah, guide us with Your grace among those You have guided, and pardon us among those You have pardoned, and take us into Your care among those You have taken into care, and bless us in what You have given, and protect us from the evil of what You have decreed. Indeed, You decree and none can decree against You. Indeed, he whom You befriend is not humbled, and he whom You treat as an enemy is not honored. Blessed are You, our Lord, and Exalted. And may Allah send blessings upon our master Muhammad, his family, and his companions, and grant them peace.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the muqtadi's response when the imam recites an additional supplication after the standard qunut (the one beginning with 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuka'). Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the muqtadi should follow the imam and recite this additional supplication along with him. Imam Muhammad holds that the muqtadi should not recite but rather respond with 'amin' throughout. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of Imam Muhammad (and implicitly Abu Hanifa), that the muqtadi only says 'amin' and does not recite the additional supplication. The text then provides the full wording of this additional supplication, which is similar to the qunut recited in the Shafi'i school for fajr. The dispute is based on different understandings of how closely the muqtadi should follow the imam in supererogatory acts within the prayer.

Key Terms
مؤتم (mu'tam): Follower in prayer, one who prays behind an imam.
دعاء (du'a): Supplication, here referring to the additional supplication after the standard qunut.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Recite the same supplication
B) Remain silent
C) Say amin
D) Recite the standard qunut again

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that the muqtadi says 'amin' and does not recite the additional supplication after qunut.

The Muqtadi Recites Qunut in Witr
Ruling that the muqtadi recites Qunut in Witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the follower (muqtadi) must recite Qunut in Witr prayer behind the imam and explain why it is wajib.

Core Idea
The follower recites Qunut himself; the imam's du'a does not substitute.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah delivers a clear ruling on the muqtadi's recitation of Qunut in Witr prayer. While many assume the imam's supplication covers all, the Hanafi school holds that the follower must actively recite the Qunut dua. This lesson examines that ruling and its basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and context
We are dealing with the Witr prayer in congregation. The act in question is the recitation of Qunut by the follower (muqtadi).
2
State the ruling
The matn states: 'And the follower recites Qunut like the imam.' This is the relied-upon Hanafi position: the muqtadi must recite Qunut.
3
Explain the underlying principle
In Hanafi fiqh, the imam's recitation only covers the Qur'anic recitation for the follower. For supplications (du'a) and tasbihat, the follower must recite them himself. Thus, Qunut, being a supplication, is individually wajib on the muqtadi.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that the follower is excused from all recitation behind the imam, including Qunut. This ikhtilaf stems from different views on the role of the imam's recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمؤتم يقرأ القنوت كالامام
And the follower recites the Qunut like the imam.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of Thamaratun Najah on the chapter of Witr. It establishes that when praying Witr behind an imam, the follower (muqtadi) must recite the Qunut supplication himself, just as the imam does. The commentary explains that the imam's recitation suffices for the follower only in terms of the Qur'anic recitation, but for supplications (du'a) and tasbihat, the follower must recite them himself. Thus, the Qunut dua is obligatory upon the follower as well.

Key Terms
المؤتم (al-mu'tam): The person who follows the imam in congregational prayer.
القنوت (al-qunut): A specific supplication recited in the Witr prayer, and also in Fajr during times of calamity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Yes, the follower recites Qunut like the imam
C) Only if the follower is alone
D) Only in the last ten nights of Ramadan

Key Takeaway
The muqtadi must recite Qunut in Witr; it is wajib upon him.

Alternatives for Qunut in Witr
Ruling on alternatives for Qunut recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on what to recite in Qunut if one cannot memorize the standard dua and identify the alternatives provided by the matn.

Core Idea
The Qunut obligation is fulfilled by any supplication; specific wording is not required.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: a person praying Witr who has not memorized the Qunut supplication. The matn provides clear alternatives, demonstrating that the essence of Qunut is du'a (supplication), not a fixed text. This reflects the Hanafi school's flexibility in acts of worship where the specific wording is not an integral part.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that the act being discussed is the recitation of Qunut in the Witr prayer. The Qunut is a supplication made after the ruku' of the last rak'ah.
2
State the default obligation
The default obligation is to make a supplication (du'a) in Qunut. The specific wording is not mandatory; any supplication fulfills the wajib.
This is based on the Hanafi principle that the obligation is the act of supplicating, not the specific words.
3
Recall the alternatives
Memorize the three alternatives given in the matn: (1) 'Allahumma ighfir li' three times, (2) 'Rabbana atina fi al-dunya hasanah...' (Quran 2:201), (3) 'Ya Rabb, Ya Rabb, Ya Rabb' three times.
These are not exhaustive; any supplication is acceptable.
4
Understand the rationale
Understand that the allowance for alternatives is based on the narration from Ali (ra) that the Prophet (saw) recited a different dua in Witr, indicating flexibility. The obligation is to make du'a, not to recite a fixed text.
This ruling shows the Hanafi school's emphasis on the spirit over the letter in acts of worship where no specific text is prescribed by the Quran or mutawatir sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن لم يحسن القنوت يقول اللهم اغفر لي ثلاث مرات او ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة و في الآخرة حسنة وقنا عذاب النار او يا رب يا رب يا رب
And whoever does not know the Qunut says 'O Allah, forgive me' three times, or 'Our Lord, give us in this world good and in the Hereafter good and protect us from the punishment of the Fire', or 'O Lord, O Lord, O Lord'.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This is a practical ruling from the matn providing alternatives for someone who has not memorized the Qunut supplication. The Qunut is wajib, but if one cannot recite the prescribed dua, they may substitute it with any supplication, such as asking for forgiveness three times, reciting the Quranic verse (2:201), or simply saying 'Ya Rabb' three times. This shows that the obligation is to make any supplication, not necessarily the specific one. The commentary from Thamaratun Najah mentions that this is based on a narration from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) where the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited a different dua in his Witr, indicating that no particular words are mandatory.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): The prescribed supplication in Witr prayer, but its exact wording is not strictly mandatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person does not memorize the Qunut dua, what should he recite according to the Hanafi school?
A) Say 'Allahumma ighfir li' three times
B) Recite Surah al-Fatiha
C) Remain silent
D) Say takbir instead

Key Takeaway
The Qunut in Witr is fulfilled by any du'a; if one cannot recite the standard wording, alternatives such as 'Allahumma ighfir li' suffice.

Hanafi Follower Behind an Imam Reciting Qunut in Fajr
Short matn giving the rule for a Hanafi follower behind a Qunut-reciting imam in Fajr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a follower who prays Fajr behind an imam reciting Qunut and identify the correct posture.

Core Idea
A Hanafi follower stands silent, hands relaxed, when a Shafi'i imam recites Qunut in Fajr.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in mixed-madhhab congregations: a Hanafi follower praying Fajr behind a Shafi'i imam who recites Qunut. The Hanafi school does not consider Qunut in Fajr as sunnah except during calamity. Therefore, the follower must not recite the Qunut but should remain standing silently out of respect for the imam's practice. The correct posture, according to Zahir al-Riwayah, is with hands hanging at the sides.

Guided Path
1
Identify the imam's madhhab
Determine that the imam follows a school (e.g., Shafi'i) that recites Qunut in Fajr as a regular sunnah.
The Hanafi school only incorporates Qunut in Fajr during major calamities (Qunut al-Nazilah).
2
Recognize the Hanafi ruling
Understand that according to Hanafi fiqh, a follower must not recite Qunut in Fajr behind such an imam. Reciting would be against the Hanafi position.
The follower's obligation is to remain silent and not participate in the Qunut recitation.
3
Apply the correct conduct
The follower stands silently, with hands relaxed at the sides (sadl), waiting for the imam to complete the Qunut and proceed to ruku'.
The posture of silent waiting is distinct from raising hands in du'a or clasping them.
4
Consider the exception
If the imam recites Qunut al-Nazilah (calamity Qunut), the Hanafi follower may silently say 'Ameen' and also raise hands, as Hanafis do perform this Qunut.
This exception applies only when the Qunut is for a specific calamity, not the regular Fajr Qunut.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اقتدى بمن يقنت فى الفجر قام معه في قنوته ساكتا
And if one follows someone who recites Qunut in Fajr, he stands with him in his Qunut silently.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn regarding a Hanafi follower who is praying Fajr behind an imam (e.g., a Shafi'i imam) who recites Qunut in Fajr. According to the Hanafi school, Qunut in Fajr is not Sunnah except in times of calamity (Qunut al-Nazilah). Therefore, the follower should not recite the Qunut but should remain standing silently. The commentary adds that in the Zahir al-Riwayah, the follower keeps his hands at his sides (sadl) rather than raising them or clasping them, as this is the proper posture for silent waiting. The note at the end of the passage explains that Qunut is of three types: Qunut al-Nazilah (during calamity, which Hanafis consider Sunnah in Fajr if a great calamity occurs), Qunut in Fajr always (which Hanafis do not practice but Shafi'is do), and Qunut in Witr (which Hanafis consider wajib throughout the year while Shafi'is only in the last half of Ramadan).

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): In this context, Qunut in Fajr prayer which is practiced by Shafi'is but not by Hanafis except during calamity.
ساكتا (sakitan): Silent, not reciting anything, and according to the commentary, with hands hanging at the sides.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Qunut in Fajr and Witr
Comparative note on three types of Qunut across Hanafi and Shafi'i schools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on Qunut in Fajr and Witr prayers and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of this difference.

Core Idea
Hanafis restrict Qunut in Fajr to calamities and recite it in Witr year-round; Shafi'is recite it in Fajr always and in Witr only in the last half of Ramadan.

This lesson examines a comparative note from a Hanafi text that classifies three types of Qunut: Qunut Nazila (during calamity), regular Qunut in Fajr, and Qunut in Witr. While both schools agree on the general merit of qunut, they differ on when and where it is recommended. We will explore these differences and their implications for prayer practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
List the three types of Qunut mentioned in the note: (1) Qunut Nazila during calamity, (2) Qunut in Fajr, (3) Qunut in Witr.
2
State the Hanafi position
For each category, note the Hanafi ruling: Qunut Nazila is Sunnah during great calamity; regular Qunut in Fajr is not prescribed; Qunut in Witr is recited throughout the year.
The Hanafi school considers Qunut in Witr as wajib.
3
State the Shafi'i position
For each category, note the Shafi'i ruling: Qunut in Fajr is recited every day; Qunut in Witr is recited only in the last half of Ramadan; Qunut Nazila is not a separate category.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference in daily prayer: Hanafis do not recite Qunut in Fajr normally; Shafi'is do. In Witr, Hanafis recite Qunut every night; Shafi'is only in the last half of Ramadan.
This directly affects the prayer practice of followers of each school.
5
Note the evidentiary basis
The text refers to proofs that have 'passed above', indicating that detailed evidence is not repeated here. Understand that the difference stems from varying interpretations of Prophetic practice.
Hanafis rely on the hadith that the Prophet recited Qunut Nazila for one month then left it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نوٹ : دعاء قنوت تین قسم کی ہیں [1] مصیبت کے وقت قنوت نازلہ پڑھنا، حضور نے ایک مہینہ پڑھا اسکے بعد چھوڑ دیا۔ البتہ عظیم مصیبت کے وقت ابھی بھی حنفیہ کے یہاں فجر کی نماز میں پڑھنا مسنون ہے ۔ [۲] فجر کی نماز میں ہمیشہ قنوت پڑھنا، یہ حنفیہ کے یہاں نہیں ہے اور امام شافعی کے یہاں ہے۔ [۳] وتر میں دعاء قنوت پڑھنا۔ یہ امام شافعی کے یہاں صرف رمضان کے نصف اخیر میں ہے، باقی دنوں میں نہیں۔ اور حنفیہ کے یہاں پورے سال میں ہے ۔۔ دلائل اور تفصیل اوپر گزرگئی ۔
Note: Supplication of Qunut is of three types: [1] Reciting Qunut Nazila at the time of calamity; the Prophet recited it for one month then left it. However, in the Hanafi school, it is still Sunnah to recite it in Fajr prayer during a great calamity. [2] Reciting Qunut always in Fajr prayer; this is not in the Hanafi school but is in the Shafi'i school. [3] Reciting Qunut in Witr. In the Shafi'i school, this is only in the last half of Ramadan, not on other days. In the Hanafi school, it is throughout the year. The proofs and details have passed above.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This note summarizes the three categories of Qunut and highlights the key differences between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. First, Qunut Nazila is a supplication during a major calamity; the Hanafis consider it Sunnah to recite in Fajr when such calamity occurs, following the Prophet's practice. Second, the permanent Qunut in Fajr is not recognized by Hanafis but is a practice in the Shafi'i school. Third, Qunut in Witr: Shafi'is restrict it to the last half of Ramadan, while Hanafis recite it throughout the year. The note serves to clarify the madhhab positions without delving into detailed proofs here.

Key Terms
قنوت نازلہ (qunut nazilah): A special supplication recited in Fajr prayer during a time of great calamity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Hanafi Follower During Imam's Qunut in Fajr
Ruling on Hanafi follower when imam recites Qunut in Fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a Hanafi follower when the imam recites Qunut in Fajr, and explain the rationale based on the principle of remaining silent during the imam's recitation.

Core Idea
A Hanafi follower remains silent with hands at sides when the imam recites Qunut in Fajr.

This lesson addresses a common situation for Hanafi Muslims praying behind a Shafi'i imam. The Shafi'i school recites the Qunut supplication in the Fajr prayer, while the Hanafi school does not. What should a Hanafi follower do? The classical Hanafi texts provide clear guidance to maintain both the unity of the congregation and the integrity of one's own madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Identify the act of the Hanafi follower: following (iqtida) an imam who recites Qunut in Fajr.
The imam is Shafi'i, but the ruling applies to any imam who recites Qunut in Fajr.
2
Identify the required action
The follower must stand with the imam (in qiyam) but remain silent (sakitan) and keep his hands at his sides (yursilu yadayhi fi janbayhi).
Silence means not reciting any du'a, including Qunut, and not saying Amin.
3
Identify the prohibited actions
The follower should not recite Qunut, raise his hands, or say Amin aloud.
Raising hands is part of the Shafi'i Qunut but not part of the Hanafi prayer.
4
Understand the rationale
The follower follows the imam in the standing, but since Qunut is not part of the Hanafi prayer, he remains silent to avoid adding an element not prescribed in his own madhhab.
The prayer remains valid if he remains silent; if he recites Qunut, his prayer may become invalid or at least makruh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اقتدى بمن يقنت فى الفجر قام معه في قنوته ساكتا ويُرسل يديه في جنبيه.
And if he follows one who recites Qunut in Fajr, he stands with him in his Qunut silently and lets his hands hang at his sides.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This ruling addresses a common scenario: a Hanafi follower praying behind a Shafi'i imam who recites Qunut in Fajr. According to the zahir al-riwayah (the apparent transmission), the follower should remain silent and not recite any supplication. He should also keep his hands at his sides, not raise them. This is because the follower is to follow the imam's actions but maintain his own madhhab's ruling regarding silence during Qunut.

Key Terms
ساكتا (sakitan): Silent, not reciting anything while the imam recites Qunut.
قنوت (qunut): A supplication recited in prayer, especially in Fajr (Shafi'i) or Witr (Hanafi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Forgetting Qunut in Witr and Remembering in Ruku
Ruling on forgetting Qunut in Witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on forgetting Qunut in Witr and identify the correct action when it is remembered during or after ruku.

Core Idea
The time for Qunut is before ruku; once ruku is entered, the opportunity is lost.

In the Witr prayer, Qunut is recited before ruku. But what if you forget and only remember while bowing? This short lesson gives a clear rule from the Hanafi school: once you are in ruku, you do not return to recite Qunut. Let's examine the exact ruling and its logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is forgetting to recite Qunut (القنوت) in the Witr prayer and then remembering it later.
2
Identify the condition
The condition specified in the text: the person remembers while in ruku (الركوع) or after rising from ruku (الرفع منه).
'After rising from ruku' means standing up to qiyam after ruku.
3
State the ruling
The ruling is clear: لا يقنت — he does not recite Qunut. The time has passed.
4
Understand the principle
The place for Qunut in Witr is before ruku. Once you have entered the ruku position, the proper place is exited, and you cannot go back.
This principle preserves the order of the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا نسى القنوت فى الوتر وتذكره في الركوع او الرفع منه لا يقنت.
And if he forgets Qunut in Witr and remembers it in ruku or after rising from it, he does not recite Qunut.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This is a clear ruling: the proper place for Qunut in Witr is before ruku. If one forgets and only remembers after having bowed into ruku or after standing up from ruku, the opportunity has passed. He should not interrupt the prayer to go back; instead, he continues and performs sajdah sahw at the end as noted in the next ruling.

Key Terms
الرفع منه (al-raf' minhu): Rising from ruku, i.e., standing up to the qiyam position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The proper place for Qunut in Witr is before ruku; once ruku is entered, the opportunity to recite Qunut is lost and one must not return to it.

Ruling on Reciting Qunut After Ruku
Ruling statement on Qunut after ruku

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when Qunut is recited after ruku and explain why Sujud al-Sahw is required.

Core Idea
Reciting Qunut after ruku does not invalidate the prayer but requires Sujud al-Sahw.

In prayer, every action has a specific place (mahall asli). If you recite Qunut after ruku instead of before, the order is disturbed. This lesson explains the ruling: the ruku is valid, but you must perform Sujud al-Sahw to compensate for the delay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the deviation
The worshiper recited Qunut after raising his head from ruku, which is after its original place (before ruku).
2
Determine the effect on ruku
The ruku itself is not invalidated; it remains valid and does not need to be repeated.
This is because the ruku was performed correctly; only the Qunut was delayed.
3
Identify the required compensation
Sujud al-Sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) must be performed at the end of the prayer.
4
Understand the reason
Sujud al-Sahw is required because the Qunut left its original place (mahall asli), which is considered a wajib that has been delayed.
The prayer remains valid but the delay requires compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قنت بعد رفع رأسه من الركوع لا يعيد الركوع ويسجد للسهو لزوال القنوت عن محله الاصلي.
And if he recites Qunut after raising his head from ruku, he does not repeat the ruku and performs sajdah sahw because the Qunut has left its original place.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This ruling clarifies the situation where someone mistakenly recites Qunut after standing up from ruku, thinking it was before ruku. The ruku itself is valid and does not need to be repeated. However, since the Qunut was recited out of its proper place (which is before ruku), the prayer has been performed with an act out of sequence. This is a type of delay (ta'khir) that requires sujud al-sahw to compensate for the deviation from the proper order.

Key Terms
محل اصلي (mahall asli): The original place of an action in prayer, here meaning before ruku for Qunut.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Repeat the ruku
B) Perform sajdah sahw
C) Repeat the entire prayer
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
Reciting Qunut after ruku does not invalidate the ruku; you perform Sujud al-Sahw to compensate for the delay.

Following the Imam in Ruku: Priority Over Completing Qunut
Ruling on follower's priority during Qunut when imam bows early.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a follower when the imam goes into ruku before Qunut is completed and explain why mutaba'ah takes precedence.

Core Idea
Catch the imam's ruku even if Qunut is incomplete — mutaba'ah overrides sunnah.

In congregational prayer, the follower must follow the imam's actions. But what if you are reciting the Qunut in Witr and the imam suddenly bows for ruku? Should you finish Qunut or join the ruku? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on this common situation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The imam makes ruku before the follower finishes reciting Qunut or even before starting it.
The source text covers both cases: during Qunut and before starting.
2
Assess the follower's fear
The follower must genuinely fear missing the ruku — that is, he cannot complete Qunut and still catch the ruku with the imam.
If there is no fear (e.g., the imam bows slowly), the ruling may differ.
3
Apply the ruling
If fear exists, the follower must immediately stop Qunut (or not start it) and go into ruku with the imam.
This is based on the principle that mutaba'ah (following the imam) is a wajib act.
4
Understand the rationale
Mutaba'ah is obligatory; Qunut is a sunnah. A sunnah cannot delay an obligatory act.
Missing a rukn like ruku without excuse can invalidate the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ركع الامام قبل فراغ المقتدى من قراءة القنوت او قبل شروع المقتدى في القنوت وخاف فوت الركوع يتابع الامام.
And if the imam makes ruku before the follower finishes reciting Qunut or before the follower starts Qunut, and he fears missing the ruku, he should follow the imam.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This ruling prioritizes following the imam over completing the Qunut. If the imam goes into ruku while the follower is still reciting Qunut or hasn't started yet, and the follower fears he will not catch the ruku with the imam, he should stop his Qunut and immediately go into ruku with the imam. This is based on the principle that the follower must follow the imam in actions, and catching the ruku is more important than completing a sunnah act like Qunut.

Key Terms
متابعة (mutaba'ah): Following the imam in all actions of the prayer.
قنوت (qunut): A supplication recited in the Witr prayer (and sometimes in Fajr) after the ruku or before it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Stop Qunut and immediately go into ruku.
C) Follow the imam only if the Qunut is long.
D) Recite Qunut louder to remind the imam.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi prayer, following the imam (mutaba'ah) takes precedence over completing a sunnah recitation like Qunut when there is risk of missing an obligatory action.

Forgetting Qunut in Witr Prayer
Ruling on not reciting Qunut after remembering in bowing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when Qunut is forgotten in Witr and apply the principle that the time for Qunut ends at bowing.

Core Idea
If Qunut is forgotten, its time ends at bowing; do not recite it after.

In the Hanafi school, Qunut in Witr is wajib and is recited before bowing. But what happens if you forget it and only remember after you have already started bowing? This passage gives a clear ruling, supported by a hadith about following the imam. Understanding this rule is essential for correct prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting Qunut in Witr. The ruling is that it is wajib, but if forgotten and remembered in bowing, do not recite it.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Aisha (رضي الله عنها) in Sahih al-Bukhari: 'انما جعل الامام ليؤتم به...'
The hadith emphasizes following the imam.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith commands following the imam's actions. Since the imam has moved to bowing, the follower should not delay to recite Qunut.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may allow reciting Qunut after bowing, but the Hanafi school holds it is not allowed.
This is a mukhtalaf fih issue.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the principle that acts of prayer have specific places; missing the place means the act is no longer valid.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) is to not recite Qunut after bowing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if he forgets Qunut in Witr and remembers it in bowing or after rising from bowing, he does not recite Qunut.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage states a ruling regarding the Qunut supplication in Witr prayer. The time for Qunut is before bowing. If one forgets to recite it and remembers only after entering the bowing position or after rising from it, the moment for Qunut has passed, so he does not recite it then. The commentary cites a hadith emphasizing that the follower must follow the imam, and then gives the specific ruling.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunūt): The supplication recited in the Witr prayer before bowing.
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, consisting of three rak'ahs.

6 min
Reciting Qunut After Rising from Bowing
Ruling on Qunut delay in Witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when Qunut is recited after bowing in Witr, identify the proof from the Tabi'i Hammad, and explain why sajda sahw is required.

Core Idea
Delaying Qunut from its proper place requires sajda sahw, but the bowing remains valid.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in Witr prayer: the worshipper mistakenly recites Qunut after rising from bowing. Does this invalidate the bowing? Is sajda sahw needed? The Hanafi position provides a clear and practical answer, balancing textual proof and legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The ruling applies when a person in Witr prayer raises his head from bowing (from ruku') and then recites the Qunut supplication, instead of reciting it before bowing.
This is a case of forgetfulness (sahw) – a delay in the prescribed order.
2
State the two-part ruling
First: the bowing is valid and does not need to be repeated. Second: two prostrations of forgetfulness (sajda sahw) must be performed at the end of the prayer.
The bowing was performed correctly; only the placement of Qunut is affected.
3
Understand the legal reasoning
The Qunut has left its original place (before bowing), causing a delay (ta'khir) in a wajib act. In Hanafi fiqh, delaying a wajib from its proper time without a valid reason necessitates compensation via sajda sahw.
This principle applies to other acts like the tashahhud or salawat.
4
Analyze the proof
The proof is the statement of the Tabi'i Hammad: 'If he forgets before he recites Qunut, then let him perform two prostrations of forgetfulness' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba). This indicates that forgetfulness concerning Qunut triggers sajda sahw.
Though the chain is mursal, it is accepted in Hanafi practice for such details.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قنت بعد رفع رأسه من الركوع لا يعيد الركوع ويسجد للسهو لزوال القنوت عن محله الاصلي ... ترجمه : (۲۱۱) اور اگر رکوع سے سر اٹھانے کے بعد دعاء قنوت پڑھی تو رکوع کو دوبارہ نہ لوٹائے لیکن اصلی محل سے قنوت زائل ہونے کی وجہ سے سجدہ سہو کرے۔ تشریح : رکوع اپنی جگہ پر ادا ہوا ہے اس لئے اس کو لوٹانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے البتہ دعاء قنوت اپنی اصلی جگہ سے ہٹ گئی ہے اور سجدے میں تاخیر ہوئی ہے اس لئے سجدہ سہو کرے۔ وجه : عن حماد قال اذا سها قبل ان يقنت فليسجد سجدتي السهو يعني في الوتر ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، باب فی السھو فی قنوت الوتر ، ج ثانی ص ۱۰۰ نمبر ۶۹۴۶) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ دعاء قنوت بھول جائے تو سجدہ سہو کرے۔
And if he recites Qunut after raising his head from bowing, he does not repeat the bowing and performs sajda sahw because the Qunut has left its original place.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This ruling addresses the case where someone mistakenly recites Qunut after rising from bowing. The bowing itself was correct and does not need to be repeated. However, because the Qunut was delayed from its proper place (before bowing), a sajda sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) is required. The proof cited is the statement of the tabi‘i Hammad that if one forgets before Qunut (i.e., omits or delays it), he should perform two prostrations of forgetfulness in Witr.

Key Terms
سجدة السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Two prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for forgetfulness.
قنوت (qunut): A supplication recited in the Witr prayer, considered wajib in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone recites Qunut after rising from bowing in Witr, what action is required?
A) Repeat the entire prayer.
B) Repeat the bowing and then perform sajda sahw.
C) Do not repeat the bowing but perform sajda sahw.
D) No action needed because Qunut is optional.

Key Takeaway
When Qunut is recited after its prescribed place in Witr, the bowing remains valid, but sajda sahw is wajib to compensate for the delay.

Follower's Qunut When Imam Bows Early
Ruling on follower leaving Qunut to join imam in bowing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that following the imam takes precedence over reciting Qunut when the imam bows early.

Core Idea
When the imam bows early, the follower must abandon Qunut and join the bowing.

This lesson examines a common scenario in congregational prayer: the follower is reciting Qunut in Witr, but the imam proceeds to bow before the follower finishes. The Hanafi school resolves this conflict by prioritizing following the imam. We will explore the ruling, its evidence, and the reasoning behind this priority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the follower's recitation of Qunut (wajib) conflicting with the requirement to follow the imam in bowing (also wajib). The ruling is that the follower must abandon Qunut and bow with the imam.
The ruling depends on the follower fearing to miss the bowing.
2
Locate the dalil
The main evidence is the hadith: 'The imam is appointed to be followed; when he bows, bow.' This command establishes that following the imam is obligatory and takes precedence.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'bow' (fa-rka'u) indicates obligation. The command is directed to the follower, implying that the follower must bow when the imam bows, even if engaged in another wajib act like Qunut.
The conflict of two wajibat is resolved by giving priority to the stronger evidence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that the follower should complete Qunut even if it means missing the bowing, because Qunut is a confirmed sunnah that should not be interrupted.
The Hanafi position relies on the explicit command to follow the imam.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi view is that following the imam is wajib based on a direct command, while Qunut is also wajib but can be abandoned to preserve congregational unity. The mufta bihi is to abandon Qunut and bow.
This ruling is found in later Hanafi fatwa collections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ركع الامام قبل فراغ المقتدى من قراءة القنوت او قبل شروعه فيه وخاف فوت الركوع تابع امامه ... ترجمه : (۶۱۲) اگر امام نے مقتدی کے قنوت پوری کرنے سے پہلے رکوع کر لیا، یا قنوت کو شروع کرنے سے پہلے رکوع کر لیا اور خوف ہے کہ رکوع فوت ہو جائے گا تو امام کی اتباع کرے۔ تشریح : اگر امام نے مقتدی کے قنوت شروع کرنے سے پہلے، یا شروع تو کر چکا تھا لیکن اس کو پوری کرنے سے پہلے رکوع کر لیا تو ، اور مقتدی کو خوف ہے کہ اگر میں نے قنوت پڑی تو امام کے ساتھ رکوع کے اخیر حصے میں بھی نہیں مل پاؤں گا تو قوت چھوڑ کر امام کے ساتھ رکوع میں مل جائے ۔
And if the imam bows before the follower finishes reciting Qunut, or before he begins it, and he fears missing the bowing, he should follow his imam.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This ruling discusses the follower's obligation when the imam bows early. The follower is required to follow the imam in all actions. Therefore, if the imam bows before the follower has completed or even started the Qunut, and there is a fear that the follower will miss the bowing entirely if he continues with Qunut, he should abandon the Qunut and join the imam in bowing. Following the imam takes precedence over reciting Qunut.

Key Terms
المقتدى (al-muqtadī): The follower praying behind an imam.
القنوت (al-qunūt): A supplication recited in the Witr prayer, considered wajib in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a follower is reciting Qunut in Witr and the imam bows before he finishes, what should he do if he fears missing the bowing?
A) Continue reciting Qunut and then bow quickly.
B) Stop reciting Qunut and bow with the imam.
C) Complete the Qunut even if it means missing the bowing.
D) Signal the imam to wait.

Key Takeaway
When the imam bows early, the follower must abandon Qunut and join the bowing, as following the imam takes precedence over completing the Qunut.
