When the Imam Omits Qunut: The Follower's Option
Ruling on follower reciting Qunut if imam omits it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition for a follower to recite Qunut when the imam omits it, and state the ruling when catching the bowing is impossible.

Core Idea
The follower recites Qunut only if he can still join the imam in bowing; otherwise, following the imam takes priority.

In Witr prayer, Qunut is a wajib act. If the imam omits it—whether forgetfully or intentionally—the follower must decide whether to recite it himself. This lesson explains the precise condition that determines when the follower should act independently and when he must follow the imam. The key is whether reciting Qunut would cause him to miss the bowing (ruku).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage rules on a situation where the imam omits Qunut in Witr. The follower (mu'tamm) does not automatically omit it too; he has a conditional option.
Remember: Qunut is wajib, not fard.
2
State the condition
The follower may recite Qunut only if he can still share in the bowing (ruku) with the imam after finishing his own Qunut. This is the critical condition.
The phrase 'ان امكنه مشاركة الامام فى الركوع' means if he can catch the imam in ruku.
3
Apply the condition
If he can recite Qunut quickly and still join the imam in ruku, he should recite it. If reciting Qunut would make him miss ruku, he must abandon Qunut and follow the imam directly.
The principle: following the imam (mu'taba'ah) is more important than the specific wajib of Qunut.
4
Understand the rationale
The commentary explains that following the imam takes precedence over the du'a of Qunut. Therefore, if the two conflict, the follower prioritizes joining the imam in ruku.
This is based on the general maxim that the follower's obligation to follow the imam is paramount.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ترک الامام القنوت يأتى به المؤتم ان امكنه مشاركة الامام فى الركوع والا تابعه ... ترجمه : (۶۱۳) اور اگر امام نے قنوت چھوڑ دی تو اگر رکوع میں امام کے ساتھ شرکت کا امکان ہو تو مقتدی قنوت پڑھے، ور نہ تو امام کی اقتدا کرے۔ وجه : پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ امام کی اقتداء دعا کی بنسبت اہم ہے اس لئے اگر رکوع میں امام کے ساتھ ملنے کی امید ہو تو دعاقنوت بھی پڑھے اور رکوع میں مل جائے ، اور امکان نہیں ہے تو دعا چھوڑ کر امام کے ساتھ مل جائے۔
And if the imam omits the Qunut, the follower recites it if he is able to share in the bowing with the imam, otherwise he follows him.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This ruling explains the follower's option when the imam intentionally or forgetfully omits the Qunut. The follower may recite Qunut himself if he can still catch up to the imam in the bowing. However, if reciting Qunut would cause him to miss the bowing, he should abandon Qunut and follow the imam. The principle is that following the imam is more important than performing the Qunut.

Key Terms
المؤتم (al-mu'tamm): The follower (same as muqtadi).
القنوت (al-qunut): A supplication recited in the Witr prayer, considered wajib in the Hanafi school.
مشاركة الامام فى الركوع (musharakat al-imam fi al-ruku'): Sharing/catching the imam in the bowing position, i.e., performing ruku with him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, when should the follower recite Qunut if the imam omits it?
A) Never; he must always follow the imam.
B) Always, regardless of the imam's action.
C) Only if he can still catch the bowing with the imam after reciting it.
D) Only if the imam omitted it forgetfully.

Key Takeaway
The follower should recite Qunut only if it does not cause him to miss the bowing with the imam; otherwise, following the imam takes precedence.

Catching the Imam in the Third Rak'ah of Witr: Ruling on Qunut
Ruling on follower catching imam in bowing of third rak'ah of Witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a follower who catches the imam in the bowing of the third rak'ah of Witr and explain why he does not recite Qunut in the rak'ahs he makes up.

Core Idea
Catching the bowing of a rak'ah means catching the entire rak'ah, including its Qunut.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in congregational Witr prayer. If a follower joins after the imam has started the third rak'ah, does he need to recite Qunut in the rak'ahs he makes up? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the principle that catching the bowing (ruku') constitutes catching the rak'ah. We will explore this ruling and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a follower catching the imam in the bowing of the third rak'ah of Witr. The ruling is that he is considered to have caught the Qunut and does not recite it in the rak'ahs he makes up.
2
Understand the underlying principle
In Hanafi fiqh, catching the bowing of a rak'ah means catching the entire rak'ah, including its recitation and specific obligations like Qunut.
This is based on the general principle that ruku' is a key integral of the rak'ah.
3
Apply the principle to the scenario
Since the follower caught the bowing of the third rak'ah, he is considered to have caught the Qunut that the imam recited before bowing.
The imam's Qunut suffices for the follower.
4
Derive the ruling for the rak'ahs he makes up
When the follower continues his prayer after the imam's salam, he does not need to recite Qunut in the first and second rak'ahs he makes up.
5
Note the authority and cross-madhhab difference
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school. Some other schools require the follower to recite Qunut even if he caught the imam's.
The practical difference is whether the follower recites Qunut in his own rak'ahs or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ادرک الامام في ركوع الثالثة من الوتر كان مدركا للقنوت فلا يأتى به فيما سبق به ... ترجمه (۶۱۴) اور اگروتر کی تیسری رکعت کے رکوع میں امام سے ملے تو گویا اس کو قنوت مل گیا، اب اس کو اپنی باقی رکعت میں نہ پڑھے۔ تشریح : یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ رکوع مل گیا تو اس رکعت کی قرآت مل گئی ، اسی طرح تیسری رکعت کے رکوع میں امام کے ساتھ ملاتو گویا کہ وہ رکعت مل گئی ، اس لئے امام کی دعاء قنوت اس مقتدی کے لئے کافی ہو جائے گی ۔ اب جب پہلی اور دوسری رکعت پڑھے گا تو اس میں دعاء قنوت پڑھنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہوگی۔
And if he catches the imam in the bowing of the third rak'ah of Witr, he has caught the Qunut, so he does not recite it in what he missed.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This ruling addresses a follower who joins the congregation after the imam has already begun the third rak'ah of Witr. If he catches the imam in the bowing of that rak'ah, he is considered to have caught the Qunut that the imam recited before bowing. Therefore, he does not need to recite Qunut in the rak'ahs he makes up after the imam's salam. The principle is that catching the bowing of a rak'ah means catching that rak'ah, including its Qunut.

Key Terms
مدرك (mudrik): One who catches a part of the prayer with the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a follower joins the Witr prayer when the imam is in the bowing of the third rak'ah, what is the ruling regarding Qunut?
A) He must recite Qunut in the rak'ahs he makes up after the imam.
B) He does not need to recite Qunut because he caught it with the imam.
C) He should recite Qunut before bowing in the third rak'ah if possible.
D) He must repeat the entire prayer because he missed Qunut.

Key Takeaway
A follower who catches the bowing of the third rak'ah of Witr has caught the Qunut and should not recite it in his own rak'ahs.

Praying Witr in Congregation – Limited to Ramadan
Ruling with proof (through reasoning) on Witr congregation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying Witr in congregation and explain the preferred view in the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Witr is prayed in congregation only in Ramadan; congregation is better than praying alone.

This passage clarifies a specific rule regarding the Witr prayer: it is performed in congregation only during Ramadan, following the Tarawih prayers. Outside Ramadan, Witr is prayed individually, ideally at the end of the night. There is a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars about which is better in Ramadan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states: 'ويوتر بجماعة في رمضان فقط' – He prays Witr with congregation only in Ramadan.
2
Understand the reason
The reason given is that in Ramadan, Witr follows Tarawih which is prayed in congregation.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some scholars hold that praying alone at the end of the night is better even in Ramadan.
4
Determine the preferred view
Qadi Khan chose the position that congregation is better; this is the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويوتر بجماعة في رمضان فقط وصلوته مع الجماعة افضل من ان يوتر وحده في آخر الليل ... ترجمه : (۶۱۵) اور صرف رمضان میں وتر کو جماعت سے پڑھے۔ اور رمضان میں اخیر شب میں تنہا وتر پڑھنے سے جماعت سے پڑھنا افضل ہے ۔ قاضی خان نے اس کو اختیار کر کے صحیح کہا ہے، اور دوسروں نے اس کے خلاف تصحیح کی ہے۔ تشریح : رمضان میں تراویح جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھتے ہیں، اور اس کے بعد وتر پڑھی جاتی ہے اس لئے وتر بھی جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھے ، اور باقی دنوں میں وتر سنت کے بعد پڑھتے ہیں اور اخیر رات میں پڑھنا افضل ہے اس لئے وتر جماعت کے ساتھ نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔ اور جن حضرات نے فرمایا کہ وتر تنہا پڑھنا افضل انکی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وتر رمضان میں بھی اخیر رات میں پڑھنا افضل ہے اس لئے اس کو تنہا پڑھے۔
And he prays Witr with congregation in Ramadan only, and his prayer with congregation is better than if he prays Witr alone at the end of the night.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This ruling specifies that Witr is performed in congregation only during Ramadan, following the Tarawih prayers. In other nights, Witr is prayed individually, and it is better to delay it to the last part of the night. There is an ikhtilaf: some scholars hold that praying Witr in congregation in Ramadan is better, while others say praying it alone at the end of the night is better even in Ramadan. The preferred view according to Qadi Khan is that congregation is better in Ramadan.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer after Isha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Every night throughout the year.
B) Only during the month of Ramadan.
C) Only on Friday nights.
D) Only when praying at the mosque.

Key Takeaway
Witr congregation is confined to Ramadan because of Tarawih; praying with congregation is better in Ramadan than praying alone.

Ruling on Muqtadi Reciting Qunut When Imam Omits It
Explains when a follower should recite Qunut if the imam leaves it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a muqtadi when the imam omits Qunut in Witr and determine whether to recite it based on the ability to join the imam in ruku.

Core Idea
When the imam omits Qunut, the follower recites it only if he can still join the imam in ruku — following the imam takes precedence.

This lesson examines a practical scenario in congregational Witr prayer: the imam omits the Qunut. What should the follower do? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling based on priority of following the imam. We will explore the proof from hadith and the application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the follower reciting Qunut when the imam omits it. The ruling is conditional: permissible if the follower can still join the imam in ruku; otherwise, he must follow without reciting.
The ruling balances the obligation to follow the imam and the desirability of Qunut.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Aisha (RA) in Sahih Bukhari: 'The imam is only appointed to be followed...'
The hadith establishes the general principle of following the imam.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'follow' indicates obligation. The hadith makes following the imam a duty; Qunut is a voluntary act that could conflict with that duty if it delays joining the imam.
The hadith's general command overrides specific practices when they conflict.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that the follower should always recite Qunut even if it delays joining the imam, because Qunut is a confirmed sunnah.
The difference stems from prioritizing the sunnah of Qunut versus the duty to follow.
5
Apply to the scenario
Check if joining the imam in ruku is possible after reciting Qunut. If yes, recite and join; if not, omit Qunut and follow immediately.
The muqtadi must gauge the timing of the imam's bowing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ترك الامام القنوت يأتي به المؤتم إن أمكنه مشاركة الامام في الركوع وإلا تابعه وجه: امام کی اتباع ضروری ہے، جبکہ دعا اتنی ضروری نہیں ہے۔ اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة أم المؤمنين أنها قالت صلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في بيته وهو شاك، فصلى جالسا وصلى وراءه قوم قياما فأشار إليهم أن اجلسوا، فلما انصرف قال ((إنما جعل الإمام ليؤتم به، فإذا ركع فاركعوا، وإذا رفع فارفعوا، وإذا قال سمع الله لمن حمده فقولوا ربنا لك الحمد، وإذا صلى جالسا فصلوا جلوسا)). (بخاری شریف، باب إنما جعل الإمام ليؤتم به ص ۹۵ نمبر ۶۸۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مقتدی کو چاہئے کہ امام کی پوری اتباع کرے۔ ترجمه: (۶۱۳) اور اگر امام نے قنوت چھوڑ دی تو اگر رکوع میں امام کے ساتھ شرکت کا امکان ہو تو مقتدی قنوت پڑھے، ورنہ امام کی اقتدا کرے۔ وجه: پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ امام کی اقتداء دعا کی نسبت اہم ہے اس لئے اگر رکوع میں امام کے ساتھ ملنے کی امید ہو تو دعا قنوت بھی پڑھے اور رکوع میں مل جائے، اور امکان نہیں ہے تو دعا چھوڑ کر امام کے ساتھ مل جائے۔
And if the imam leaves the Qunut, the follower recites it if he can join the imam in the ruku; otherwise he follows him. Explanation: Following the imam is necessary, while the supplication is not that necessary. This hadith: From Aisha, Mother of the Believers, that she said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prayed in his house while he was ill, so he prayed sitting, and a group prayed behind him standing, so he gestured to them to sit. When he finished, he said: 'The imam is only appointed to be followed. So when he bows, bow; when he raises, raise; and when he says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah', say 'Rabbana lakal hamd'; and when he prays sitting, pray sitting.' (Bukhari, chapter: The imam is only appointed to be followed, p. 95, no. 688). In this hadith, the follower should completely follow the imam. Translation: (613) And if the imam leaves the Qunut, if there is a possibility of joining the imam in the ruku, the follower recites Qunut; otherwise he follows the imam. Explanation: It has passed earlier that following the imam is more important than the supplication. Therefore, if there is hope of joining the imam in ruku, he recites the Qunut supplication and joins in ruku; and if not possible, he leaves the supplication and joins the imam.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The ruling states that when the imam omits the Qunut in Witr prayer, the follower (muqtadi) should recite it himself only if he can still join the imam in the subsequent ruku. If he cannot join the ruku, he should omit the Qunut to follow the imam. The proof is the famous hadith of Aisha (RA) where the Prophet (PBUH) emphasized following the imam. The commentary explains that following the imam takes precedence over reciting personal supplications like Qunut. Thus, the decision hinges on whether the muqtadi can maintain congruence with the imam's actions.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): A specific supplication recited in Witr prayer, often after ruku.
المؤتم (al-mu'tam): The follower in congregational prayer.
مشاركة الامام في الركوع (musharakah al-imam fi al-ruku'): Joining the imam in the bowing posture before he rises.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the imam omits Qunut in Witr and the muqtadi fears missing the ruku if he recites it, what should he do?
A) Recite Qunut quickly and then join ruku
B) Omit Qunut and follow the imam into ruku
C) Recite Qunut after the prayer
D) Wait until the imam finishes and repeat the rak'ah

Key Takeaway
The follower recites Qunut only if it does not prevent timely joining of the imam's subsequent ruku; following the imam is paramount.

Catching the Imam in the Third Ruku of Witr
Ruling statement with principle-based expansion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muqtadi who joins the imam in the third ruku of Witr and explain the principle of catching the rak'ah through catching the ruku.

Core Idea
Joining the imam in the third ruku of Witr means you have caught the Qunut.

In the Hanafi school, Witr prayer includes Qunut in the third rak'ah. A common question is what happens if a latecomer joins the imam during that ruku. Does he need to recite Qunut later? The matn gives a clear ruling based on a key principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes a muqtadi who joins the imam in the ruku (bowing) of the third rak'ah of Witr. Note: he misses the beginning of the third rak'ah but catches the ruku.
2
Apply the Hanafi principle
Recall that in Hanafi fiqh, catching the ruku of a rak'ah means you have caught that rak'ah entirely for the purpose of recitation and rulings.
This is a general principle: idrak al-ruk' kal-idrak al-rak'.
3
Derive the ruling on Qunut
Since the third rak'ah includes Qunut, catching the ruku means the muqtadi has caught the Qunut. Therefore, the imam's Qunut suffices for him. When he later completes the missed rak'ahs (first and second), he does not need to recite Qunut again.
The matn says: 'so he does not recite it in what preceded him.'
4
Contrast with opposing view
The Shafi'i school holds that the muqtadi must recite Qunut in the missed rak'ahs because the imam's Qunut does not transfer. This highlights the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أدرك الإمام في ركوع الثالثة من الوتر كان مدركا للقنوت فلا يأتي به فيما سبق به تشریح: یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ رکوع مل گیا تو اس رکعت کی قرآت مل گئی، اسی طرح تیسری رکعت کے رکوع میں امام کے ساتھ ملا تو گویا کہ وہ رکعت مل گئی، اس لئے امام کی دعاء قنوت اس مقتدی کے لئے کافی ہو جائے گی۔ اب جب پہلی اور دوسری رکعت پڑھے گا تو اس میں دعاء قنوت پڑھنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہوگی۔ ترجمه: (۶۱۴) اور اگر وتر کی تیسری رکعت کے رکوع میں امام سے ملے تو گویا اس کو قنوت مل گیا، اب اس کو اپنی باقی رکعت میں نہ پڑھے۔
And if he catches the imam in the ruku of the third rak'ah of Witr, he has caught the Qunut, so he does not recite it in what preceded him. Explanation: This issue is based on the principle that if the ruku is caught, the recitation of that rak'ah is caught. Similarly, if he joins the imam in the ruku of the third rak'ah, it is as if he caught that rak'ah. Therefore, the imam's Qunut supplication will suffice for this follower. When he prays the first and second rak'ahs, he will not need to recite Qunut in them. Translation: (614) And if he joins the imam in the ruku of the third rak'ah of Witr, it is as if he caught the Qunut; so he should not recite it in his remaining rak'ahs.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This is a ruling statement explaining the consequence of joining the imam in the third rak'ah of Witr. The matn states that the follower has effectively caught the Qunut by joining in that ruku. The commentary expands using the Hanafi principle that catching the ruku means catching the entire rak'ah. Since the Qunut in Witr is recited in the third rak'ah, joining the imam in that ruku means the imam's Qunut counts for the follower. Therefore, when the follower completes the missed rak'ahs, he does not repeat the Qunut.

Key Terms
مدرك للقنوت (mudrik li al-qunut): Having caught the Qunut by joining the imam in the ruku of the third rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A muqtadi joins the imam in the ruku of the third rak'ah of Witr. According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting Qunut in the missed rak'ahs?
A) He must recite Qunut in all missed rak'ahs.
B) He should not recite Qunut because he caught it with the imam.
C) He may choose to recite it or not.
D) He should recite Qunut only in the first missed rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
In Witr, joining the imam in the third ruku means you have caught the Qunut and need not recite it later.

Witr in Congregation: Ramadan Only
States the Ramadan-only rule for congregational Witr and presents proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying Witr in congregation and explain why it is restricted to Ramadan.

Core Idea
Witr in congregation is a Ramadan-specific practice; outside it, individual prayer is preferred.

The Hanafi school permits and recommends praying Witr in congregation exclusively during Ramadan, following the practice of the early community. This lesson examines the ruling, the proofs, and the differences of opinion within and outside the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Praying Witr in congregation. What is the hukm? The passage states it is done 'only in Ramadan' and that congregational prayer is better than alone (in Ramadan).
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (highly recommended) for Ramadan.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are cited: a hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet prayed 20 rak'ahs and Witr in congregation in Ramadan, and the practice of Ubayy ibn Ka'b leading the people in Witr during Umar's caliphate.
These are ahad and zanni in transmission and indication.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows the Prophet's action, and the companion's practice demonstrates the early community's consensus during Ramadan. Both indicate that congregational Witr is established only in Ramadan.
The linguistic link is the explicit mention of Ramadan in the hadith and the context of the practice.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi difference: Qadi Khan holds congregation as better even in Ramadan, while others say alone at the end of the night is better. Cross-madhhab: Shafi'is do not allow congregational Witr at all.
The mufta bihi follows Qadi Khan's view.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The preferred view relies on Qadi Khan's choice and the established practice of the early Muslims. The hadith and companion practice support the Ramadan-specific concession.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And he prays Witr in congregation only in Ramadan, and his prayer with congregation (is better). Explanation: And only in Ramadan, he should pray Witr with congregation. And in Ramadan, praying Witr with congregation is better than praying it alone at the end of the night. Qadi Khan adopted this and declared it correct, while others declared the opposite as correct. Tashrih: In Ramadan, they pray Tarawih with congregation, and after it Witr is prayed, so Witr should also be prayed with congregation. On other days, Witr is prayed after the Sunnah, and praying at the end of the night is better, so Witr will not be prayed in congregation. And those who said that praying Witr alone is better, their proof is that even in Ramadan it is better to pray at the end of the night, so he should pray alone. (He said) that praying it in congregation in Ramadan is better than performing it alone at the end of the night, in the choice of Qadi Khan; he said it is correct, and others declared contrary. Proof: (1) From Ibn Abbas: the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray twenty rak'ahs and Witr in Ramadan. (Tabarani al-Kabir) In this hadith, he prayed Witr with congregation in Ramadan. (2) From al-Hasan: that Ubayy led the people in the caliphate of Umar; he prayed with them the first half of Ramadan without Qunut; when the half passed, he recited Qunut after ruku; when the last ten days entered, he kept it and left them? (unclear) and led them in the last ten days, Mu'adh al-Qari in the caliphate of Umar. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) This practice of a Tabi'i shows that Witr was prayed with congregation in Ramadan.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that in the Hanafi school, Witr prayer is prayed in congregation only during Ramadan. Outside Ramadan, it is prayed individually. The commentary discusses a difference of opinion: Qadi Khan holds that congregational Witr in Ramadan is superior to offering it alone at the end of the night, while others hold the opposite. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that it is better to pray Witr in congregation in Ramadan because of the practice of the early community. Two proofs are cited: the hadith of Ibn Abbas stating the Prophet (PBUH) prayed Witr with the Tarawih in congregation, and the practice of Ubayy ibn Ka'b leading the people in Witr during Ramadan in Umar's caliphate.

Key Terms
الوتر بجماعة (al-witr bi-jama'ah): Praying Witr in congregation, specifically allowed in Ramadan only.
قاضی خان (Qadi Khan): A later Hanafi jurist whose fatwa is cited in support of congregational Witr in Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Witr in congregation is a Ramadan-specific practice; outside it, the individual prayer at the end of the night is preferred.

Witr in Ramadan: Congregation Is Superior
Ruling on congregational Witr in Ramadan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing Witr in congregation during Ramadan and cite the two proofs from the hadith and the practice of the Companions.

Core Idea
Congregational Witr in Ramadan is superior to performing it alone, based on the practice of the Prophet and the early community.

The Witr prayer is a beloved night prayer in the Hanafi school, and during Ramadan its performance takes on special significance. The passage before us clarifies that praying Witr in congregation during Ramadan is better than praying it alone at the end of the night. This ruling is grounded in two clear proofs: a hadith of Ibn Abbas describing the Prophet's practice, and the practice of Ubayy ibn Ka'b leading the people during Umar's caliphate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Ikhtilaf
Read the first sentence: 'In Ramadan, it is better than performing it alone at the end of the night, according to the choice of Qadi Khan.' Recognize that the author affirms Qadi Khan's view that congregation is superior, while noting a difference of opinion.
Qadi Khan is a later Hanafi authority; his view is preferred here.
2
Examine the First Proof: Hadith of Ibn Abbas
Look at the hadith: The Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed twenty rak'ahs and Witr in Ramadan. The implication is that the twenty rak'ahs (taraweeh) were prayed in congregation, and Witr was prayed alongside them, thus also in congregation.
This hadith is the primary dalil naqli.
3
Examine the Second Proof: Practice of Ubayy ibn Ka'b
Read the report from al-Hasan: Ubayy led the people in Witr during Umar's caliphate, with qunut after ruku' in the second half of Ramadan. This shows that the Companions practiced congregational Witr in Ramadan.
This is an action of a Companion, considered strong evidence in Hanafi usul.
4
Understand the Superiority
The passage concludes that congregational Witr in Ramadan is better than individual performance at the end of the night. This is the mufta bihi (operative) position in the Hanafi school, especially during Ramadan when the community gathers for taraweeh.
The key is the specific time (Ramadan) and setting (congregation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الوتر
في رمضان افضل من ادائه منفردا آخر الليل في اختيار قاضی خان قال هو الصحيح وصحح غيره
خلافه .
وجه : (۱) عن ابن عباس قال كان النبي عل الله يصلي في شهر رمضان عشرين ركعة والوتر (طبراني الكبير، باب ،ص ب مقسم عن ابن عباس، ج حادی عشر ، ص ۱۳۱۱، نمبر ۱۲۱۰۲ سفن سیھتی ، باب ماروی فی عدد ركعات القيام في شهر رمضان ، ج ثانی ن ص ۶۹۸ نمبر ۴۶۱۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ رمضان میں وتر بھی جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھے۔ (۲) ـ عن الحسن ان ابيا ام
الـنـاس فـي خـلافـة عـمـر فصلى بهم النصف من رمضان لا يقنت فلما مضى النصف قنت بعد الركوع فلما دخل العشر ابقى و خلى عنهم فصلى بهم العشر معاذ القاري في خلافة عمر (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من قال القنوت في النصف من رمضان ، ج ثانی ، ص ۱۹، نمبر ۶۹۳۴ ) اس عمل تابعی میں ہے کہ رمضان میں وتر جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھی گئی۔
Chapter on Witr. In Ramadan, it is better than performing it alone at the end of the night, according to the choice of Qadi Khan. He said it is correct, and others corrected contrary to him. Proof: (1) From Ibn Abbas, he said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray twenty rak'ahs and Witr in the month of Ramadan. (Tabrani al-Kabir...) This hadith indicates that in Ramadan, Witr was also prayed in congregation. (2) From al-Hasan: That Ubayy led the people during the caliphate of Umar, so he prayed with them the first half of Ramadan without qunut. When half passed, he performed qunut after bowing. When the last ten days entered, he kept something and left them, so he prayed with them the last ten days, and Mu'adh al-Qari [led] during the caliphate of Umar. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba...) This action of the Tabi'i indicates that Witr was prayed in congregation in Ramadan.
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi tradition concerning the performance of Witr prayer in Ramadan. The author states that praying Witr in congregation during Ramadan is superior to performing it alone at the end of the night, and this is the correct view according to Qadi Khan, though others have disputed it. Two proofs are presented: first, a hadith from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed twenty rak'ahs plus Witr in Ramadan, implying congregation. Second, the practice of the Tabi'i al-Hasan al-Basri, who reported that Ubayy ibn Ka'b led the people in Witr during Umar's caliphate, with qunut starting from the middle of Ramadan. These evidences establish that the early community performed Witr in congregation in Ramadan, and the Hanafi school considers this practice commendable.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after the night prayers, typically 1, 3, 5, 7, or 9 rak'ahs.
جماعة (jama'ah): Praying in congregation, i.e., following an imam.
قنوت (qunut): A supplication recited during Witr prayer, often after bowing (ruku').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) A hadith from Ibn Abbas and the practice of Ubayy ibn Ka'b
C) Qiyas on the five daily prayers
D) The consensus of all scholars

Key Takeaway
Praying Witr in congregation during Ramadan is sunnah muakkadah and superior to individual performance, as proven by the Prophet's practice and that of the Companions.

Emphasized Sunnah Prayers (Sunnan Muakkadah)
Listing of twelve sunnah muakkadah with four hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the twelve rak'ahs of sunnah muakkadah and identify the hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
Twelve rak'ahs of sunnah muakkadah are consistently performed by the Prophet; they earn a house in Paradise.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text lists the emphasized voluntary prayers (sunan muakkadah) and provides hadith proofs. Understanding these sunnahs helps you complete your daily salah with the Prophet's practice. The matn gives a concise list, and the commentary expands on the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the twelve rak'ahs
From the matn, list the specific sunnah muakkadah prayers: 2 before Fajr, 4 before Zuhr, 2 after Zuhr, 2 after Maghrib, and 2 after Isha. Note that the Jumu'ah sunnahs (4 before and 4 after) are additional and not part of the twelve.
2
Examine the hadith proofs
Read the four hadith cited: the detailed practice from Aisha, the promise of a house in Paradise, the hadith of Umm Habiba, and the Jumu'ah hadith. Match each hadith to the specific rak'ahs it supports.
The hadith of Umm Habiba mentions four before and four after Zuhr, but the Hanafi position is four before and two after; the four after Zuhr may be considered mustahabb or sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
3
Understand the Hanafi ruling
Note that these prayers are sunnah muakkadah, meaning the Prophet never abandoned them. Abandoning without excuse is makruh tanzihi. They are not wajib, but highly recommended.
The Hanafi school distinguishes between sunnah muakkadah and other nawafil.
4
Apply to daily practice
For each of the five daily prayers, note which sunnah muakkadah are attached. For example, before Fajr: 2 rak'ahs; before Zuhr: 4; after Zuhr: 2; after Maghrib: 2; after Isha: 2.
Some sunnahs like the four before Asr are not sunnah muakkadah.

Section on Nawafil. (616) Sunnah muakkadah: two rak'ahs before Fajr, two rak'ahs after Zuhr, after Maghrib, and after Isha, and four before Zuhr and four before and after Jumu'ah with one salam, it is sunnah muakkadah. Explanation: These twelve rak'ahs are sunnah muakkadah; their emphasis is great. [1] Two rak'ahs before Fajr, [2] four rak'ahs before Zuhr, [3] two rak'ahs after Zuhr, [4] two rak'ahs after Maghrib, [5] two rak'ahs after Isha. Proof: (1) The evidence for twelve rak'ahs is this hadith: I asked Aisha about the voluntary prayer of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). She said: He used to pray in my house four before Zuhr, then go out and lead the people, then come in and pray two rak'ahs. And he would lead the people in Maghrib, then come in and pray two rak'ahs, and lead the people in Isha, and come into my house and pray two rak'ahs... And when dawn broke, he prayed two rak'ahs. (Muslim...) This hadith indicates that before and after the obligatory prayers throughout the day and night, there are sunnah muakkadah, and they are twelve rak'ahs. Their emphasis is established. (2) From Aisha, she said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever perseveres in twelve rak'ahs of sunnah, Allah will build for him a house in Paradise: four rak'ahs before Zuhr, two after it, two after Maghrib, two after Isha, and two before Fajr.' (Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, Muslim) This hadith states that whoever is constant upon twelve rak'ahs of sunnah, Allah will build a house in Paradise. (3) And the evidence for four before Zuhr is this hadith: Umm Habiba, the wife of the Prophet (peace be upon him), said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever preserves four rak'ahs before Zuhr and four after it, Allah will forbid him from the Fire.' (Abu Dawud) This hadith indicates that the sunnah of Zuhr is four before and four after. (4) And the evidence for four after Jumu'ah is this hadith: From Abu Hurairah, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When one of you prays Jumu'ah, let him pray four after it.' (Muslim) This hadith indicates that
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that defines the emphasized sunnah prayers (sunan muakkadah) according to the Hanafi school. The matn (616) lists the twelve rak'ahs as: 2 before Fajr, 4 before Zuhr, 2 after Zuhr, 2 after Maghrib, 2 after Isha, and also mentions 4 before and after Jumu'ah with one salam. The commentary explains that these are emphatic. The author then provides four hadith proofs. First, the detailed account of Aisha describing the Prophet's regular practice of these twelve rak'ahs. Second, a hadith promising a house in Paradise for consistency. Third, a hadith from Umm Habiba specifically about four before and after Zuhr, which also supports the four before Zuhr (though the matn states four before Zuhr and two after, the hadith mentions four after as well, but the Hanafi position is two after, as clarified elsewhere). Fourth, a hadith for four after Jumu'ah. The lesson establishes that these sunnahs are highly recommended and the Prophet (peace be upon him) never abandoned them.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah muakkadah): An emphasized supererogatory act that the Prophet consistently performed and rarely omitted.
نافلة (nafilah): Voluntary or supererogatory prayer, additional to the obligatory ones.

The twelve rak'ahs of sunnah muakkadah are: 2 before Fajr, 4 before Zuhr, 2 after Zuhr, 2 after Maghrib, 2 after Isha; maintaining them earns Paradise.

Mustahabb Prayers Before Asr, After Maghrib, and After Isha
List of mustahabb prayers with hadith proofs and flexible number for Asr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the mustahabb prayers listed, state the hadith proofs for each, and explain the flexibility in the number of rak'ahs before Asr.

Core Idea
Mustahabb prayers are recommended but not obligatory; their number can vary based on weaker evidence.

In this lesson, we explore the category of mustahabb prayers – those that are recommended but not as strongly emphasized as the sunnah mu'akkadah. The text lists specific voluntary prayers before and after the obligatory prayers and provides hadith evidence. Understanding the distinction between mustahabb and sunnah is crucial for proper fiqh classification. We will examine the proofs and note the intra-Hanafi difference on the number of rak'ahs before Asr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that certain prayers are mustahabb (recommended). Understand that mustahabb is lower in rank than sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
List the specific prayers
Four before Asr, four before Isha, four after Isha, and six after Maghrib. Note that the number before Asr is flexible (two or four).
3
Locate the dalil for each
For Asr, hadith of Ibn Umar (four) and Ali (two). For Isha after, hadith of Ibn Abbas (four) and Aisha (four or six). For Maghrib, the hadith is incomplete but referenced from Ibn Umar.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'رحم الله امرء' in the Ibn Umar hadith indicates recommendation (istihbab) rather than obligation. The variation in numbers (two vs four) shows flexibility.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafis consider four before Asr as sunnah, others two. The author allows both.

Translation: (617) And it is mustahabb: four before Asr, four before Isha and four after it, and six after Maghrib. Explanation: Four before Asr are mustahabb. Four before Isha are mustahabb; its proof is not found, but four after Maghrib can be used as evidence for it. And four after Isha, and six after Maghrib. Reasoning: (1) The proof for four before Asr being mustahabb is the hadith of Ibn Umar: May Allah have mercy on a person who prays four before Asr (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). From this hadith, it is learned that four before Asr are sunnah. But another hadith indicates two are sunnah. (2) In a hadith of Ali: The Prophet used to pray two before Asr (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). Based on this, the author says one can also pray two before Asr. (3) Four after Isha are sunnah; proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: I spent the night in my aunt Maimuna's house; the Messenger of Allah prayed Isha, then came and prayed four rak'ahs, then slept (Bukhari). This hadith shows four after Isha are sunnah. (4) From Aisha: I asked her about the prayer of the Messenger of Allah; she said: He never prayed Isha then came to me except that he prayed four or six rak'ahs (Abu Dawud). This hadith mentions four and six. (4) Four after Maghrib is proven by the hadith... and this same hadith can be used as proof for four before Isha. From Ibn Umar: I think he raised it (to the Prophet) ...
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage discusses the mustahabb (recommended) prayers, which are of lesser emphasis than the sunnah mu'akkadah. The author lists: four before Asr, four before Isha, four after Isha, and six after Maghrib. The Urdu commentary notes that while these are recommended, the evidence is weaker. For Asr, there is a hadith from Ibn Umar praising one who prays four before Asr, but also a hadith from Ali showing the Prophet prayed two. Thus, both are permissible, but the author leans toward four being mustahabb. For Isha, the hadith of Ibn Abbas shows four after Isha, and a hadith of Aisha mentions four or six. For Maghrib, the hadith is incomplete in the OCR. The commentary also suggests that the same hadith used for Maghrib can apply to before Isha, though no direct evidence is cited. Overall, these are optional but rewarding prayers, not as strongly emphasized as the sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): A recommended act that brings reward but is not emphasized; leaving it is not disliked.

Recommended Voluntary Prayers: Rak'ah Counts and Proofs
Rulings on voluntary rak'ah counts with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of rak'ahs recommended before and after Zuhr, Jumu'ah, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha, and cite the relevant proofs.

Core Idea
Four before Asr, four before Isha, four after Isha, six after Maghrib — each supported by hadith or companion practice.

The Hanafi school specifies distinct numbers of voluntary rak'ahs for each obligatory prayer. This lesson extracts the rulings and their proofs from the matn of Thamaratun Najah. You will learn not only what to pray but why these numbers are recommended, based on direct hadith and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer times
List the five obligatory prayers and note which have voluntary rak'ahs before and/or after according to this passage.
Zuhr and Jumu'ah have both before and after; Asr before only; Maghrib after only; Isha before and after.
2
State the rak'ah counts
For each voluntary time, note the exact number of rak'ahs: e.g., before Zuhr and Jumu'ah: four with one taslim; after Jumu'ah: four; before Asr: four (mustahabb); before Isha: four; after Isha: four; after Maghrib: six.
The text mentions different categories: sunnah mu'akkadah for some, mustahabb for others.
3
Classify the ruling level
Determine whether each voluntary prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah, mustahabb, or just recommended. The passage uses terms like 'sunnah' and 'mustahabb'.
Before Zuhr and Jumu'ah are sunnah mu'akkadah; before Asr and Isha are mustahabb; after Isha is sunnah; after Maghrib is mustahabb (or sunnah? Text mentions both).
4
Examine the proofs
For each count, identify the hadith or athar cited. The text provides explicit references for most, e.g., hadith of Ibn Umar for four before Asr, hadith of Ibn Abbas for four after Isha, etc.
Some proofs are stronger than others; the author notes where no direct proof was found.

ترجمه : (۶۱۷) اور مستحب ہے عصر سے پہلے چار رکعت اور عشا سے پہلے چار رکعت اور اس کے بعد چار رکعت ، اور مغرب کے
بعد چھ رکعت ۔ تشریح : عصر سے پہلے چار رکعتیں مستحب ہیں۔ اور عشاء سے پہلے چار رکعتیں مستحب ہیں ، اس کی دلیل نہیں مل رہی ہے، البتہ مغرب کے بعد جو چار رکعتیں ہیں اس کو عشاء سے پہلے کی دلیل بنا سکتے ہیں۔ اور عشاء کے بعد چار رکعتیں ہیں، اور مغرب کے بعد چھ
رکعتیں ہیں۔ وجه : (۱) عصر سے پہلے چار رکعتیں رکعت مستحب ہیں اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔عــن ابـن عــمــر قال قال رسول الله لا الله ورحم الله امرء صلى قبل العصر اربعا (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الصلوة قبل العصر ص ۱۸۷، نمبر ۱۲۷ ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الا ربع قبل العصر ص ۹۸ نمبر ۴۳۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عصر سے پہلے چار رکعتیں سنت ہیں ۔ لیکن دوسری حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ دور کعتیں سنت ہیں۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن علي ان النبي الله كان يصلى قبل العصر رکعتین ۔ (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الصلوة قبل العصرص ۱۸۷ نمبر ۱۲۷۲ رترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الا ربع قبل العصرص ۹۸ نمبر ۴۲۹) اس حدیث کی بنا پر صاحب کتاب نے فرمایا کہ عصر کی سنت دو رکعت بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے۔(۳) عشاء کے بعد چار رکعتیں سنت ہیں اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال بت في بيت خالتي ميمونة فصلى رسول الله الله العشاء ثم جاء فصلی اربع رکعات ثم نام ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب يقوم عن یمین الامام بحذاه سواء اذا کانا اثنین، ص۱۱۴،نمبر ۶۹۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عشاء کے بعد چار رکعتیں سنت ہیں۔ (۴) عن عائشة قال سألتها عن صلوة رسول الله الله فقالت ما صلى رسول الله العشاء قط فدخل على الاصلى اربع رکعات او ست رکعات (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الصلوۃ بعد العشاء ص۱۹۲ نمبر ۱۳۰۳) اس حدیث میں چار رکعت ، اور چھ رکعت کا بھی ذکر ہے۔ (۴) مغرب کے بعد چار رکعت ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔۔ اور یہی حدیث عشاء سے پہلے چار رکعت کی دلیل بن سکتی ہے۔ عن ابن عمر ـ لا اعلمه الا رفعه

المغرب (۶۱۸) ويقتصر فى الجلوس الاول من الرباعيّة المؤكدة على التشهد ولا يأتي في الثالثة بدعاء الاستفتاح بـخـلاف المندوبة (٦١٩) واذا صلى نافلة اكثر من ركعتين ولم يجلس الا في آخرها صح استحسانا لانها صارت صلوة واحدة وفيها الفرض الجلوس آخرها
قال من ركع بعد المغرب اربع ركعات كان كالمعقب [ غزوة بعد غزوة - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الصلاة فيما بین المغرب والعشاء ، ج ثانی ،ص ۴۱۵، نمبر ۴۷۴۰) اس حدیث میں چار رکعتوں کا تذکرہ ہے ، (۵) اور دوسری حدیث میں دو رکعتوں کا تذکرہ ہے اس لئے ملا کر چھ رکعتیں ہو گئیں ۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ سألت عائشـة عـن صلوة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن
صلى الله
تطوعه؟.... وكان يصلي بالناس المغرب ثم يدخل فيصلى ركعتين . (مسلم شریف، باب جواز النافلة قائما وقاعدا ،ص۲۵۲، نمبر ۶۹۹/۷۳۰ ا ر ابوداؤد شریف ، ابواب التطوع وركعات السنتہ ،ص ۱۸۵، نمبر ۱۲۵۱)
ترجمه : ( ۶۱۸) اور سنت مؤکدہ کی چار رکعت کے پہلے قعدہ میں صرف تشہد پر اقتصار (اکتفا) کرے، اور تیسری رکعت میں ثانہ پڑھے۔ بخلاف مستحبات کے۔
تشریح : چار رکعت سنت مؤکدہ کی دو حیثیتیں ہیں [1] ایک یہ کہ چاروں رکعتیں گویا کہ مجموعہ ہیں اس لئے دورکعتوں کے بعد سلام نہ پھیرے، پہلی دو رکعتوں کے بعد قعدہ اولی میں صرف تشہد پڑھے، دعا اور درود شریف نہ پڑھے ، اور سلام نہ پھیرے، اور چونکہ تیسری رکعت بھی پہلے کا ہی حصہ ہے اس لئے تیسری رکعت میں ثانہ پڑھے ۔ [۲] اور دوسری حیثیت نوافل کی ہے، اس لئے اگر سلام پھیر دیا تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ اس کے بخلاف چار رکعت مستحبات کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ قعدہ اولی میں تشہد کے بعد درود شریف بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے اور دعاء بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے اور تیسری رکعت میں شنا بھی پڑھے، کیو کہ اس کا ہر شفع الگ الگ نماز ہے۔
وجه : (۱) چار سنتیں ایک ساتھ پڑھے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال : كان النبي الله يركع قبل الجمعة أربعا ، لا يفصل في شيء منهن . (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الصلوۃ قبل الجمعة، ص ۱۵۸، نمبر ۱۱۲۹) اس حدیث میں لا يفصل في شيء منهن ، سے معلوم ہوا کہ درمیان میں سلام نہ پھیرے۔(۲) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ چار رکعتیں ایک ساتھ پڑھے۔ (۲) عن ابي هريرة قال : قال رسول الله الله ) ( اذا صلى أحدكم الجمعة فليصل بعدها أربعا . (مسلم شريف باب الصلوة بعد الجمعة، ص۳۵۲، نمبر ۲۰۳۶/۸۸ ابن ماجہ شریف، باب ماجاء فی الصلوۃ بعد الجمعة ، ص ۱۵۸، نمبر ۱۱۳۲) ان حدیثوں میں ہے کہ جمعہ سے پہلے ایک سلام کے ساتھ چار رکعت پڑھے۔
ترجمه : (۲۱۹) اگر نفل دورکعتوں سے زیادہ پڑھے اور اخیر میں بیٹھے تو استحسانا جائز ہے، اس لئے کہ وہ ایک نماز کی طرح ہوگئی ، اور اس میں اخیر میں بیٹھنا فرض ہے۔
Chapter on Voluntary Prayers. Before Zuhr and before Jumu'ah and after it with one taslim. (217) And it is recommended four before Asr and Isha and after it, and six after Maghrib ... after that pray four rak'ahs sunnah. (5) And before Jumu'ah pray four rak'ahs, its proof is the practice of the Companion: 'Indeed Ibn Mas'ud used to pray before Jumu'ah four rak'ahs, and after it four rak'ahs.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Salah Qabl al-Jumu'ah wa Ba'daha, vol. 3, p. 130, no. 5541) In this athar, that he prayed four rak'ahs before Jumu'ah. (6) In this hadith there is proof of two rak'ahs before Jumu'ah: from Abu Hurairah... Translation: (617) And it is recommended four before Asr, and four before Isha, and four after it, and six after Maghrib. Explanation: Four before Asr are mustahabb, and four before Isha are mustahabb; I haven't found a proof for this, except that the four after Maghrib can be used as proof for before Isha. And four after Isha, and six after Maghrib. Reasoning: (1) The proof for four before Asr being mustahabb is this hadith: from Ibn Umar... (2) In another hadith: from Ali that the Prophet used to pray two rak'ahs before Asr. (3) The proof for four after Isha being sunnah is the hadith of Ibn Abbas... (4) From Aisha: four or six after Isha. (4) The proof for four after Maghrib is this hadith: from Ibn Umar... On page 424: Maghrib (618) And one restricts in the first sitting of the four-rak'ah mu'akkadah to tashahhud, and does not recite the istiftah prayer in the third, contrary to the mandubah. (619) And if one prays a voluntary prayer of more than two rak'ahs and does not sit except at the end, it is valid istihsanan, because it becomes a single prayer, and in it the obligatory sitting is at its end. ... Translation: (618) And for the mu'akkadah sunnah of four rak'ahs, in the first sitting one restricts to only tashahhud, and does not recite thana in the third, contrary to mustahabbat. Explanation: The four-rak'ah mu'akkadah sunnah has two aspects: (1) the four rak'ahs are like a composite, so do not say salam after two, after the first sitting recite only tashahhud, do not recite dua and durood, and do not say salam; and since the third rak'ah is part of the first, recite thana in the third. (2) The second aspect is like nawafil, so if one says salam there is no harm. In contrast, for four mustahabbat, one may recite durood and dua after tashahhud in the first sitting, and recite thana in the third, because each pair is a separate prayer. Reasoning: (1) The proof for praying four sunnats together is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: the Prophet used to pray four before Jumu'ah without separating between them. (2) Also from Abu Hurairah: 'When one of you prays Jumu'ah, let him pray four after it.' These hadiths show that one prays four before Jumu'ah with one salam. Translation: (219) If one prays a nafl of more than two rak'ahs and sits only at the end, it is valid istihsanan, because it becomes a single prayer, and in it the obligatory sitting is at the end.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is a section from the chapter on voluntary prayers (nawafil) in a Hanafi fiqh work, combining matn and commentary. It covers three main rulings: first, the recommended number of rak'ahs before and after certain prayers; second, the manner of sitting in the four-rak'ah mu'akkadah sunnah; and third, the validity of praying a nafl of more than two rak'ahs with only one sitting at the end. The author begins by stating that before Zuhr and before Jumu'ah and after Jumu'ah one prays with one taslim (i.e., without separating into two rak'ahs). Then he mentions that four rak'ahs are recommended before Asr, before Isha, and after Isha, and six after Maghrib. He provides hadith evidence for each. Notably, for the four before Asr, he cites two hadiths: one recommending four, and another from Ali that the Prophet prayed two, so either is permissible. For the four before Isha, he admits he did not find a direct proof but analogizes from the four after Maghrib. On page 424, the text moves to the first sitting in the four-rak'ah mu'akkadah sunnah: one restricts to only tashahhud and does not recite the opening supplication (istiftah) in the third rak'ah, unlike the mandubah where one may recite more. The reasoning is that the four rak'ahs are considered a single unit for mu'akkadah, so the first sitting is minimal, while mandubah are treated as separate pairs. Finally, the ruling on a nafl of more than two rak'ahs: if one sits only at the end, it is valid by istihsan (juristic preference) because it becomes one prayer, and the obligatory sitting is at the end. The author supports this by analogy and hadith. Throughout, the text uses the Hanafi methodology: citing hadith, applying qiyas, and using istihsan where appropriate.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Voluntary prayer, any supererogatory act of worship beyond the obligatory.
سنت مؤکدہ (sunnah mu'akkadah): Emphasized sunnah; a prayer that the Prophet consistently performed and recommended, and is considered close to wajib.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended, but not emphasized; includes mandubah prayers.
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited in the sitting position of prayer, including 'at-tahiyyat lillah...'
استفتاح (istiftah): The opening supplication recited after takbirat al-ihram, e.g., 'Subhanaka Allahumma...'
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, a method of reasoning that departs from strict analogy in favor of a more equitable or practical ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in the lesson, what is the ruling on praying four rak'ahs before Asr?
A) It is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah).
B) It is mustahabb (recommended).
C) It is wajib (obligatory).
D) It is not recommended at all.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes specific numbers of voluntary rak'ahs before and after obligatory prayers, with four before Zuhr and Jumu'ah as sunnah mu'akkadah, and mustahabb counts for Asr, Maghrib, and Isha, each supported by hadith or companion practice.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Sitting in Four-Rak'ah Mu'akkadah Sunnah: Tashahhud Only
Ruling on the first sitting and third rak'ah in four-rak'ah mu'akkadah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the sitting posture in four-rak'ah mu'akkadah sunnah from that of mustahabb prayers, and state the correct recitation in the first sitting and third rak'ah.

Core Idea
In four-rak'ah mu'akkadah, first sitting has only tashahhud; do not recite istiftah in the third rak'ah.

The Hanafi school differentiates between the performance of emphasized sunnah (mu'akkadah) and recommended (mustahabb) prayers. This lesson focuses on the specific rule for the four-rak'ah mu'akkadah sunnah: the first sitting is restricted to tashahhud, and the opening supplication (istiftah) is not recited in the third rak'ah. This is contrary to the mandubah, where each pair is independent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer type
Recognize that the ruling applies to four-rak'ah sunnah mu'akkadah, such as the sunnah before Zuhr and before/after Jumu'ah.
These are distinct from four-rak'ah mustahabb prayers like before Asr or after Isha.
2
Observe the first sitting
In the first sitting (after the second rak'ah), recite only tashahhud. Do not add durood, dua, or salam.
The text says 'ويقتصر على التشهد' meaning restricts to tashahhud.
3
Observe the third rak'ah
Do not recite the istiftah (opening supplication) in the third rak'ah. The text says 'ولا يأتي في الثالثة بدعاء الاستفتاح'.
Istiftah is normally recited in the first rak'ah of a prayer; for mu'akkadah, it is not repeated in the third.
4
Contrast with mandubah
In four-rak'ah mustahabb (mandubah), each pair is a separate prayer. Hence, in the first sitting one may recite durood and dua after tashahhud, and one may also recite istiftah in the third rak'ah.
The text says 'بخلاف المندوبة' meaning contrary to mandubah.
5
Understand the rationale
The mu'akkadah four rak'ahs are considered a single prayer unit, so the first sitting is a qa'dah between the two pairs, and the third rak'ah is a continuation. Hence, minimal recitation is sufficient. Mustahabb prayers are two separate prayer units, so each pair has its own identity.
The commentary explains that the mu'akkadah has two aspects: one as a composite, the other as nawafil.

ترجمه : (۶۱۷) اور مستحب ہے عصر سے پہلے چار رکعت اور عشا سے پہلے چار رکعت اور اس کے بعد چار رکعت ، اور مغرب کے

رکعتیں ہیں۔ وجه : (۱) عصر سے پہلے چار رکعتیں رکعت مستحب ہیں اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔عــن ابـن عــمــر قال قال رسول الله لا الله ورحم الله امرء صلى قبل العصر اربعا (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الصلوة قبل العصر ص ۱۸۷، نمبر ۱۲۷ ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الا ربع قبل العصر ص ۹۸ نمبر ۴۳۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عصر سے پہلے چار رکعتیں سنت ہیں ۔ لیکن دوسری حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ دور کعتیں سنت ہیں۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن علي ان النبي الله كان يصلى قبل العصر رکعتین ۔ (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الصلوة قبل العصرص ۱۸۷ نمبر ۱۲۷۲ رترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الا ربع قبل العصرص ۹۸ نمبر ۴۲۹) اس حدیث کی بنا پر صاحب کتاب نے فرمایا کہ عصر کی سنت دو رکعت بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے۔(۳) عشاء کے بعد چار رکعتیں سنت ہیں اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال بت في بيت خالتي ميمونة فصلى رسول الله الله العشاء ثم جاء فصلی اربع رکعات ثم نام ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب يقوم عن یمین الامام بحذاه سواء اذا کانا اثنین، ص۱۱۴،نمبر ۶۹۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عشاء کے بعد چار رکعتیں سنت ہیں۔ (۴) عن عائشة قال سألتها عن صلوة رسول الله الله فقالت ما صلى رسول الله العشاء قط فدخل على الاصلى اربع رکعات او ست رکعات (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الصلوۃ بعد العشاء ص۱۹۲ نمبر ۱۳۰۳) اس حدیث میں چار رکعت ، اور چھ رکعت کا بھی ذکر ہے۔ (۴) مغرب کے بعد چار رکعت ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔۔ اور یہی حدیث عشاء سے پہلے چار رکعت کی دلیل بن سکتی ہے۔ عن ابن عمر ـ لا اعلمه الا رفعه

المغرب (۶۱۸) ويقتصر فى الجلوس الاول من الرباعيّة المؤكدة على التشهد ولا يأتي في الثالثة بدعاء الاستفتاح بـخـلاف المندوبة (٦١٩) واذا صلى نافلة اكثر من ركعتين ولم يجلس الا في آخرها صح استحسانا لانها صارت صلوة واحدة وفيها الفرض الجلوس آخرها
قال من ركع بعد المغرب اربع ركعات كان كالمعقب [ غزوة بعد غزوة - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الصلاة فيما بین المغرب والعشاء ، ج ثانی ،ص ۴۱۵، نمبر ۴۷۴۰) اس حدیث میں چار رکعتوں کا تذکرہ ہے ، (۵) اور دوسری حدیث میں دو رکعتوں کا تذکرہ ہے اس لئے ملا کر چھ رکعتیں ہو گئیں ۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ سألت عائشـة عـن صلوة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن
صلى الله
تطوعه؟.... وكان يصلي بالناس المغرب ثم يدخل فيصلى ركعتين . (مسلم شریف، باب جواز النافلة قائما وقاعدا ،ص۲۵۲، نمبر ۶۹۹/۷۳۰ ا ر ابوداؤد شریف ، ابواب التطوع وركعات السنتہ ،ص ۱۸۵، نمبر ۱۲۵۱)
ترجمه : ( ۶۱۸) اور سنت مؤکدہ کی چار رکعت کے پہلے قعدہ میں صرف تشہد پر اقتصار (اکتفا) کرے، اور تیسری رکعت میں ثانہ پڑھے۔ بخلاف مستحبات کے۔
تشریح : چار رکعت سنت مؤکدہ کی دو حیثیتیں ہیں [1] ایک یہ کہ چاروں رکعتیں گویا کہ مجموعہ ہیں اس لئے دورکعتوں کے بعد سلام نہ پھیرے، پہلی دو رکعتوں کے بعد قعدہ اولی میں صرف تشہد پڑھے، دعا اور درود شریف نہ پڑھے ، اور سلام نہ پھیرے، اور چونکہ تیسری رکعت بھی پہلے کا ہی حصہ ہے اس لئے تیسری رکعت میں ثانہ پڑھے ۔ [۲] اور دوسری حیثیت نوافل کی ہے، اس لئے اگر سلام پھیر دیا تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ اس کے بخلاف چار رکعت مستحبات کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ قعدہ اولی میں تشہد کے بعد درود شریف بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے اور دعاء بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے اور تیسری رکعت میں شنا بھی پڑھے، کیو کہ اس کا ہر شفع الگ الگ نماز ہے۔
وجه : (۱) چار سنتیں ایک ساتھ پڑھے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال : كان النبي الله يركع قبل الجمعة أربعا ، لا يفصل في شيء منهن . (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الصلوۃ قبل الجمعة، ص ۱۵۸، نمبر ۱۱۲۹) اس حدیث میں لا يفصل في شيء منهن ، سے معلوم ہوا کہ درمیان میں سلام نہ پھیرے۔(۲) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ چار رکعتیں ایک ساتھ پڑھے۔ (۲) عن ابي هريرة قال : قال رسول الله الله ) ( اذا صلى أحدكم الجمعة فليصل بعدها أربعا . (مسلم شريف باب الصلوة بعد الجمعة، ص۳۵۲، نمبر ۲۰۳۶/۸۸ ابن ماجہ شریف، باب ماجاء فی الصلوۃ بعد الجمعة ، ص ۱۵۸، نمبر ۱۱۳۲) ان حدیثوں میں ہے کہ جمعہ سے پہلے ایک سلام کے ساتھ چار رکعت پڑھے۔
ترجمه : (۲۱۹) اگر نفل دورکعتوں سے زیادہ پڑھے اور اخیر میں بیٹھے تو استحسانا جائز ہے، اس لئے کہ وہ ایک نماز کی طرح ہوگئی ، اور اس میں اخیر میں بیٹھنا فرض ہے۔
Chapter on Voluntary Prayers. Before Zuhr and before Jumu'ah and after it with one taslim. (217) And it is recommended four before Asr and Isha and after it, and six after Maghrib ... after that pray four rak'ahs sunnah. (5) And before Jumu'ah pray four rak'ahs, its proof is the practice of the Companion: 'Indeed Ibn Mas'ud used to pray before Jumu'ah four rak'ahs, and after it four rak'ahs.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Salah Qabl al-Jumu'ah wa Ba'daha, vol. 3, p. 130, no. 5541) In this athar, that he prayed four rak'ahs before Jumu'ah. (6) In this hadith there is proof of two rak'ahs before Jumu'ah: from Abu Hurairah... Translation: (617) And it is recommended four before Asr, and four before Isha, and four after it, and six after Maghrib. Explanation: Four before Asr are mustahabb, and four before Isha are mustahabb; I haven't found a proof for this, except that the four after Maghrib can be used as proof for before Isha. And four after Isha, and six after Maghrib. Reasoning: (1) The proof for four before Asr being mustahabb is this hadith: from Ibn Umar... (2) In another hadith: from Ali that the Prophet used to pray two rak'ahs before Asr. (3) The proof for four after Isha being sunnah is the hadith of Ibn Abbas... (4) From Aisha: four or six after Isha. (4) The proof for four after Maghrib is this hadith: from Ibn Umar... On page 424: Maghrib (618) And one restricts in the first sitting of the four-rak'ah mu'akkadah to tashahhud, and does not recite the istiftah prayer in the third, contrary to the mandubah. (619) And if one prays a voluntary prayer of more than two rak'ahs and does not sit except at the end, it is valid istihsanan, because it becomes a single prayer, and in it the obligatory sitting is at its end. ... Translation: (618) And for the mu'akkadah sunnah of four rak'ahs, in the first sitting one restricts to only tashahhud, and does not recite thana in the third, contrary to mustahabbat. Explanation: The four-rak'ah mu'akkadah sunnah has two aspects: (1) the four rak'ahs are like a composite, so do not say salam after two, after the first sitting recite only tashahhud, do not recite dua and durood, and do not say salam; and since the third rak'ah is part of the first, recite thana in the third. (2) The second aspect is like nawafil, so if one says salam there is no harm. In contrast, for four mustahabbat, one may recite durood and dua after tashahhud in the first sitting, and recite thana in the third, because each pair is a separate prayer. Reasoning: (1) The proof for praying four sunnats together is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: the Prophet used to pray four before Jumu'ah without separating between them. (2) Also from Abu Hurairah: 'When one of you prays Jumu'ah, let him pray four after it.' These hadiths show that one prays four before Jumu'ah with one salam. Translation: (219) If one prays a nafl of more than two rak'ahs and sits only at the end, it is valid istihsanan, because it becomes a single prayer, and in it the obligatory sitting is at the end.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is a section from the chapter on voluntary prayers (nawafil) in a Hanafi fiqh work, combining matn and commentary. It covers three main rulings: first, the recommended number of rak'ahs before and after certain prayers; second, the manner of sitting in the four-rak'ah mu'akkadah sunnah; and third, the validity of praying a nafl of more than two rak'ahs with only one sitting at the end. The author begins by stating that before Zuhr and before Jumu'ah and after Jumu'ah one prays with one taslim (i.e., without separating into two rak'ahs). Then he mentions that four rak'ahs are recommended before Asr, before Isha, and after Isha, and six after Maghrib. He provides hadith evidence for each. Notably, for the four before Asr, he cites two hadiths: one recommending four, and another from Ali that the Prophet prayed two, so either is permissible. For the four before Isha, he admits he did not find a direct proof but analogizes from the four after Maghrib. On page 424, the text moves to the first sitting in the four-rak'ah mu'akkadah sunnah: one restricts to only tashahhud and does not recite the opening supplication (istiftah) in the third rak'ah, unlike the mandubah where one may recite more. The reasoning is that the four rak'ahs are considered a single unit for mu'akkadah, so the first sitting is minimal, while mandubah are treated as separate pairs. Finally, the ruling on a nafl of more than two rak'ahs: if one sits only at the end, it is valid by istihsan (juristic preference) because it becomes one prayer, and the obligatory sitting is at the end. The author supports this by analogy and hadith. Throughout, the text uses the Hanafi methodology: citing hadith, applying qiyas, and using istihsan where appropriate.

Key Terms
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited in the sitting position of prayer.
استفتاح (istiftah): The opening supplication recited after takbirat al-ihram.
سنت مؤکدہ (sunnah mu'akkadah): Emphasized sunnah; a prayer that the Prophet consistently performed and recommended.
مندوبة (mandubah): Recommended but not emphasized voluntary prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the lesson, what should you recite in the first sitting of a four-rak'ah sunnah mu'akkadah prayer?
A) Tashahhud, durood, and a dua.
B) Only tashahhud.
C) Tashahhud and istiftah.
D) Subhanaka and tashahhud.

Key Takeaway
In four-rak'ah mu'akkadah sunnah, the first sitting contains only tashahhud and the third rak'ah does not include the opening supplication, reflecting the unity of the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Validity of Nafl with More Than Two Rak'ahs and Single Final Sitting
Ruling on nafl with more than two rak'ahs and single final sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying a voluntary prayer of more than two rak'ahs with only one sitting at the end, and explain why it is valid by istihsan.

Core Idea
A nafl of more than two rak'ahs is valid if you sit only at the end, because it becomes one prayer and the obligatory sitting is at the end.

Normally, a voluntary prayer is performed in units of two rak'ahs. However, the Hanafi school, by juristic preference (istihsan), allows a nafl of more than two rak'ahs (e.g., four) to be performed as a single unit with only one final sitting. This lesson explains the reasoning and the proof from hadith.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Voluntary prayers (nafl) are typically prayed in pairs of two rak'ahs, with a sitting (tashahhud) after each pair.
This is the default based on the hadith: 'صلاة الليل مثنى مثنى' (night prayer is two by two).
2
Identify the exceptional case
The ruling being discussed is when someone prays a nafl of more than two rak'ahs (e.g., four) but does not sit after the second rak'ah; instead, they sit only at the end.
This is considered a departure from the norm.
3
Apply istihsan
By strict analogy (qiyas), this might be invalid because it deviates from the standard two-rak'ah structure. However, by istihsan (juristic preference), it is valid because the entire set of rak'ahs is considered a single prayer, and the obligatory sitting is at the end.
Istihsan is used to mitigate the harshness of qiyas.
4
Support from hadith
The text cites a hadith about praying four after Maghrib without specifying a sitting in between, implying that four rak'ahs can be a single unit.
The hadith of Aisha also mentions the Prophet praying four or six after Isha without mention of a middle sitting.
5
Conclude the ruling
Thus, the Hanafi ruling is that such a prayer is valid (sahih) by istihsan, and the final sitting is the obligatory (fard) sitting.
This applies to nafl generally, not just mu'akkadah.

المغرب (۶۱۸) ويقتصر فى الجلوس الاول من الرباعيّة المؤكدة على التشهد ولا يأتي في الثالثة بدعاء الاستفتاح بـخـلاف المندوبة (٦١٩) واذا صلى نافلة اكثر من ركعتين ولم يجلس الا في آخرها صح استحسانا لانها صارت صلوة واحدة وفيها الفرض الجلوس آخرها
قال من ركع بعد المغرب اربع ركعات كان كالمعقب [ غزوة بعد غزوة - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الصلاة فيما بین المغرب والعشاء ، ج ثانی ،ص ۴۱۵، نمبر ۴۷۴۰) اس حدیث میں چار رکعتوں کا تذکرہ ہے ، (۵) اور دوسری حدیث میں دو رکعتوں کا تذکرہ ہے اس لئے ملا کر چھ رکعتیں ہو گئیں ۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ سألت عائشـة عـن صلوة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن
صلى الله
تطوعه؟.... وكان يصلي بالناس المغرب ثم يدخل فيصلى ركعتين . (مسلم شریف، باب جواز النافلة قائما وقاعدا ،ص۲۵۲، نمبر ۶۹۹/۷۳۰ ا ر ابوداؤد شریف ، ابواب التطوع وركعات السنتہ ،ص ۱۸۵، نمبر ۱۲۵۱)
ترجمه : ( ۶۱۸) اور سنت مؤکدہ کی چار رکعت کے پہلے قعدہ میں صرف تشہد پر اقتصار (اکتفا) کرے، اور تیسری رکعت میں ثانہ پڑھے۔ بخلاف مستحبات کے۔
تشریح : چار رکعت سنت مؤکدہ کی دو حیثیتیں ہیں [1] ایک یہ کہ چاروں رکعتیں گویا کہ مجموعہ ہیں اس لئے دورکعتوں کے بعد سلام نہ پھیرے، پہلی دو رکعتوں کے بعد قعدہ اولی میں صرف تشہد پڑھے، دعا اور درود شریف نہ پڑھے ، اور سلام نہ پھیرے، اور چونکہ تیسری رکعت بھی پہلے کا ہی حصہ ہے اس لئے تیسری رکعت میں ثانہ پڑھے ۔ [۲] اور دوسری حیثیت نوافل کی ہے، اس لئے اگر سلام پھیر دیا تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ اس کے بخلاف چار رکعت مستحبات کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ قعدہ اولی میں تشہد کے بعد درود شریف بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے اور دعاء بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے اور تیسری رکعت میں شنا بھی پڑھے، کیو کہ اس کا ہر شفع الگ الگ نماز ہے۔
وجه : (۱) چار سنتیں ایک ساتھ پڑھے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال : كان النبي الله يركع قبل الجمعة أربعا ، لا يفصل في شيء منهن . (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الصلوۃ قبل الجمعة، ص ۱۵۸، نمبر ۱۱۲۹) اس حدیث میں لا يفصل في شيء منهن ، سے معلوم ہوا کہ درمیان میں سلام نہ پھیرے۔(۲) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ چار رکعتیں ایک ساتھ پڑھے۔ (۲) عن ابي هريرة قال : قال رسول الله الله ) ( اذا صلى أحدكم الجمعة فليصل بعدها أربعا . (مسلم شريف باب الصلوة بعد الجمعة، ص۳۵۲، نمبر ۲۰۳۶/۸۸ ابن ماجہ شریف، باب ماجاء فی الصلوۃ بعد الجمعة ، ص ۱۵۸، نمبر ۱۱۳۲) ان حدیثوں میں ہے کہ جمعہ سے پہلے ایک سلام کے ساتھ چار رکعت پڑھے۔
ترجمه : (۲۱۹) اگر نفل دورکعتوں سے زیادہ پڑھے اور اخیر میں بیٹھے تو استحسانا جائز ہے، اس لئے کہ وہ ایک نماز کی طرح ہوگئی ، اور اس میں اخیر میں بیٹھنا فرض ہے۔
Chapter on Voluntary Prayers. Before Zuhr and before Jumu'ah and after it with one taslim. (217) And it is recommended four before Asr and Isha and after it, and six after Maghrib ... after that pray four rak'ahs sunnah. (5) And before Jumu'ah pray four rak'ahs, its proof is the practice of the Companion: 'Indeed Ibn Mas'ud used to pray before Jumu'ah four rak'ahs, and after it four rak'ahs.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Salah Qabl al-Jumu'ah wa Ba'daha, vol. 3, p. 130, no. 5541) In this athar, that he prayed four rak'ahs before Jumu'ah. (6) In this hadith there is proof of two rak'ahs before Jumu'ah: from Abu Hurairah... Translation: (617) And it is recommended four before Asr, and four before Isha, and four after it, and six after Maghrib. Explanation: Four before Asr are mustahabb, and four before Isha are mustahabb; I haven't found a proof for this, except that the four after Maghrib can be used as proof for before Isha. And four after Isha, and six after Maghrib. Reasoning: (1) The proof for four before Asr being mustahabb is this hadith: from Ibn Umar... (2) In another hadith: from Ali that the Prophet used to pray two rak'ahs before Asr. (3) The proof for four after Isha being sunnah is the hadith of Ibn Abbas... (4) From Aisha: four or six after Isha. (4) The proof for four after Maghrib is this hadith: from Ibn Umar... On page 424: Maghrib (618) And one restricts in the first sitting of the four-rak'ah mu'akkadah to tashahhud, and does not recite the istiftah prayer in the third, contrary to the mandubah. (619) And if one prays a voluntary prayer of more than two rak'ahs and does not sit except at the end, it is valid istihsanan, because it becomes a single prayer, and in it the obligatory sitting is at its end. ... Translation: (618) And for the mu'akkadah sunnah of four rak'ahs, in the first sitting one restricts to only tashahhud, and does not recite thana in the third, contrary to mustahabbat. Explanation: The four-rak'ah mu'akkadah sunnah has two aspects: (1) the four rak'ahs are like a composite, so do not say salam after two, after the first sitting recite only tashahhud, do not recite dua and durood, and do not say salam; and since the third rak'ah is part of the first, recite thana in the third. (2) The second aspect is like nawafil, so if one says salam there is no harm. In contrast, for four mustahabbat, one may recite durood and dua after tashahhud in the first sitting, and recite thana in the third, because each pair is a separate prayer. Reasoning: (1) The proof for praying four sunnats together is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: the Prophet used to pray four before Jumu'ah without separating between them. (2) Also from Abu Hurairah: 'When one of you prays Jumu'ah, let him pray four after it.' These hadiths show that one prays four before Jumu'ah with one salam. Translation: (219) If one prays a nafl of more than two rak'ahs and sits only at the end, it is valid istihsanan, because it becomes a single prayer, and in it the obligatory sitting is at the end.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is a section from the chapter on voluntary prayers (nawafil) in a Hanafi fiqh work, combining matn and commentary. It covers three main rulings: first, the recommended number of rak'ahs before and after certain prayers; second, the manner of sitting in the four-rak'ah mu'akkadah sunnah; and third, the validity of praying a nafl of more than two rak'ahs with only one sitting at the end. The author begins by stating that before Zuhr and before Jumu'ah and after Jumu'ah one prays with one taslim (i.e., without separating into two rak'ahs). Then he mentions that four rak'ahs are recommended before Asr, before Isha, and after Isha, and six after Maghrib. He provides hadith evidence for each. Notably, for the four before Asr, he cites two hadiths: one recommending four, and another from Ali that the Prophet prayed two, so either is permissible. For the four before Isha, he admits he did not find a direct proof but analogizes from the four after Maghrib. On page 424, the text moves to the first sitting in the four-rak'ah mu'akkadah sunnah: one restricts to only tashahhud and does not recite the opening supplication (istiftah) in the third rak'ah, unlike the mandubah where one may recite more. The reasoning is that the four rak'ahs are considered a single unit for mu'akkadah, so the first sitting is minimal, while mandubah are treated as separate pairs. Finally, the ruling on a nafl of more than two rak'ahs: if one sits only at the end, it is valid by istihsan (juristic preference) because it becomes one prayer, and the obligatory sitting is at the end. The author supports this by analogy and hadith. Throughout, the text uses the Hanafi methodology: citing hadith, applying qiyas, and using istihsan where appropriate.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Voluntary prayer, any supererogatory act of worship beyond the obligatory.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, a method of reasoning that departs from strict analogy in favor of a more equitable or practical ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the lesson, what is the basis for the validity of a nafl of more than two rak'ahs with only one final sitting?
A) Qiyas (analogy) to the obligatory prayers.
B) The hadith 'صلاة الليل مثنى مثنى'.
C) Istihsan (juristic preference) because it becomes one prayer.
D) The consensus of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
A voluntary prayer of more than two rak'ahs is valid even if you only sit at the end, due to istihsan, as it becomes one continuous prayer.

The First Sitting in 4-Rak'ah Mu'akkadah Prayers
Ruling with proof on first sitting content

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for the first sitting in a 4-rak'ah mu'akkadah sunnah and differentiate it from the mandubah.

Core Idea
In mu'akkadah four-rak'ah prayers, the first sitting contains only tashahhud; no additional supplications.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between emphasized (mu'akkadah) and non-emphasized (mandubah) sunnah prayers. This lesson focuses on the first sitting in a four-rak'ah mu'akkadah prayer—what should be recited and what should be omitted. The ruling is supported by a hadith encouraging four rak'ahs after Maghrib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer type
Determine whether the four-rak'ah sunnah is mu'akkadah (emphasized) or mandubah (recommended). The ruling applies only to mu'akkadah prayers such as the sunnah before Zuhr or after Jumu'ah.
Mu'akkadah sunnah are those the Prophet (peace be upon him) never omitted unnecessarily.
2
State the ruling for the first sitting
In the first sitting after two rak'ahs, recite only the tashahhud (the Attahiyyat). Do not add salawat, du'as, or blessings.
This restriction is specific to mu'akkadah; mandubah prayers allow additional recitations.
3
Note the omission in the third rak'ah
When standing for the third rak'ah, do not recite the opening supplication (du'a al-istiftah) again. The first rak'ah already includes it.
In mandubah prayers, one may repeat istiftah if desired.
4
Differentiate from mandubah
In mandubah (non-emphasized) four-rak'ah prayers, the first sitting is more flexible; one may recite salawat and other supplications after tashahhud.
The source contrasts mu'akkadah with mandubah using the phrase 'bikhilāfi al-mandūbah'.
5
Understand the proof
The ruling is supported by a hadith: 'Whoever prays four rak'ahs after Maghrib is like one who has performed a raid after a raid.' This establishes the virtue and practice of four rak'ahs after Maghrib, which is mu'akkadah.
The hadith is from Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, indicating the Prophet's practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقتصر فى الجلوس الاول من الرباعيّة المؤكدة على التشهد ولا يأتي في الثالثة بدعاء الاستفتاح بـخـلاف المندوبة. قال من ركع بعد المغرب اربع ركعات كان كالمعقب [ غزوة بعد غزوة - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الصلاة فيما بین المغرب والعشاء ، ج ثانی ،ص ۴۱۵، نمبر ۴۷۴۰).
He restricts in the first sitting of the emphasized four-rak'ah to the tashahhud and does not come in the third with the opening supplication, contrary to the recommended. Whoever prays four rak'ahs after maghrib is like one who has performed a raid after a raid.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn of Thamaratun Najah on supererogatory prayers. It states that in the four-rak'ah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), when one sits for the first tashahhud after the second rak'ah, only the tashahhud should be recited. One should not recite the opening supplication (du'a al-istiftah) when standing for the third rak'ah, nor should one recite blessings or supplications after the tashahhud. This is in contrast to the mandubah (recommended non-emphasized nawafil) where one may recite more. The hadith quoted supports the virtue of four rak'ahs after maghrib, which is part of the mu'akkadah. The proof is that the Prophet's practice was to pray four rak'ahs continuously without separation.

Key Terms
رباعيّة مؤكدة (ruba'iyyah mu'akkadah): A four-rak'ah prayer that is an emphasized sunnah, such as the sunnah before zuhr or after jumu'ah.
تشهد (tashahhud): The recitation of 'Attahiyyat lillah...' in the sitting posture.
استفتاح (istiftah): The opening supplication (thanā) recited at the beginning of the first rak'ah after takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a four-rak'ah mu'akkadah sunnah, what should be recited in the first sitting?
A) Only tashahhud
B) Tashahhud and salawat
C) Tashahhud, salawat, and a supplication
D) Nothing, as one does not sit

Key Takeaway
In mu'akkadah four-rak'ah prayers, the first sitting is limited to the tashahhud; do not add salawat or du'a al-istiftah in the third rak'ah.
