Joining Nafilah Rak'ahs: Validity by Istihsan
Ruling on joining more than two rak'ahs in nafilah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of istihsan to evaluate the validity of joining multiple nafilah rak'ahs with a single taslimah, and distinguish the Hanafi position from that of the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Joining more than two nafilah rak'ahs in one sitting is valid by istihsan.

Is it permissible to pray four rak'ahs of nafilah with only one sitting at the end? The Hanafi school says yes, based on a principle called istihsan (juristic preference), which overrides a strict analogy. This ruling demonstrates how the school prioritises practical ease and prophetic practice over rigid logical deductions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the default ruling
Recognise the scenario: someone prays more than two rak'ahs of nafilah and sits only at the end. According to qiyas (analogy), every two rak'ahs should be separated by a taslimah, so this would be invalid. Note that default ruling based on qiyas is invalidity.
Qiyas treats each pair as a separate unit.
2
Recognise the role of istihsan
Understand that istihsan overrides qiyas here. The reason: the entire set becomes one single prayer, and the obligatory sitting (for tashahhud) is only at the end. This is based on ease and prophetic practice.
3
Examine the evidence
Look at the hadith cited (from Aisha about the Prophet's practice after Maghrib). While the hadith mentions two rak'ahs, the principle is derived from other narrations where he prayed four or eight together. The istihsan is supported by the fact that the Prophet combined rak'ahs without sitting in between.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Note that the Shafi'i school requires separation after every two rak'ahs for nafilah. This difference shows how a different usul principle (no istihsan in Shafi'i) leads to a different ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا صلى نافلة اكثر من ركعتين ولم يجلس الا في آخرها صح استحسانا لانها صارت صلوة واحدة وفيها الفرض الجلوس آخرها. سألت عائشـة عـن صلوة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن تطوعه؟.... وكان يصلي بالناس المغرب ثم يدخل فيصلى ركعتين . (مسلم شریف، باب جواز النافلة قائما وقاعدا ،ص۲۵۲، نمبر ۶۹۹/۷۳۰ ا ر ابوداؤد شریف ، ابواب التطوع وركعات السنتہ ،ص ۱۸۵، نمبر ۱۲۵۱).
And if one prays a supererogatory prayer of more than two rak'ahs and does not sit except at the end of it, it is valid by istihsan because it has become a single prayer, and in it the obligatory sitting is at its end. I asked Aisha about the supererogatory prayer of the Messenger of Allah... and he used to pray maghrib with the people, then enter and pray two rak'ahs.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This ruling addresses a scenario where someone intends to pray more than two rak'ahs of nafilah as a single prayer (e.g., four rak'ahs with one taslimah). According to qiyas, this would be invalid because each pair of rak'ahs should be separated by taslim. However, by istihsan (juristic preference based on prophetic practice), it is valid. The reason is that the entire set becomes one prayer, and the obligatory sitting is only at the end. The hadith from Aisha mentions that the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs after maghrib, but the proof for joining is from other narrations where he prayed four or eight together. The text does not quote a direct hadith for joining, but the istihsan is based on the principle of following the practice.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that overrides qiyas in favor of a stronger evidence or convenience.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to derive rulings for new cases based on existing ones.
نافلة (nafila): Supererogatory prayer, voluntary act of worship beyond the obligatory ones.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone prays four rak'ahs of nafilah with only one sitting at the end, the prayer is:
A) Invalid because it should be two by two
B) Valid by istihsan
C) Valid only if it is a mu'akkadah sunnah
D) Invalid unless it is performed sitting

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, through istihsan, permits joining multiple nafilah rak'ahs with one taslimah, prioritizing ease and prophetic practice over strict analogy.

Karahah of Excessive Rak'ahs per Taslimah
Ruling on disliked number of rak'ahs per taslimah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maximum number of nafl rak'ahs per taslimah during the day and night and identify the ruling as makruh tanzih.

Core Idea
Four rak'ahs by day, eight by night: exceeding these per taslimah is makruh tanzih, not invalid.

In the Hanafi school, supererogatory prayers (nafl) follow specific etiquettes regarding how many rak'ahs may be offered together with a single taslimah. This lesson examines a clear ruling from the matn: it is disliked to join more than four rak'ahs during the day and more than eight at night with one taslimah. Understanding this helps the believer balance devotion with the sunna of moderation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is offering nafl rak'ahs in a single taslimah. The ruling is makruh (disliked) if a certain limit is exceeded.
2
Note the limit for daytime
During the day, the maximum is four rak'ahs per taslimah. Exceeding that is makruh.
This applies to any nafl, e.g., Duha.
3
Note the limit for nighttime
During the night, the maximum is eight rak'ahs per taslimah. Exceeding that is makruh.
This includes Tahajjud and other night prayers.
4
Understand the consequence
Exceeding the limit does not invalidate the prayer; it remains valid but is disliked (makruh tanzih).
The prayer is still accepted, but one should avoid the disliked action.
5
Recognize the evidence
The ruling is based on the prophetic practice: the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed four rak'ahs for Duha and eight for Tahajjud.
No explicit hadith is cited in the matn, but it is the understood dalil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره الزيادة على اربع بتسليمة فى النهار وعلى ثمان ليلا.
And it is disliked to increase beyond four with one taslimah during the day and beyond eight at night.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This is a clear ruling from the matn stating the limits for joining rak'ahs of nafilah with one taslimah. During the day, it is makruh (disliked) to exceed four rak'ahs. During the night, it is makruh to exceed eight. The proof for this is the prophetic practice: the Prophet prayed four rak'ahs for duha (day) and eight rak'ahs for tahajjud (night). Exceeding these limits without separation is considered makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked) because it departs from the optimal form.

Key Terms
بتسليمة (bi-taslimah): With one taslimah, meaning one salutation to end the prayer; i.e., joining rak'ahs without separating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) More than 2
B) More than 4
C) More than 8
D) More than 6

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts voluntary rak'ahs to 4 per taslimah by day and 8 by night; exceeding is makruh tanzih.

The Preferred Structure of Night Nawafil: Abu Hanifa vs the Sahibayn
Dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn on night nafilah structure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the preferred number of rak'ahs in night nawafil and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
In night nawafil, the fatwa follows the Sahibayn's view of praying two by two, not Abu Hanifa's four.

This lesson examines a subtle but important disagreement within the Hanafi school between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The issue is whether night voluntary prayers (nawafil) are better performed as four rak'ahs with one taslim or in separate pairs. Understanding this dispute deepens appreciation for how later Hanafi jurists reconciled and sometimes preferred the disciples' view over the imam's.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
Determine the exact fiqh issue: the preferred number of rak'ahs per taslimah in night nawafil. Note that the dispute is about afdaliyyah (preference), not validity—both forms are valid.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and evidence
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that both day and night nawafil are best as four rak'ahs with one taslim. His evidence is the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet prayed four rak'ahs of Duha.
The hadith is in Sahih Muslim.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and evidence
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that night nawafil are best performed two by two, based on the general command: 'Pray at night two by two.' For day nawafil, they agree with four.
The evidence is from Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: a person following Abu Hanifa may pray four rak'ahs of tahajjud together, while one following the Sahibayn must break them into two-rak'ah units with taslim after each.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and tarjih mechanism
The text explicitly says 'wa bihi yufta' (and with it is given fatwa), meaning the relied-upon position for fatwa is the Sahibayn's view for night prayers. The Sahibayn's view is more cautious and aligns with the general practice.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin (later fatwa works).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والافضل فيهما رباع عند ابي حنيفة وعندهما الافضل فى الليل مثنى مثنى و به یفتی.
And the best in both (day and night) is four according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the best at night is two by two, and this is what is given for fatwa.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the preferred number of rak'ahs per taslimah in night nawafil and day nawafil. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, both day and night nawafil are best performed as four rak'ahs with one taslimah. According to Sahibayn, at night it is better to pray in pairs (two by two), but during the day they agree with four. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is the view of Sahibayn for night prayers. The proof for Abu Hanifa includes the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet prayed four rak'ahs of duha (day). For night, Sahibayn rely on the hadith that the Prophet used to pray night prayers two by two. The fatwa follows Sahibayn because their view is more cautious and closer to general practice.

Key Terms
رباع (ruba'): Four rak'ahs performed with one sitting at the end.
مثنى مثنى (mathna mathna): Two rak'ahs performed separately with taslim after each pair.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Abu Hanifa's view of four rak'ahs
B) Sahibayn's view of two by two
C) Both are equally valid
D) Neither; the text does not specify

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, night nawafil are preferably prayed two by two, though praying four together is valid.

The Disliked Excess and Preferred Number in Voluntary Prayers
State of disliked excess and preferred number of rak'ats in nawafil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the maximum disliked rak'ats per taslim in voluntary prayers and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the preferred number for night prayers.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayers should be prayed in sets of two, but praying four together is valid—only disliked if exceeding the limit.

This passage presents two key points: first, the maximum number of rak'ats that can be prayed with one taslim before it becomes disliked (makruh); second, the preferred (afdal) method, which is debated within the Hanafi school. We will examine the Prophetic evidence and see how the school's later fatwa resolves the difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Find the two distinct rulings: (a) the maximum disliked limit (220) and (b) the preferred number (221).
The first is a ruling of karahah (dislike), the second of afdaliyyah (preference).
2
Locate evidence for the disliked limit
Examine the hadith from Aisha on the Prophet's night prayer (13 rak'ats total, 8 before witr) and Dhuha prayer (4 rak'ats). These set the maximum.
The limit is based on the Prophet's actual practice, not an explicit command.
3
Analyze evidence for the preferred number
Abu Hanifa cites hadith where the Prophet prayed four rak'ats together in Tahajjud and Dhuha. The Sahibayn cite the general command 'صلاة الليل والنهار مثنى مثنى' and reports of two-by-two practice.
The difference is in how the hadith are prioritized and interpreted.
4
Understand the tarjih (preference)
The text states 'و به یفتی' meaning the Sahibayn's view is the relied-upon position for night prayers. For day, there is no disagreement: four is better.
Tarjih is based on the strength of the general command supported by multiple ahadith.
5
Know the practical consequences
The limit is on karahah, not haram; exceeding it is disliked but valid. The preference is a recommendation, not an obligation; both methods are valid.
Avoid confusing 'preferred' with 'required'.

Chapter on voluntary prayers. (220) It is disliked to exceed four rak'ats with one taslim during the day, and eight at night. (221) The preferable in both is four according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the preferable at night is two-by-two, and on that is the fatwa. [Urdu commentary: It explains that each two rak'ats should be prayed separately with its own salam, but if one intends four rak'ats together and sits after the fourth, it is permissible. Evidence from hadith on the Prophet's night prayer. Translation of (220): And exceeding four rak'ats during the day and eight at night with one salam is disliked. Explanation: The hadith of Dhuha shows day prayer can be up to four together; the hadith of witr shows eight together at night. Translation of (221): According to Imam Abu Hanifa, both day and night, four rak'ats are better. According to the two companions, at night two-by-two is better, and this is the fatwa. Explanation: Abu Hanifa's evidence includes hadith of Aisha on Dhuha and Tahajjud; the companions' evidence includes hadith of Ibn Umar 'Prayer of night and day is two-by-two' and others.]
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage opens the section on voluntary prayers (نوافل). It contains two rulings. First, it is disliked (مکروہ) to pray more than four rak'ats with a single taslim during the day, or more than eight at night. The evidence comes from the practice of the Prophet ﷺ as reported by Aisha: he would pray eight rak'ats at night before witr, and four rak'ats for Dhuha. Second, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the preferred number of rak'ats per taslim. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that both day and night, four rak'ats in one taslim is better (أفضل), citing hadith where the Prophet prayed four in Dhuha and four in Tahajjud. The two companions (Sahibayn), Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that at night, two rak'ats with a separate taslim is better, based on the general command 'صلاة الليل والنهار مثنى مثنى' and other hadith. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the view of the Sahibayn for night prayers, while for day prayers there is no dispute that four is better. The commentary also clarifies that if one intends four rak'ats together, it is valid.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Voluntary, supererogatory prayer beyond the obligatory.
مثنى مثنى (mathna mathna): Two-by-two, i.e., praying two rak'ats with a separate taslim.
رباع (ribaa'): Four rak'ats with one taslim.
صاحبین (ṣāḥibayn): The two disciples of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
افضل (afḍal): Better, more meritorious; indicating a recommended preference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Voluntary prayers are valid with multiples of two up to the disliked limit, but the preferred method for night prayers is two-by-two per the Sahibayn's view.

Virtue of Night Prayer and Preferring Lengthy Standing
Ruling with proof: preferences in voluntary prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the superiority of night prayer over day prayer and the preference for lengthy standing over many prostrations, and explain the supporting evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Night prayer is superior, and lengthy standing outweighs many prostrations.

This passage from the fiqh text establishes two key preferences in voluntary prayers: night prayer is more excellent than day prayer, and it is better to prolong the standing (qiyam) than to increase the number of rak'ats. The author supports these rulings with authentic hadith from Sahih Muslim, including the special hour of acceptance and the divine descent in the last third of the night.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Note that the passage makes two distinct claims: (a) night prayer is better than day prayer, (b) lengthy standing is more beloved than many prostrations. These are recommendations (mustahabb) for greater reward, not obligations.
These rulings apply to voluntary prayers, not obligatory ones.
2
Locate the dalil for night prayer's virtue
The author cites two hadith: the special hour of acceptance and the divine descent. Explain how each supports the virtue of praying at night. The first hadith indicates a specific time when supplications are answered; the second shows Allah's closeness and mercy in the last third of the night.
Both hadith are from Sahih Muslim.
3
Locate the dalil for lengthy standing
The hadith 'The best prayer is the one with lengthy qunut' is cited. Understand that qunut here means standing, not the supplication. The phrase directly shows that lengthening standing enhances the prayer's merit.
Qunut has multiple meanings; context clarifies it means standing.
4
Analyze wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'افضل الصلاة طول القنوت' explicitly states that the best prayer is that with lengthy standing. This is a clear textual indication (zanni dalala) of preference.
The hadith is ahad, so thubut is zanni, but it is accepted for virtuous deeds.
5
Consider the consensus
This ruling is uncontested across schools (muttafaq alayh). The Hanafi school adheres to these preferences as mustahabb.
There is no ikhtilaf on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في النوافل (۶۲۲) وصلوة الليل افضل من صلوة النهار وطول القيام احبُّ من كثرة السجود. تشريح : : نوافل دن کی بھی بہتر ہیں، اور رات کی بھی لیکن رات کی نوافل زیادہ محبوب ہیں ، اور دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ، کثرت سے رکعتیں پڑھے اس سے بہتر ہے کہ رکعتیں کم ہوں اور قیام کافی لمبا ہو۔ وجه : (۱) رات کی نفل دن سے افضل ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن جابر ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ان من الليل ساعة لا يوافقها عبد مسلم يسأل الله خيرا الا اعطها اياه - (مسلم شریف ، باب فی اللیل ساعة مستجاب فيها الدعاء،ص۳۰۶ نمبر ۱۷۷۰/۷۵۷) (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ينزل ربنا صلى الله تبارک و تعالى كل ليلة الى السماء الدنيا حين يبقى ثلث الليل الآخير فيقول من يدعوني فأستجيب له و من يسألني فأعطيه و من يستغفرني فأغفر له . Chapter on voluntary prayers (222). And the night prayer is more excellent than the day prayer, and length of standing is more beloved than abundance of prostrations. [Urdu commentary: The voluntary prayers of the night are more beloved than those of the day. It is better to have long standing with fewer rak'ats than many rak'ats with brief standing. Evidence: (1) Hadith of Jabir: 'There is an hour in the night when no Muslim asks Allah for good but He gives it.' (2) Hadith of Abu Huraira: 'Our Lord descends to the lowest heaven in the last third of the night, saying: Who asks Me so that I may give him, who seeks forgiveness so that I may forgive him.' (3) Hadith of Jabir: 'The best prayer is the one with lengthy standing (qunut).']
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage establishes two important preferences in voluntary prayers. First, night prayer (صلوة الليل) is superior to day prayer. The evidence includes the special hour of acceptance and the divine descent in the last third of the night. Second, when praying, whether at night or day, it is better to prolong the standing (qiyam) rather than increase the number of rak'ats with short recitation. This is supported by the Prophet's statement: 'The best prayer is the one with lengthy standing (قنوت).' Note that here 'qunut' refers to standing in prayer, not the supplication of qunut. The Urdu commentary clarifies these points and emphasizes that fewer rak'ats with extended qiyam are more meritorious.

Key Terms
صلوة الليل (ṣalāt al-layl): Night prayer, including tahajjud and other voluntary prayers performed after 'Isha.
طول القيام (ṭūl al-qiyām): Lengthy standing in prayer, reading more Quran or prolonging recitation.
قنوت (qunūt): In this context, it means lengthy standing, not the supplication of qunut.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Night Prayer Virtue and the Rak'ah Dispute
Ruling on night prayer virtue and intra-Hanafi rak'ah dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the virtue of night prayer and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on rak'ah format, identifying the evidence for Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Night prayer is the most virtuous optional prayer; the rak'ah format—two-by-two vs four together—is a valid Hanafi difference.

In this passage, the author establishes the superiority of night prayer over day prayer and the preference for lengthy standing. He then addresses an internal Hanafi dispute: how many rak'ahs can be combined in tahajjud without a middle taslim? Imam Abu Hanifa permits four together, while his two chief companions (the Sahibayn) insist on two-by-two. Understanding this ikhtilaf and its evidence sharpens your ability to navigate the school's internal methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The passage first states that night prayer is better than day prayer, and long standing is more beloved than many prostrations. Note the hadith cited: the descent of Allah and the special hour.
This establishes the virtue of salat al-layl.
2
Locate the disputed issue
The dispute is on the format: how many rak'ahs can be prayed together without a middle taslim? Abu Hanifa says four together is allowed and even better; the Sahibayn say two-by-two is better.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not a difference with other madhhabs.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and dalil
Abu Hanifa's evidence is the hadith of Aisha: the Prophet prayed four rak'ahs (without mentioning taslim in between) and then four, totalling eleven for the night.
The operative phrase is 'prayed four' - indicating no taslim between them.
4
State the Sahibayn's position and dalil
The Sahibayn cite three hadith: (1) 'Night and day prayer is two-by-two' (Ibn Umar), (2) Aisha's report that he made taslim between every two, and (3) Umm Hani's report on duha prayer being eight with taslim after every two.
These hadith explicitly require taslim every two rak'ahs.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah al-khilaf
Both positions are valid, but the mufta bihi (relied-upon view) is to pray two-by-two, as it is more cautious and avoids disagreement. Practical difference: if someone prays four together, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa but considered makruh tanzihi by the Sahibayn.
In practice, the two-by-two method is encouraged for the general public.

فصل في النوافل
(۶۲۲) وصلوة الليل افضل من صلوة النهار وطول القيام احبُّ من كثرة السجود. ایک ساتھ پڑھی۔ (۲) اور تہجد میں چار رکعت ایک ساتھ پڑھی اس لئے رات کے نوافل میں چار رکعتیں افضل ہیں۔ عن عائشة كيف كانت صلاة رسول الله عليه في رمضان ؟ قالت ما كان رسول الله يزيد في رمضان و لا في غيره على احدى عشرة ركعة يصلى أربعا فلا تسأل عن حسنهن وطولهن ثم يصلي أربعا فلا تسأل عن حسنهن وطولهن - (مسلم شریف ، باب صلوة الليل وعدد ركعات النبى فى الليل ، ص ۲۹۹ نمبر ۱۷۲۳/۷۳۸) اس حدیث میں تہجد کی نماز ایک ساتھ چار رکعت پڑھی۔ وجه : اور صاحبین کے یہاں دو دو افضل ہیں اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے (۱) عن ابن عمر عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال صلوة الليل والنهار مثنى مثنى ان تشهد في كل ركعتين (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی صلوۃ النھار ص۱۹۰ نمبر ۱۲۹۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دن میں بھی دو دو رکعت پڑھے اور رات میں بھی دو رکعت پڑھے۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت كان رسول الله لا يصلى فيما بين ان يفرغ من صلوة العشاء وهي التي يدعو الناس العتمة الى الفجر احدى عشر ركعة يسلم بين كل ركعتين ۔ ( مسلم شریف ، باب صلوة الليل وعدد ركعات النبی ص في الليل، ص ۲۵۴، نمبر ۱۷۱۸/۷۳۶) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ رات کی نماز دو دو رکعت پڑھنی چاہئے ۔ (۳) اور دن کے بارے میں یہ حدیث ہے عن ام هانی بنت ابى طالب ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوم الفتح صلى سبحة الضحى ثماني ركعات يسلم من کل رکعتین۔ (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب صلوۃ الضحی ص۱۹۰ نمبر۱۲۹۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ دن کی نماز دو دورکعتیں پڑھے
ترجمه : (۶۲۲) رات کی نماز دن کی نماز سے افضل ہے۔ اور زیادہ رکعت پڑھنے سے دیر تک کھڑا رہنا افضل ہے۔ تشريح : نوافل دن کی بھی بہتر ہیں، اور رات کی بھی لیکن رات کی نوافل زیادہ محبوب ہیں ، اور دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ کثرت سے رکعتیں پڑھے اس سے بہتر ہے کہ رکعتیں کم ہوں اور قیام کافی لمبا ہو۔ وجه : (۱) رات کی نفل دن سے افضل ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن جابر ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ان من الليل ساعة لا يوافقها عبد مسلم يسأل الله خيرا الا اعطاها اياه - (مسلم شریف ، باب فی اللیل ساعة مستجاب فيها الدعاء،ص۳۰۶ نمبر ۱۷۷۰/۷۵۷) (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ينزل ربنا تبارك و تعالى كل ليلة الى السماء الدنيا حين يبقى ثلث الليل الآخير فيقول من يدعوني فأستجيب له و من يسألني فأعطيه و من يستغفرني فأغفر له . (مسلم شریف، باب الترغيب في الدعاء والذکر فی آخر اللیل والاجابتہ فیہ ص ۱۳۰۷، نمبر ۱۷۷۲/۷۵۸) (۳) اور طول قیام بہتر ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن جابر قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم افضل الصلاة طول القنوت (مسلم شریف ، باب افضل الصلاة طول القنوت ،ص ۳۰۶ نمبر ۱۷۶۸/۷۵۶)
Section on supererogatory prayers. (622) Night prayer is better than day prayer, and long standing is more beloved than many prostrations. Pray together. (2) And in tahajjud, pray four rak'ahs together, so for night supererogatory prayers, four rak'ahs are better. From Aisha: How was the prayer of the Messenger of Allah in Ramadan? She said: The Messenger of Allah did not increase in Ramadan or other than it beyond eleven rak'ahs. He prayed four - do not ask about their beauty and length - then he prayed four - do not ask about their beauty and length. (Muslim) In this hadith, tahajjud prayer is prayed four rak'ahs together. Reason: And according to the two companions (Sahibayn), two-by-two is better; their evidence is this hadith: (1) From Ibn Umar from the Prophet (SAW): Night and day prayer is two-by-two, with a tashahhud in every two rak'ahs. (Abu Dawood) In this hadith, it says that in day and night, pray two rak'ahs. (2) In a hadith: From Aisha: The Messenger of Allah would not pray between finishing Isha prayer - which people call Atama - until Fajr except eleven rak'ahs, making taslim between every two rak'ahs. (Muslim) From this hadith it is also known that night prayer should be prayed two-by-two. (3) Regarding day, this hadith: From Umm Hani bint Abi Talib that the Messenger of Allah on the day of conquest prayed the forenoon prayer (salat al-duha) eight rak'ahs, making taslim after every two rak'ahs. (Abu Dawood) This hadith shows that day prayer is prayed two-by-two. Translation: (622) Night prayer is better than day prayer, and it is better to stand long rather than many rak'ahs. Explanation: Supererogatory prayers are good both day and night, but night supererogatory prayers are more beloved. And the second point: many rak'ahs are better than fewer rak'ahs with long standing. Reason: (1) Night supererogatory is better than day for this hadith: From Jabir: The Messenger of Allah said: There is an hour in the night that no Muslim slave asks Allah for good but He gives it to him. (Muslim) (2) In this hadith too: From Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah said: Our Lord, blessed and exalted, descends every night to the lowest heaven when the last third of the night remains, and says: Who calls upon Me so I answer him? Who asks Me so I give him? Who seeks My forgiveness so I forgive him? (Muslim) (3) And long standing is better; its evidence is this hadith: From Jabir: The Messenger of Allah said: The best prayer is long standing (qunut). (Muslim)
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage covers two main rulings on night prayer from a Hanafi fiqh work. First, it states that night prayer (salat al-layl) is superior to day prayer, and that lengthy standing (qiyam) is more virtuous than performing many prostrations with shorter standing. The proof includes hadith about the special hour of acceptance and the Lord's descent to the lowest heaven. Second, the passage details a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the number of rak'ahs in night prayers (especially tahajjud). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that praying four rak'ahs together in one unit (i.e., without taslim between each two) is permissible and even better, citing the practice of the Prophet praying four and then four in Ramadan. However, the two companions (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that night prayers should be prayed two-by-two (muthanna muthanna), based on the hadith 'Night and day prayer is two-by-two' and other reports. The text presents both views with their respective dalil (hadith). The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that it is permissible to pray up to four rak'ahs together at night, but two-by-two is also acceptable and considered better by the Sahibayn. The student should note that this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf, and both positions are valid within the school.

Key Terms
صلاة الليل (salat al-layl): Night prayer, including tahajjud and other voluntary prayers at night
طول القيام (tul al-qiyam): Lengthy standing in prayer, considered more virtuous than many prostrations
صاحبين (sahibayn): The two companions of Imam Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, how many rak'ahs can be prayed together in a single unit (without taslim between them) during night prayer (tahajjud)?
A) Only two
B) Up to four
C) Up to eight
D) Only one

Key Takeaway
Night prayer is the most virtuous supererogatory prayer; within the Hanafi school, praying two-by-two is the cautious view, but four together is also valid based on sound evidence.

Tahiyyat al-Masjid: Sunnah and Substitution by Any Prayer
Ruling on tahiyyat al-masjid and its substitution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tahiyyat al-masjid as sunnah mu'akkadah and explain how any prayer upon entry, including fard, fulfills it.

Core Idea
Any prayer upon entering a mosque fulfills tahiyyat al-masjid, even without specific intention.

Tahiyyat al-masjid is a confirmed sunnah when entering a mosque, but does it require a dedicated two-rak'ah prayer? This passage clarifies that the 'right of the mosque' is discharged by any prayer you perform before sitting—whether it is fard, sunnah, or nafl. We will examine the hadith proof and the practical implications for daily worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is tahiyyat al-masjid? It is a prayer of greeting upon entering a mosque. According to the Hanafi school, it is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah) to pray two rak'ahs before sitting down. It is not wajib or fard.
Sunnah mu'akkadah is a practice the Prophet consistently performed and recommended.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Abu Qatada al-Sulami: The Prophet (ﷺ) said, 'When one of you enters the mosque, let him pray two rak'ahs before sitting.' (Bukhari and Muslim). Note that the hadith uses an imperative (فَلْيَرْكَعْ).
The text quotes the hadith in Arabic and references Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Hanafi school interprets the imperative 'فَلْيَرْكَعْ' as indicating recommendation (sunnah) rather than obligation (wajib) because the context is optional prayers and the Prophet did not enforce it strictly. Thus, the hadith proves sunnah, not fard.
This is a key Hanafi usul principle: al-amr al-mutlaq yufidu al-wujub unless there is a qarinah (context) suggesting recommendation.
4
Understand the substitution rule
The text states that 'the performance of the fard substitutes for it, and every prayer performed upon entering without the intention of tahiyyat suffices.' This means that any prayer—fard, sunnah, or nafl—that you pray before sitting fulfills the right of the mosque (haqq al-masjid). The specific intention of tahiyyat is not required.
This is based on the principle that the purpose (greeting the mosque) is achieved by any prayer.
5
Apply to a scenario
If you enter the mosque and immediately join the congregation for the fard prayer (e.g., Zuhr), you have performed tahiyyat al-masjid. You do not need to pray an additional two rak'ahs before or after the fard.
The same applies if you pray a sunnah prayer (like sunnah of fajr) upon entry.

Section on tahiyyat al-masjid, salat al-duha, and reviving the nights. (623) Tahiyyat al-masjid is sunnah: two rak'ahs before sitting. (224) The performance of the fard substitutes for it, and every prayer performed upon entering without the intention of tahiyyat (suffices). (225a) And two rak'ahs after wudu before it dries are recommended (mustahabb). Section on tahiyyat al-masjid, salat al-duha, and tahajjud etc. Translation: (623) Before sitting, two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid are sunnah. Explanation: When entering the Baitullah (Ka'bah), its right is to perform tawaf; similarly, when entering a mosque, its right is to pray two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid. So if one prays any prayer without the intention of tahiyyat, the right of the mosque is still fulfilled and tahiyyat al-masjid is considered performed. Reason: The hadith is: From Abu Qatada al-Sulami: The Messenger of Allah said: When one of you enters the mosque, let him pray two rak'ahs before sitting. (Bukhari, Muslim) In this hadith, it says to pray two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid before sitting. The point: The right of the mosque is to pray any prayer when entering. Translation: (624) The performance of the fard is sufficient for tahiyyat al-masjid, and every prayer that one prays upon entering without the intention of tahiyyat also suffices for tahiyyat al-masjid. Explanation: If one enters the mosque and prays the fard prayer, tahiyyat al-masjid is fulfilled because the right of the mosque is discharged. Similarly, if one prays any other prayer without the intention of tahiyyat, tahiyyat al-masjid is also fulfilled. Reason: In this hadith, the sunnah of Jumu'ah and tahiyyat al-masjid were combined with one intention. He heard Jabir say: A man entered on Friday while the Prophet was giving the khutbah, and he said: Have you prayed? He said: No. He said: Pray two rak'ahs. (Bukhari, Abu Dawood)
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling of tahiyyat al-masjid (the prayer of greeting the mosque) according to the Hanafi school. It is a sunnah (confirmed, though not fard) to pray two rak'ahs before sitting down when entering a mosque. However, the text clarifies that this is not a strict obligation; rather, the right of the mosque (haqq al-masjid) is discharged by any prayer offered upon entry, even without the specific intention of tahiyyat. For example, if one enters and prays the fard (obligatory) prayer, or any other sunnah or nafl prayer, that suffices for tahiyyat al-masjid. The proof is the hadith commanding two rak'ahs before sitting, and also the incident of the man entering during the Friday khutbah: the Prophet ordered him to pray two rak'ahs, which were both the sunnah of Friday and the tahiyyat al-masjid combined. This shows that the intention does not need to be specific; any voluntary prayer upon entry fulfills the greeting. The text also notes that the 'right of the mosque' is to offer a prayer, not necessarily a specific one. This is a practical ruling: if one is late for a fard prayer upon entering the mosque, they can join the fard and it will count as tahiyyat al-masjid, so they don't need to pray a separate two rak'ahs. The student should understand that while the best is to intend the two-rak'ah tahiyyat, the obligation (haqq) is fulfilled by any prayer that is prayed before sitting.

Key Terms
تحیۃ المسجد (tahiyyat al-masjid): A prayer of greeting upon entering a mosque, consisting of two rak'ahs before sitting
سنة (sunnah): An act that the Prophet consistently did and recommended; not obligatory but rewarded
فرض (fard): Obligatory prayer that can substitute for tahiyyat al-masjid upon entry

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person enters the mosque and immediately joins the congregation for the fard prayer (without praying two rak'ahs first), has he performed tahiyyat al-masjid?
A) No, because he did not intend it
B) Yes, because the fard fulfills the right of the mosque
C) No, because he must pray two rak'ahs before sitting
D) Yes, but only if he prays two rak'ahs after the fard

Key Takeaway
Tahiyyat al-masjid is a sunnah fulfilled by any valid prayer performed upon entering the mosque before sitting; intention of greeting is not required.

Tahiyyat al-Wudu: The Recommended Prayer After Wudu
Ruling on prayer after wudu before limbs dry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Tahiyyat al-Wudu in the Hanafi school and explain the evidence from hadith that supports its recommendation.

Core Idea
Tahiyyat al-Wudu is mustahabb, not wajib: the hadith promises forgiveness, not command.

This lesson deals with a specific recommended prayer known as Tahiyyat al-Wudu. The text states that two rak'ahs after wudu, before the limbs dry, are mustahabb. We will examine the evidence from the hadith of 'Uthman and understand why the Hanafi school classifies it as mustahabb rather than sunnah muakkadah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying two rak'ahs after completing wudu before the limbs dry. The ruling is mustahabb (recommended).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of the Prophet reported by 'Uthman: 'No Muslim performs wudu and does it well, then prays a prayer, except that his sins between that prayer and the next are forgiven.' (Muslim, Nasa'i)
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith promises forgiveness as an incentive, but uses no commanding imperative. In Hanafi usul, a promise of reward without a command indicates recommendation (nadb).
The evidence is zanni al-dalala (general virtue).
4
Confirm the Hanafi classification
Since the dalil is zanni and general, the ruling is mustahabb, not wajib or sunnah muakkadah. The text uses 'ندب' (recommended) explicitly.
Some other schools may consider it sunnah, but Hanafi considers it mustahabb.

And two rak'ahs after wudu before its drying are recommended. Translation: (625a) And after wudu, before the limbs dry, two rak'ahs (are mustahabb). Explanation: Here five prayers that are mustahabb are mentioned; they should be prayed when opportunity arises. Among them, the first is Tahiyyat al-Wudu. Evidence: (1) This hadith proves it: He saw 'Uthman call for water... then he said: The Messenger of Allah said... (2) Also in this hadith: I heard 'Uthman ibn 'Affan... I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'No Muslim performs wudu and does it well, then prays a prayer, except that his sins between that prayer and the next are forgiven.' (Muslim, Nasa'i)
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on Tahiyyat al-Wudu. The matn states that two rak'ahs after wudu before the limbs dry are mustahabb (recommended). The commentary classifies it as one of five mustahabb prayers. The proof is the hadith from 'Uthman where the Prophet mentioned forgiveness for one who performs wudu properly and prays afterward. Another hadith emphasizes the virtue of praying after wudu. The Hanafi position considers this mustahabb, not sunnah muakkadah, as it is based on general virtue rather than a specific command.

Key Terms
تحية الوضوء (tahiyyat al-wudu): Two rak'ahs prayed after completing wudu before the wetness of the limbs dries.

Recommended Prayers: Duha, Tahajjud, Istikhara, and Salat al-Hajat
Rulings on Duha, Tahajjud, Istikhara, and Salat al-Hajat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Duha, Tahajjud, Istikhara, and Salat al-Hajat, and identify the textual evidence for each.

Core Idea
Four recommended prayers — each supported by Quran and Sunnah — are mustahabb, not wajib.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents the rulings for four recommended prayers: Duha (forenoon), Tahajjud (night), Istikhara (seeking guidance), and Salat al-Hajat (prayer of need). Each is classified as mustahabb in the Hanafi school. The text provides the minimum rak'ahs for Duha (four) and Tahajjud (sets of two or four), and describes the procedure for Istikhara. We will examine the evidence and understand the flexibility in the recommended acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify each prayer and its ruling
List the four prayers: Duha, Tahajjud, Istikhara, Salat al-Hajat. All are mustahabb (recommended) according to the text's use of the term 'ندب'.
2
Locate the dalil for Duha
Examine the two hadiths: 'Aisha narrates the Prophet prayed four rak'ahs and increased as he wished; Umm Hani narrates eight rak'ahs on the conquest of Mecca. These establish flexibility.
The Hanafi minimum is four, not two.
3
Locate the dalil for Tahajjud
The Quranic verse 17:79 commands Tahajjud as a nafilah (supererogatory), and hadiths confirm the Prophet's practice, including the narration of 'Aisha about eleven rak'ahs in sets of four.
The command is for nafilah, not fard.
4
Understand the Istikhara procedure
When uncertain about a permissible matter, pray two rak'ahs with the specific du'a. If no clarity after one day, repeat for up to a week. Sometimes guidance comes in a dream.
The du'a is recommended but not required for validity.
5
Synthesize the common ruling
All four prayers are mustahabb, not obligatory. They share flexibility in number and timing, with evidence from prophetic practice.
The Hanafi school relies on these proofs for the recommended status.

And four or more in Duha, and night prayer, Istikhara prayer, and Salat al-Hajat are recommended. Translation: (225b) And at the time of Duha [forenoon], four or more, and Tahajjud, Istikhara, and Salat al-Hajat are mustahabb. Explanation: [2] Duha prayer: pray four rak'ahs or more. The prayer offered at 9 a.m. is called Salat al-Duha. Evidence: (1) Hadith of 'Aisha: 'The Prophet used to pray Duha four rak'ahs and increase as he wished.' (Muslim) (2) Hadith of Umm Hani: 'The Prophet entered her house on the day of conquest of Mecca, bathed, and prayed eight rak'ahs.' (Bukhari) [3] Tahajjud prayer is mustahabb. Evidence: (1) Quran 17:79: 'And from the night, pray Tahajjud as an extra prayer for you.' (2) Hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet used to get up at night to pray Tahajjud.' (Bukhari) (3) Hadith of 'Aisha: 'The Prophet prayed eleven rak'ahs in Ramadan and other months, four at a time...' (Muslim, Bukhari) [4] Istikhara prayer: When uncertain about a good deed, pray two rak'ahs with the supplication; this is mustahabb. If not revealed in one day, continue for a week. Sometimes it is revealed in a dream...
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage provides rulings and proofs for several recommended prayers. Duha prayer: minimum four rak'ahs (can be more), based on 'Aisha's hadith that the Prophet prayed four and increased as he wished, and Umm Hani's hadith of eight rak'ahs. Tahajjud is mustahabb, supported by Quran 17:79 and hadith of the Prophet's practice. Istikhara prayer is recommended when one is uncertain about a matter: pray two rak'ahs with the specific du'a, and continue for up to a week if needed. Salat al-Hajat is also mentioned as mustahabb. The Hanafi school considers these all mustahabb (recommended) but not obligatory. The text emphasizes flexibility: Duha can be four or more, Tahajjud can be prayed in sets of two or four, and Istikhara should be repeated if no clarity.

Key Terms
صلاة الضحى (salat al-duha): Forenoon prayer, minimum four rak'ahs, prayed after sunrise until before noon.
تهجد (tahajjud): Night prayer after waking from sleep, mustahabb.
صلاة الاستخارة (salat al-istikhara): Two rak'ahs prayed when uncertain about a matter, followed by a specific supplication seeking guidance.

Key Takeaway

Ruling on Salat al-Duha: Minimum Rak'ahs and Proof
Ruling on the supererogatory prayer of Duha with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Salat al-Duha and explain the hadith evidence for four rak'ahs as the minimum.

Core Idea
Salat al-Duha is an emphasized sunnah with a minimum of four rak'ahs based on the Prophet's consistent practice.

This lesson covers the ruling on the forenoon prayer, Salat al-Duha, which is highly recommended in the Hanafi school. The passage provides the matn stating 'four or more' and supports it with two key hadiths. We will examine the legal ruling, the proof structure, and the difference from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Salat al-Duha is the forenoon supererogatory prayer. The passage classifies it as recommended (sunna) and specifies a minimum of four rak'ahs.
The ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadiths are cited: from Aisha (RA) that the Prophet (SAW) prayed four rak'ahs, and from Umm Hani (RA) that he prayed eight rak'ahs on the day of conquest.
Both are ahad hadiths, so the thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's actual practice (sunnah fi'liyyah) indicates recommendation. The four rak'ahs show the minimum, and the eight show permissibility of more.
The hadith of Aisha is primary for the minimum.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that the minimum is two rak'ahs, based on other hadiths and their method of combining proofs.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Sunni schools.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school prefers the four rak'ah minimum as mufta bihi, relying on the explicit practice of the Prophet in Aisha's hadith.
The ruling is taken from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Chapter on supererogatory prayers. And four or more in Duha, and recommended are Salat al-Layl, Salat al-Istikhara, and Salat al-Hajah. Perform wudu like my wudu then pray two rak'ahs not speaking to himself in them, his past sins will be forgiven. (Bukhari, Muslim) (2) Also in this hadith: I heard Uthman ibn Affan... Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on Salat al-Duha (the forenoon prayer). The Arabic matn states that one should pray four or more rak'ahs in the Duha time, and lists it among recommended prayers. The Urdu commentary explains that Duha prayer is prayed at about 9 am and provides two hadith proofs. The first from Aisha shows the Prophet prayed four rak'ahs as a minimum, and the second from Umm Hani shows he prayed eight rak'ahs on one occasion. The commentary also mentions that the prayer can be increased. This establishes that Duha prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) according to the Hanafi school, with the minimum being four rak'ahs, though two rak'ahs are also permissible according to some scholars.

Key Terms

Ruling on Salat al-Tahajjud (Night Prayer)
Ruling on the supererogatory night prayer (Tahajjud)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tahajjud prayer and cite the Quranic and hadith evidence that support its recommendation.

Core Idea
Tahajjud is a highly recommended sunnah, not obligatory, as the Quran explicitly calls it a nafila.

This passage explains the ruling on Tahajjud (night prayer) in the Hanafi school. It provides three pieces of evidence: a Quranic verse, a hadith from Ibn Abbas describing the Prophet's practice, and a narration from Aisha detailing the number of rak'ahs. The passage establishes that Tahajjud is mustahabb (recommended) and gives insight into its format.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the hukm level (sunnah muakkadah) and the basis for it being recommended, not obligatory.
The verse description 'nafila' is key.
2
Analyze the primary dalil
Examine Quran 17:79. Note the command 'fatahajjad' and the qualifier 'nafila' which indicates supererogatory status for the Prophet and by extension the ummah.
The Hanafi school interprets the command as nadb (recommendation) due to the explicit mention of nafila.
3
Confirm with secondary dalil
Review the hadith from Ibn Abbas (general practice) and Aisha (specific number of rak'ahs) to see the Prophetic application.
These hadith show Tahajjud was prayed in sets of four, not exceeding eleven rak'ahs in total.
4
Determine practical application
Synthesize the evidence: Tahajjud is performed after Isha until Fajr, preferably in sets of two or four, with no maximum but following the Prophet's example.
Witr is typically prayed after Tahajjud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳] تهجد کی نماز پڑھنا مستحب ہے۔
وجه : (۱) اس آیت میں ہے۔ و مـن الـلـيـل فتهجد به نافلة لك عسى ان یبعثک ربک مقاما محمودا ( آیت ۷۹، سورۃ الاسراء۱۷) (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ سمع ابن عباس قال كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا قام من الليل يتهجد ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب التهجد باللیل ،ص ۱۷۹ نمبر ۱۱۲۰) (۳) سأل عائشة كيف كانت صلاة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في رمضان ؟ قالت ما كان رسول الله الا الله يزيد في رمضان ولا فی غیره على احدى عشرة ركعة يصلي أربعا فلا تسأل عن حسنهن وطولهن ثم يصلي أربعا فلا تسأل عن حسنهن وطولهن ۔ (مسلم شریف، باب صلوۃ اليل و عدد ركعات النبي في الليل، ص ۲۹۹ نمبر ۷۲۳/۷۳۸ار بخاری شریف، باب قیام النبی ع باليل في رمضان و غیره ،ص۱۸۳، نمبر ۱۱۴۷) اس حدیث میں تہجد کی نماز ایک ساتھ چار رکعت پڑھی۔
[3] It is recommended to pray Tahajjud prayer. Evidence: (1) This verse: And from the night, perform Tahajjud as an additional prayer for you; perhaps your Lord will raise you to a praised station. (Surah Al-Isra 17:79) (2) This hadith: Ibn Abbas said: The Prophet, when he got up at night, would pray Tahajjud. (Bukhari #1120) (3) He asked Aisha: How was the prayer of the Messenger of Allah in Ramadan? She said: He did not exceed eleven rak'ahs, not in Ramadan nor other times. He would pray four, and do not ask about their beauty and length, then pray four, and do not ask about their beauty and length... (Muslim #723/738) In this hadith, Tahajjud was prayed four rak'ahs at a time.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage discusses Salat al-Tahajjud, the night prayer. The Urdu commentary states it is mustahabb (recommended) and provides three pieces of evidence. First, Quran 17:79 specifically commands 'Tahajjud' as a nafila (supererogatory) prayer for the Prophet, which the Hanafi school interprets as recommending it for the ummah as well. Second, a hadith from Ibn Abbas describes the Prophet's practice of waking at night for Tahajjud. Third, a narration from Aisha describes the Prophet's night prayer in Ramadan as eleven rak'ahs total, prayed in sets of four and four, showing the format. The Hanafi school considers Tahajjud as a separate sunnah (not necessarily contiguous with witr), though it is often included in qiyam al-layl.

Key Terms
تهجد (Tahajjud): Supererogatory prayer performed at night after sleeping, with evidence from Quran and Sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Surah Al-Isra 17:79
C) Surah Al-Fatiha
D) Surah Al-Baqarah

Key Takeaway
Tahajjud is a recommended sunnah prayer based on Quran and Sunnah, evidenced by the command in Surah Al-Isra and the Prophet's practice.

Ruling on Salat al-Istikhara (Prayer for Guidance)
Ruling on the prayer for seeking guidance (Istikhara)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Salat al-Istikhara, describe its procedure, and identify signs of its acceptance according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Istikhara: two rak'ahs of nafil + du'a for guidance when uncertain about a permissible matter.

When facing a decision, a Muslim may feel uncertain about which choice is better. The Hanafi school teaches that Salat al-Istikhara is a recommended (mustahabb) means of seeking Allah's guidance. This lesson explains the procedure, the evidence from the hadith of Jabir, and how to interpret the outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage clearly states that Istikhara is mustahabb (recommended). Note that it applies only to permissible (mubah) matters, not to obligatory or prohibited acts.
Hanafi view: if the act is wajib, no need for Istikhara; if haram, Istikhara is inappropriate.
2
Describe the prescribed procedure
The procedure is: pray two rak'ahs of non-obligatory prayer (nafil), then recite the du'a taught by the Prophet (peace be upon him). The passage advises repeating for up to one week if no clear sign appears.
The du'a asks Allah for guidance based on His knowledge and power.
3
Analyze the evidence (dalil)
The hadith of Jabir (Bukhari and Abu Dawud) is the primary proof. The Prophet taught the companions Istikhara for all matters. The command 'fal yarka' (let him pray) indicates recommendation in Hanafi usul.
This hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) so the ruling is sunnah/mustahabb, not fard.
4
Understand the signs of acceptance
Guidance may come as a dream directing one choice, or more commonly as an inclination of the heart towards one option. If the heart feels inclined, the Istikhara is considered fulfilled.
If no inclination after a week, one may proceed with the choice that seems best after consulting others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[4] The prayer of Istikhara: when there is hesitation in doing a good deed, he should pray two rak'ahs and recite the following supplication, and seek guidance from Allah. It is recommended. If the matter is not revealed in one day, he should continue for a week. Sometimes the guidance comes in a dream that says do this or don't do this. Sometimes the heart inclines towards doing or not doing, so if the heart inclines, the Istikhara is fulfilled. It is better for the person to do the Istikhara himself. Evidence: (1) This hadith: Jabir said: The Prophet taught us Istikhara in all matters as he taught us a surah from the Quran. When one of you intends a matter, let him pray two rak'ahs of voluntary prayer then say: 'O Allah, I seek guidance by Your knowledge, and I seek ability by Your power, and I ask You of Your great bounty...' (Bukhari #6382, Abu Dawud #1538) This hadith contains the supplication of Istikhara and the method of its prayer.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage covers Salat al-Istikhara, the prayer for seeking guidance when one is uncertain about a decision. The author states it is mustahabb (recommended). The commentary expands on the method: pray two rak'ahs of non-obligatory prayer, recite the well-known du'a, and continue for up to a week if no clear sign. Signs of guidance may come in a dream or through the heart's inclination. The proof is the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet taught the sahaba Istikhara with the specific du'a. The Hanafi school emphasizes that Istikhara is for matters that are permissible (mubah) or recommended (mustahabb), not for actions that are clearly obligatory or prohibited. The prayer should be performed with full concentration.

Key Terms
استخارة (Istikhara): A prayer of two rak'ahs followed by a specific du'a to seek Allah's guidance in a decision.

Salat al-Istikhara is a recommended prayer of two rak'ahs with a specific du'a; guidance may come through a dream or heart inclination, and if no sign appears after a week, one may proceed with the best apparent choice.

Introduction to Salat al-Hajah: The Prayer for Need
Ruling with proof on Salat al-Hajah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Salat al-Hajah, identify its key steps from the hadith, and explain why it is recommended (sunnah) based on the dalil.

Core Idea
Salat al-Hajah is a recommended prayer for any lawful need, proven by a specific hadith.

Salat al-Hajah is a supererogatory prayer that Muslims may offer when they have a particular need, whether from Allah or from people. The Hanafi school views it as a sunnah (recommended) act, not obligatory. In this lesson, we will examine the ruling and the method prescribed in the hadith narrated by Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (Salat al-Hajah) and the hukm level according to the Hanafi school (sunnah/mustahabb).
The author states it is recommended when a need arises.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith of Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa. Note its source (Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah) and its chain (ahad).
The hadith is ahad (single-narrator), making it zanni al-thubut.
3
Extract the wajh al-dalalah
Identify how the hadith indicates recommendation: the command 'fal yatawadda' (let him perform wudu) and 'fal yusalli' (let him pray) are understood in Hanafi usul to indicate nadb (recommendation) when there is no qarina (context) making it obligatory.
The Hanafi rule: al-amr yufidu al-wujub unless there is a qarina to the contrary; here the context of dua and request suggests nadb.
4
List the method as given in the hadith
Break down the steps: wudu, prayer of two rak'ahs, praise, salawat, du'a. Note the specific du'a text.
The du'a includes asking for forgiveness, relief, and fulfillment of the need.
5
Note the practical implication
Understand that this prayer is not time-specific; it can be performed whenever a need arises, as a general nafl prayer.
Hanafi: no fixed time; it is simply a recommended prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۵] نماز حاجت کوئی ضرورت پڑ جائے تو دورکعت حاجت کی نماز پڑھے
وجه : اس حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن ابی اوفی قال قال رسول الله له من كانت له الى الله حاجة او الى احد من بني آدم فليتوضأ و ليحسن الوضوء ثم ليصل ركعتين ثم ليثن على الله و ليصل على النبي الله ثم ليقل ، لا اله الا الله الحليم الكريم سبحان الله رب العرش العظيم ، الحمد لله رب العالمين ، اسألک موجبات رحمتک و عزائم مغفرتک ، و الغنيمة من كل بر و السلامة من كل اثم ، لا تدع لى ذنبا إلا غفرته و لا هما الا فرجته و لا حاجة هي لك رضا الا قضيتها يا ارحم الرحمین ۔(ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء في صلاة الحاجة ، ص ۱۲۶، نمبر ۴۷۹ رابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ما جاء فی صلاۃ الحاجة ، ص ۱۹۷، نمبر ۱۳۸۴) اس حدیث میں نماز حاجت کا طریقہ بتایا گیا ہے۔
[5] Prayer of Need: When a need arises, he should pray two rak'ahs of Hajah prayer. Evidence: This hadith provides proof. From Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa that the Messenger of Allah said: Whoever has a need from Allah or from any human, let him perform wudu and perfect it, then pray two rak'ahs, then praise Allah and send blessings on the Prophet, then say: 'There is no god but Allah, the Forbearing, the Generous. Glory be to Allah, Lord of the Great Throne. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds. I ask You for the means of Your mercy and the firm resolve of Your forgiveness, and gain in every good and safety from every sin. Do not leave any sin of mine except that You forgive it, nor any worry except that You relieve it, nor any need that is pleasing to You except that You fulfill it, O Most Merciful of the merciful.' (Tirmidhi #479, Ibn Majah #1384) This hadith explains the method of Salat al-Hajah.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage covers Salat al-Hajah, the prayer offered when one has a specific need from Allah or from people. The author states it is recommended (mustahabb) without specifying the number of rak'ahs other than two. The proof is the hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa, which gives the full method: perform wudu properly, pray two rak'ahs, praise Allah, send blessings on the Prophet, and recite the specific du'a. The Hanafi school considers this prayer to be from the general category of nafl prayers; it does not have a fixed time and can be offered whenever a need arises. The du'a includes seeking forgiveness, relief from worry, and the fulfillment of the need.

Key Terms
صلاة الحاجة (Salat al-Hajah): A supererogatory prayer of two rak'ahs with a specific du'a to request fulfillment of a need from Allah.

Salat al-Hajah is a recommended prayer (sunnah) for any lawful need, performed by first doing wudu, praying two rak'ahs, and then reciting the specific du'a from the hadith.

Which Nights to Revive and Their Ruling
Ruling with proof on reviving specific nights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the nights recommended for reviving with worship and state the Hanafi ruling (sunnah mu'akkadah) along with the primary evidence.

Core Idea
Reviving certain blessed nights is a highly recommended sunnah, not an obligation.

The Hanafi school encourages Muslims to seek extra rewards by spending specific nights in prayer and worship. This passage identifies which nights are specially recommended and gives the basis for their virtue. Understanding this ruling helps you prioritize your devotional time effectively.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nights mentioned
Read the passage carefully and list all the nights explicitly mentioned for revival. The Arabic matn mentions three, and the Urdu commentary adds a fourth.
The nights are: last ten nights of Ramadan, two Eid nights, first ten nights of Dhul Hijjah, and the 15th night of Sha'ban.
2
Determine the hukm (ruling)
Note the verb used: 'nadb' or 'mustahabb' – both indicate a recommended act, not obligatory. The Hanafi position is that reviving these nights is sunnah mu'akkadah.
Sunnah mu'akkadah is a confirmed sunnah; omitting it is disliked but not sinful.
3
Find the evidence (dalil)
The passage cites a hadith from Aisha about seeking Laylat al-Qadr in the odd nights of the last ten of Ramadan. This is used as proof for reviving all last ten nights, and by analogy, the other nights also have similar virtues.
The hadith is a hadith ahad, so its thubut is zanni, but it is widely accepted.
4
Connect the ruling to the evidence
Explain how the hadith supports the recommendation: the command 'seek' implies effort and worship, which extends to reviving the entire set of nights.
The Hanafi school emphasizes that reviving these nights means spending most of the night in worship, not necessarily the entire night.

Source Text

(٦٢٦) وندب احياء ليالى العشر الاخير من رمضان واحياء ليلتي العيدين وليالي عشر ذي الحجة
ترجمه : (۶۲۶) اور رمضان کی اخیر کی دس راتیں اور دونوں عیدین کی شب اور عشرہ ذی الحجہ کی راتیں اور شعبان کی پندرہوں رات کو ( نماز وغیرہ سے ) زندہ رکھنا مستحب ہے۔

Chapter on supererogatory prayers. (626) And it is recommended to revive the last ten nights of Ramadan, the nights of the two Eids, the nights of the ten days of Dhul Hijjah. Translation: (626) And to revive (spend in worship) the last ten nights of Ramadan, the nights of both Eids, the nights of the ten days of Dhul Hijjah, and the fifteenth night of Sha'ban is recommended. Explanation: From here, mention is made of these four nights in which it is recommended to pray many prayers and worship. Among them, the first is the last ten nights of Ramadan. During these days, one should perform i'tikaf and worship at night as much as possible. Evidence: (1) From Aisha that the Messenger of Allah said: Seek Laylat al-Qadr in the odd nights of the last ten of Ramadan.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage introduces the ruling on reviving certain blessed nights with worship. The Arabic matn states it is recommended (nadb) to revive the last ten nights of Ramadan, the two Eid nights, and the nights of the ten days of Dhul Hijjah. The Urdu commentary adds the night of mid-Sha'ban (15th Sha'ban) as well. The explanation notes that these are four sets of nights where it is recommended to engage in abundant prayer and worship, especially the last ten of Ramadan, which include i'tikaf and seeking Laylat al-Qadr. The hadith quoted emphasizes seeking Laylat al-Qadr in the odd nights of the last ten. The Hanafi school considers reviving these nights a highly recommended act (sunnah).

Key Terms
إحياء الليالي (Ihya al-Layali): Reviving nights by staying awake in worship, especially prayer and dhikr, on specific blessed nights.

Recommended Nights for Worship in the Hanafi School
Ruling with multi-source proof for recommended nights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five categories of nights recommended for worship and identify the evidence for each from the Quran, Hadith, and Salaf.

Core Idea
Reviving specific nights is mustahab, not wajib, proven by ahadith, Quranic verse, and practice of the Salaf.

This lesson focuses on Mas'ala 626 from the Hanafi matn: 'It is recommended to revive the last ten nights of Ramadan, the two Eid nights, the nights of the ten days of Dhul Hijjah, and the night of mid-Sha'ban.' We will walk through each category and its evidence, noting the legal classification and why it remains mustahab, not obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The matn opens with 'Wa nudiba ihya'u layali...' – the verb 'nudiba' indicates recommendation (mustahab). Identify the act: reviving nights via prayer, dhikr, recitation.
The ruling level is sunnah / mustahab, not wajib.
2
List the Five Categories
From the Arabic: (1) Layali al-ashr al-akhir min Ramadan, (2) Laylata al-Eidayn, (3) Layali ashr Dhil Hijjah, (4) Laylat al-nisf min Sha'ban. The commentary adds the last ten of Ramadan count as ten nights.
Some lists combine or separate differently; the matn explicitly states four, but the last ten includes multiple nights.
3
Locate Proofs for Each Category
The commentary provides specific evidence. For Ramadan last ten: hadith 'taharrau laylata al-qadr' and 'kana al-nabi idha dakhala al-ashr...'. For Eid nights: qawl al-Sahabi (Abu Darda) and narration from Shafi'i about five nights. For Dhul Hijjah: Quran 'Wal-fajri wa layalin ashr' plus hadith 'ma al-amalu fi ayyam al-ashr afdal'. For mid-Sha'ban: hadith 'inna Allaha yanzilu laylata al-nisf min Sha'ban' and qawl al-Tabi'i.
The proofs vary in strength; all are sufficient for istihbab (recommendation).
4
Examine the Primary Dalil for Ramadan Nights
The hadith 'taharrau laylata al-qadr' contains an imperative (taharrau) which in Hanafi usul indicates recommendation when there is no qarinah for wujub. The second hadith describes the Prophet's active practice: 'ahya laylahu wa ayqadha ahlahu'. Together they establish the recommendation strongly.
Wajh al-dalalah: the imperative is for seeking (talab) and the Prophet's consistent practice reinforces istihbab.
5
Summarize the Overall Hukm
All these nights are mustahab (recommended) not wajib. The term 'nudiba' in the matn and the nature of the proofs (zanni al-thubut for hadith, and qawl of Sahaba/Tabi'in) confirm the level.
Cross-madhhab: some schools may view certain nights as more emphasized, but Hanafi holds them all as mustahab.

[۵] نماز حاجت کوئی ضرورت پڑ جائے تو دورکعت حاجت کی نماز پڑھے
صلى الله
صلى الله
وجه : اس حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن ابی اوفی قال قال رسول الله له من كانت له الى الله حاجة او الى احد من بني آدم فليتوضأ و ليحسن الوضوء ثم ليصل ركعتين ثم ليثن على الله و ليصل على النبي الله ثم ليقل ، لا اله الا الله الحليم الكريم سبحان الله رب العرش العظيم ، الحمد لله رب العالمين ، اسألک موجبات رحمتک و عزائم مغفرتک ، و الغنيمة من كل بر و السلامة من كل اثم ، لا تدع لى ذنبا إلا غفرته و لا هما الا فرجته و لا حاجة هي لك رضا الا قضيتها يا ارحم الرحمین ۔(ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء في صلاة الحاجة ، ص ۱۲۶، نمبر ۴۷۹ رابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ما جاء فی صلاۃ الحاجة ، ص ۱۹۷، نمبر ۱۳۸۴) اس حدیث میں نماز حاجت کا طریقہ بتایا گیا ہے۔ ترجمه : (۶۲۶) اور رمضان کی اخیر کی دس راتیں اور دونوں عیدین کی شب اور عشرہ ذی الحجہ کی راتیں اور شعبان کی پندرہوں رات کو ( نماز وغیرہ سے ) زندہ رکھنا مستحب ہے۔

سے [1] پہلی ہے رمضان کی اخیر کی دس راتیں۔ ان دنوں میں اعتکاف کرے اور رات کو زیادہ سے زیادہ عبادت کرے۔ وجه : (۱) عن عائشة ان رسول الله الله قال تحروا ليلة القدر في الوتر من العشر الأواخر من رمضان - ( بخاری شریف، باب تحری لیلۃ القدر فی الوتر من العشر الاواخر ص ۱۳۲۳، نمبر ۲۰۱۷) (۲) عن عائشة قالت كان النبي عل الله اذا دخل العشر شد مئزره و أحيا ليله و ايقظ أهله - ( بخاری شریف، باب العمل فى العشر الاواخر من رمضان ، ص ۳۲۴ نمبر ۲۰۲۴) ان احادیث میں ہے کہ اخیر کی دس راتوں میں عبادت زیادہ سے زیادہ کرے۔
اور دونوں عیدین کی شب۔ وجه : اس کے لئے قول صحابی یہ ہے۔ عن ابي الدرداء قال من قام ليلتي العيد لله محتسبا فلم يمت قلبه حتى تموت القلوب .... قال الشافعى و بلغنا انه كان يقال ان الدعاء يستجاب فى خمس ليال : في ليلة الجمعة ، و ليلة الاضحى ، و ليلة الفطر ، و اول ليلة من رجب ، و ليلة النصف من شعبان ۔ (سنن بیہقی ، باب عبادة ليلة العیدین، ج ثالث ص ۴۴۵، نمبر ۶۲۹۳)
اور عشرہ ذی الحجۃ کی راتیں

Chapter on supererogatory prayers. (626) It is recommended to revive the nights of the last ten [days] of Ramadan, and to revive the two nights of the two Eids, and the nights of the ten days of Dhul Hijjah, and the night of mid-Sha'ban. [Urdu commentary:] Do this or not... [extensive commentary on istikhara, salat al-hajah, and proofs for each night].
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Chapter on Supererogatory Prayers. It begins by stating the ruling (mas'ala 626): it is recommended (mustahab) to revive specific nights: the last ten nights of Ramadan, the nights of Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha, the nights of the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah, and the night of mid-Sha'ban. The commentary then elaborates, first covering two related prayers: Istikhara (seeking guidance) and Salat al-Hajah (prayer for need), providing hadith proofs and the method for each. Then it returns to the main topic, translating the Arabic matn into Urdu and providing detailed proofs for each category of nights using Quranic verses, hadith, and statements of companions and successors. For the last ten of Ramadan, it cites hadith about seeking Laylat al-Qadr and the Prophet's practice. For Eid nights and the ten days of Dhul Hijjah, it provides hadith and a Quranic verse. For mid-Sha'ban, it cites hadith on divine forgiveness. The overall ruling is that these nights should be spent in worship, but gathering in congregation is discussed separately in the next mas'ala.

Key Terms
إحياء الليالي (ihya' al-layali): Spending the night in worship, including prayer, dhikr, and recitation.
ليلة النصف من شعبان (laylat al-nisf min Sha'ban): The night of the 15th of Sha'ban, recommended for worship.
الوتر من العشر الأواخر (al-witr min al-ashr al-awakhir): The odd nights of the last ten days of Ramadan, especially emphasized for seeking Laylat al-Qadr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following nights is NOT included among the recommended nights?
A) The last ten nights of Ramadan
B) The night of the 15th of Sha'ban
C) The first night of Rajab
D) The night of Eid al-Fitr

Key Takeaway
Reviving specific nights (the last ten of Ramadan, two Eids, ten of Dhul Hijjah, and mid-Sha'ban) is mustahab, supported by ahadith and Quran, but must be done without fixed congregational innovation.

Salah — Prayer

The Prayers of Istikhara and Hajah: Method and Proof
Expansion on two recommended prayers with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the method of performing salat al-istikhara and salat al-hajah and cite the hadith proofs for each.

Core Idea
Istikhara and salat al-hajah are recommended prayers with specific du'as, proven by authentic ahadith.

The passage expands on two important supererogatory prayers: Istikhara (seeking guidance) and Salat al-Hajah (prayer for a need). These are not part of the main matn but are included in the commentary as relevant to the chapter on nawafil. We will examine the hadith evidence, the prescribed method, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Prayers
The commentary presents two separate prayers: Istikhara (prayer for guidance) and Salat al-Hajah (prayer for a specific need). Both are two rak'at prayers followed by a specific supplication.
They are not mentioned in the matn but are explained in the commentary as part of the chapter on supererogatory prayers.
2
Examine the Hadith for Istikhara
The passage quotes the hadith from Jabir: 'The Prophet used to teach us istikhara in all matters as he taught us a surah. He said: When one of you intends a matter, let him pray two rak'at of non-obligatory prayer, then say...' The full du'a is provided.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Abu Dawud; it is authentic (sahih).
3
Examine the Hadith for Salat al-Hajah
The passage quotes the hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa: 'Whoever has a need from Allah or from any human, let him perform ablution well, then pray two rak'at, then praise Allah and send blessings on the Prophet, then say...' The full du'a is provided.
This hadith is from Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah; it has some weakness but is accepted for fada'il.
4
Note the Ruling Level
Both prayers are considered sunnah/mustahab in the Hanafi school. The proofs are ahad hadith, sufficient for recommendation.
There is no dispute among the four schools regarding their general recommendation, though the exact wording of the du'a may vary.
5
Understand the Practical Method
For istikhara: after the prayer, recite the du'a. The text clarifies that the answer comes through inclination of the heart toward one option. For salat al-hajah: the prayer is followed by praise, salawat, then the du'a.
The passage explicitly states that the istikhara is completed when the heart becomes inclined toward a choice, not necessarily a dream or external sign.

Ruling on Gathering for Night Vigils in Mosques
Ruling on gathering in mosques to revive specific nights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on gathering in mosques for night vigils and identify the condition that distinguishes permissible from disliked gatherings.

Core Idea
Organised night vigils in mosques are disliked if festive, but permissible if purely devotional.

This passage provides a concise ruling on a common practice: gathering in the mosque to revive special nights (e.g., 15th Sha'ban, Laylat al-Qadr). The text clarifies that the disliked element is not the gathering itself, but the festive atmosphere sometimes associated with it. Understanding this distinction helps avoid both excessive prohibition and unwarranted innovation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is 'gathering in the mosque to revive a specific night'. The default ruling is 'makruh' (disliked). Note that makruh here is tanzihi (not sinful but better avoided).
The Arabic term 'يكره' is used.
2
Locate the condition that modifies the ruling
The commentary explains that the karaha (dislike) attaches when the gathering involves festive elements like lighting lamps and drumming. Without these, if done with sincerity and seriousness, the gathering is permissible.
The condition is based on the presence or absence of festive activities.
3
Apply the distinction to practical scenarios
Consider two cases: (a) a mosque organises a night vigil with decorative lights and social activities – disliked; (b) a mosque invites people for extra prayers and dhikr without embellishments – permissible.
The intention and atmosphere determine the ruling.

Source Text

(۲۲۷) ويُكْرَهُ الِاجْتِمَاعُ عَلَى إِحْيَاءِ لَيْلَةٍ مِنْ هَذِهِ اللَّيَالِي فِي الْمَسَاجِدِ.
ترجمه : (۶۲۷) ہاں ان راتوں میں سے کسی شب کے لئے بھی مسجد میں جمع ہونے کا اہتمام کرنا) مکروہ ہے۔ تشریح : کچھ لوگ ان راتوں میں جمع ہو کر چراغاں کرتے ہیں اور دھمال کرتے ہیں وہ مکروہ ہے، جمع ہو کر سنجیدگی سے عبادت کرے تو جائز ہے۔
(227) And it is disliked to gather for reviving any of these nights in the mosques. Translation: (627) Yes, arranging gathering in the mosque for any of these nights is makruh. Explanation: Some people gather in these nights, light lamps, and engage in drumming; that is makruh. If they gather to worship with seriousness, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This is a ruling statement (mas'ala 627) that it is makruh (disliked) to organize congregational gatherings in mosques specifically for reviving the aforementioned nights. The commentary explains that the disliked aspect is the common practice of gathering with lights and frivolous activities (dhumal/drumming). However, if people choose to gather and engage in sincere worship (prayer, dhikr) without the festive atmosphere, it is permissible (ja'iz). The ruling does not forbid individual acts of worship; it only discourages formal group events that may resemble innovations or lead to excessive celebration.

Key Terms
الاجتماع على إحياء ليلة (al-ijtima' 'ala ihya' laylah): Gathering with the intention of collectively performing night worship in the mosque.
مكروه (makruh): A legal category meaning disliked; in this context, it is tanzihi (not sinful but better to avoid).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does a gathering for night vigil in the mosque become makruh?
A) When it involves festive elements like lights and drumming
B) Whenever more than ten people gather
C) Only if the gathering is for a specific night other than Ramadan
D) It is always makruh regardless of circumstances

Key Takeaway
A gathering in the mosque for night vigils is permissible if free from festive elements; otherwise, it is makruh tanzihi.
