Ruling on Gathering in Mosques for Special Nights
Ruling on gathering in mosques for special nights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on gathering in mosques for specific nights and explain the evidence for the virtue of those nights.

Core Idea
Reviving special nights individually is recommended; gathering in mosques for that purpose is makruh.

This passage discusses the Hanafi position on the virtuous nights and the practice of communal gatherings. It distinguishes between individual worship, which is recommended, and organized mosque gatherings, which are disliked. The author cites Quranic verses, hadiths, and scholarly opinions to establish the virtue of these nights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act is 'gathering in mosques to revive specific nights'. The hukm is makruh (disliked). Individual worship on those nights is mustahab (recommended).
The text explicitly says 'ويكره الاجتماع'.
2
Locate the dalil for the virtue of the nights
The author provides evidence for each set of nights: last ten of Ramadan (hadith from Aisha), two Eids (saying of Companion Abu Darda and report from Shafi'i), ten nights of Dhul Hijjah (Quran 89:1-3 and hadith), and mid-Sha'ban (hadith of descent and saying of Tabi'i).
The hadith for mid-Sha'ban is from Tirmidhi and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah for the Quranic verse
The verse 'by the ten nights' is interpreted by Hanafi scholars as referring to the first ten nights of Dhul Hijjah, indicating their special virtue.
This is an example of tafsir bi al-ma'thur.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school may permit or encourage communal gatherings on these nights, as indicated by the mention of al-Shafi'i's list. The Hanafi ruling is that such gatherings are makruh.
The text does not provide a full dispute, but cross-madhhab difference is implied.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that gathering is makruh, but individual worship is recommended. This is based on the principle of avoiding bid'ah while encouraging personal devotion.
The later Hanafi masters (fatawa mutakhkhirin) uphold this.

فصل في النوافل
وليلة النصف من شعبان (۲۲۷) ويكره الاجتماع على احياء ليلة من هذه الليالي في المساجد. بخاری شریف، باب تحری لیلۃ القدر فی الوتر من العشر الاواخر ص ۱۳۲۳، نمبر ۲۰۱۷) (۲) عن عائشة قالت كان النبي عل الله اذا دخل العشر شد مئزره و أحيا ليله و ايقظ أهله - ( بخاری شریف، باب العمل فى العشر الاواخر من رمضان ، ص ۳۲۴ نمبر ۲۰۲۴) ان احادیث میں ہے کہ اخیر کی دس راتوں میں عبادت زیادہ سے زیادہ کرے۔
اور دونوں عیدین کی شب۔ وجه : اس کے لئے قول صحابی یہ ہے۔ عن ابي الدرداء قال من قام ليلتي العيد لله محتسبا فلم يمت قلبه حتى تموت القلوب .... قال الشافعى و بلغنا انه كان يقال ان الدعاء يستجاب فى خمس ليال : في ليلة الجمعة ، و ليلة الاضحى ، و ليلة الفطر ، و اول ليلة من رجب ، و ليلة النصف من شعبان ۔ (سنن بیہقی ، باب عبادة ليلة العیدین، ج ثالث ص ۴۴۵، نمبر ۶۲۹۳)
اور عشرہ ذی الحجۃ کی راتیں
وجه : (۱) اس کے لئے آیت یہ ہے والفجرہ ولیال عشره والشفع والوتر ۔ ( آیت ۲ ، سورۃ الفجر ۸۹) اس آیت میں دس راتوں سے ذی الحجہ کی دس راتیں مراد ہیں۔ (۲) اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابن عباس عن النبى الله انه قال ما العمل في أيام العشر افضل منها في هذه قالوا و لا الجهاد ؟ قال ولا الجهاد الا رجل خرج يخاطر بنفسه و ماله فلم يرجع بشيء ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب فضل العمل في ايام التشريق، ص ۱۵۶ نمبر ۹۹۹ ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی صیام العشر ، ص ۱۹۱، نمبر ۷۵۸ )
اور شعبان کی پندرھوں رات کو نماز وغیرہ سے ) زندہ رکھنا مستحب ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت فقدت رسول الله الله ليلة .... فقال ان الله عزو جل ينزل ليلة النصف من شعبان الى السماء الدنيا فيغفر لأكثر من عدد شعر غنم كلب ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء في ليلة النصف من شعبان ص ۱۸۷ نمبر ۷۳۹ ) (۲) قول تابعی یہ ہے ۔ عن كثير بن مرة ان الله يطلع ليلة النصف من شعبان الى العباد فيغفر لاهل الارض ، الا رجل مشرک او مشاحن ) مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب النصف من شعبان، ج رابع ، ص ۲۴۵، نمبر ۷۹۵۳)
ترجمه : (۶۲۷) ہاں ان راتوں میں سے کسی شب کے لئے بھی مسجد میں جمع ہونے کا اہتمام کرنا) مکروہ ہے۔ تشریح : کچھ لوگ ان راتوں میں جمع ہو کر چراغاں کرتے ہیں اور دھمال کرتے ہیں وہ مکروہ ہے، جمع ہو کر سنجیدگی سے عبادت کرے تو جائز ہے۔
Section on voluntary prayers. And the night of the middle of Sha'ban (227). And gathering in mosques to revive any of these nights is disliked. Bukhari, Chapter of searching for Laylat al-Qadr in the odd of the last ten, p. 1323, no. 2017. (2) From Aisha, she said: When the Prophet entered the last ten, he tightened his waist-wrapper, stayed awake at night, and awakened his family. (Bukhari, Chapter of deeds in the last ten of Ramadan, p. 324, no. 2024) These hadiths indicate that one should increase worship in the last ten nights. And the nights of both Eids. Evidence: For this there is the saying of a Companion: From Abu Darda: Whoever stands the two nights of Eid for Allah seeking reward, his heart will not die until hearts die. Al-Shafi'i said: It has reached us that supplication is answered on five nights: Friday night, night of Adha, night of Fitr, first night of Rajab, and the night of mid-Sha'ban. (Sunan Bayhaqi, Chapter of worship on the nights of the two Eids, vol. 3, p. 445, no. 6293) And the nights of the ten days of Dhul Hijjah. Evidence: (1) For this there is the verse: 'By the dawn, and by the ten nights, and by the even and the odd.' (Surah al-Fajr 89:1-3) In this verse, the ten nights refer to the ten nights of Dhul Hijjah. (2) For this there is the hadith: From Ibn Abbas from the Prophet: He said: 'There are no days in which deeds are better than in these ten.' They said: 'Not even jihad?' He said: 'Not even jihad, except a man who goes out risking his life and wealth and does not return with anything.' (Bukhari, Chapter of virtue of deeds during the days of Tashreeq, p. 156, no. 999; Tirmidhi, Chapter of fasting the ten days, p. 191, no. 758) And reviving the 15th night of Sha'ban through prayer etc. is recommended. Evidence: (1) For this there is the hadith: From Aisha: I missed the Messenger of Allah one night... He said: 'Verily Allah, Mighty and Sublime, descends on the night of mid-Sha'ban to the lowest heaven and forgives more than the number of hairs of the sheep of Kalb.' (Tirmidhi, Chapter of the night of mid-Sha'ban, p. 187, no. 739) (2) The saying of a Tabi'i: From Kathir ibn Murrah: Allah looks upon His servants on the night of mid-Sha'ban and forgives the people of the earth, except a polytheist or one who harbors rancor. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter of the night of mid-Sha'ban, vol. 4, p. 245, no. 7953) Translation: (627) Yes, for any of these nights, organizing a gathering in the mosque is disliked. Explanation: Some people gather on these nights with lights and celebrations; that is disliked. If they gather in seriousness for worship, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the recommended nights and the disliked nature of gathering in mosques to revive them. The author begins by listing several virtuous nights mentioned in the Hanafi tradition: the last ten nights of Ramadan (especially Laylat al-Qadr), the two nights of Eid, the first ten nights of Dhul Hijjah, and the night of mid-Sha'ban. For each, he provides textual evidence from the Quran, Sunnah, sayings of Companions, and later scholars. Despite the recommendation to worship individually on these nights, the author explicitly states that organizing communal gatherings in the mosque specifically for these nights is makruh (disliked). In the Urdu explanation, he clarifies that what is disliked is the practice of gathering with lights and celebration; if people gather for serious worship without such displays, it is permissible. The mention of al-Shafi'i's list of five nights serves as a supporting proof for the virtue of these nights, not as a disagreement on the ruling of gathering.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): An action that is disliked and discouraged but not sinful. In Hanafi fiqh, makruh tanzihi is less severe than makruh tahrimi.
احیاء اللیل (ihya' al-layl): Spending the night in worship, such as prayer, remembrance of Allah, and recitation of Quran.
مستحب (mustahab): An action that is recommended but not obligatory. Performing it brings reward, and omitting it is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, what is the ruling on gathering in mosques to revive specific nights such as mid-Sha'ban?
A) Mustahab (recommended)
B) Makruh (disliked)
C) Haram (prohibited)
D) Wajib (obligatory)

Key Takeaway
Individual worship on virtuous nights is recommended, but communal gatherings in mosques specifically for those nights are disliked (makruh tanzihi).
